Taharah — Purification
beginner
10 min
Definition of Purification and the Seven Purifying Waters
Opening of Kitab al-Taharah with definitions and first ruling on water types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi legal definition of taharah and list the seven types of water that are valid for purification.

Core Idea
Seven waters are valid for purification; rainwater is the origin, but all share the same ruling.

We begin the study of purification (taharah), a prerequisite for prayer. The text first establishes what 'book' and 'taharah' mean from a legal perspective, then identifies the essential medium of purification: water. The opening passage defines the types of water that are permissible to use, grounding the ruling in Quranic evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definitions
Locate the definitions of 'kitab' and 'taharah' in the text. Note that 'kitab' is a group of independent fiqh issues, and 'taharah' is a legal effect removing hadath or khabath from body, garment, or place.
The definition of taharah is crucial as it sets the scope for the entire book.
2
Understand the ruling on waters
The text states that purification is permissible (ja'iz) with seven waters. Identify the seven and note that they are listed with rainwater first.
The plural 'waters' indicates the unity of ruling across these types.
3
Analyze the linguistic and legal definition of water
Water is defined as a delicate flowing substance. The text explains its linguistic properties and why the plural is used. Understand that the legal definition includes only substances that are true water.
This definition excludes things like dew, as discussed later.
4
Examine the Quranic proof for rainwater
The author cites two Quranic verses to show that rainwater is the original type of purifying water. Recognize that this does not exclude other waters but establishes the primary status.
The verses are from Az-Zumar and Al-Anfal.
5
Note the omission of dew water
The text mentions that dew (al-tall) is not included because some consider it the breath of an animal and not true water. Understand that the correct view is left incomplete, but the omission is deliberate.
This illustrates how the legal definition of water affects which sources are valid.

كتاب الطهارة
المياه التي يجوز التطهير بها سبعةُ مياه: ماءُ السَّماءِ .
كتاب الطهارة
(۲)
الكتاب والكتابة لغة: الجمع، كجمع الحروف، واصطلاحاً طائفة من المسائل الفقهية اعتبرت مستقلة، شملت أنواعاً ) وفصولاً، أو لم تشمل ) . والطهارة - بفتح الطاء - مصدر طهر الشيء يطهر النظافة مطلقاً وبكسرها - الآلة وبضمها - فضل ما يتطهر به.
بمعنى
وشرعاً: أثر يظهر بالمحل حكماً بزوال الحدث، أو الخبث عما تعلق به الصلاة، ليشمل الثوب والمكان. والإضافة فيه، بمعنى اللام، ويبعد كونها بمعنى من؛ لأن ضابطه صحة تقديرها، مــع صحة الإخبار عن الأول بالثاني، كخاتم فضة، وهو مفقود هنا، إذ لا يصح أن يقال: الكتاب طهارة. وقدمت الطهارة على الصلاة)، وإن كانت الصلاة أهم، لكون الطهارة شرطاً لها، وهـو مـقـدم، ولمـا كان الماء مزيلاً للحدث والخبث، قدم الكلام عليه فقال : ( المياه) جمع كثرة، وجمع القلة أمواه. والماء: هو الجوهر اللطيف السيال، الذي يتلون بلون الإناء. والعذب منــه بـه حـيـاة كــل نـام. وهو ممدود، وقد يقصر ، وأصله موه، تحركت واوه، وانفتح ما قبلها، فقلبت ألفاً. إلا أن الهاء أبدلت إبدالاً شاذاً في اللغة المشهورة، وعبر بصيغة الجمع لاتحاد حكم المياه، (التي يجوز) -أي: يصح- (التطهير بها ) وهي (سبعةُ مياه). وبدأ بذكر (ماء السَّماءِ)، لأنه الأصل، لقوله تعالى: ﴿أَلَمْ تَرَ أَنَّ اللَّهَ أنزَلَ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مَاءً فَسَلَكَهُ يَبِيعَ فِي الْأَرْضِ ﴾ [ال : ۲۱ ]، ولهذا كان غير ماء السماء قسيماً لــه، باعتبـار توطنه، ومثل ذلك لا ينكر، والأشياء المختلفة الحقائق تصير واحداً باعتبار الأمــر الـعـام، وسيأتي تتمته في تقسيم الصوم إن شاء الله تعالى، وكان طهوراً لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَيُنَزِلُ عَلَيْكُم مِّنَ السَّمَاءِ مَاءً ليطهركم به ﴾ [الأنفال: ۱۱] والمراد بماء السماء ماء المطر، والسماء كل ما عـــلاك فأظلك، ومنه قيـل لسقف البيت سماء، ولم يذكر ماء الطل، وهو الندى، لما قيل إنه نَفَس دابة، وليس بماء، والصحيح
And God I ask that He benefit with it His servants, and perpetuate with it the benefit. (And God) the Generous (I ask), and by His chosen beloved I beseech, that He benefit with it His servants) perpetually, (and perpetuate with it the benefit) by the aid of the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him. Note: The Shaykh Imam Shihab al-Din al-Naqshbandi, may God have mercy on him, said: For the scholars, at the beginning of authorship there are seven methods, three of which are obligatory to use: the basmalah, then the hamdalah, then the prayer upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, and the reason has preceded. And four are permissible to use: mentioning the motivation for authorship, naming the book, praising the subject of the authorship, and mentioning how the author proceeded in summary. And this is the time to begin the intended purpose with the help of the Worshipped King. -- The Book of Purification. The waters by which purification is permissible are seven waters: rainwater. The Book of Purification (2) The book and writing linguistically means: gathering, like gathering letters, and terminologically: a group of fiqh issues considered independent, whether they include types and chapters or not. And taharah - with fatha on the ta - is the infinitive of tahara al-shay'u yatuhuru meaning cleanliness absolutely; with kasra - the tool; with damma - the surplus of what one uses for purification. And legally: an effect that appears on the place ruling-wise by the removal of hadath or khabath from that which prayer is connected to, to include garment and place. The idafa here is in the sense of lam, and it is unlikely to be in the sense of min because its criterion is the validity of its estimation with the validity of predicating the first by the second, like a silver ring, and this is lacking here because it is not correct to say: the book is purification. And taharah was placed before salah, even though salah is more important, because taharah is a condition for it, and the condition is given precedence. And since water is the remover of hadath and khabath, he gave precedence to speaking about it, so he said: (the waters) - plural of abundance, and plural of fewness is amwah. And water: the delicate flowing substance that takes the color of its container. The sweet (fresh) of it gives life to every growing thing. It is long (mamdud) and sometimes shortened, and its origin is mawh, its waw moved and what preceded it opened, so it became alif. Except that the ha was replaced irregularly in the well-known language. And he used the plural form due to the unity of ruling of waters, (by which it is permissible) i.e., valid (purification) and they are (seven waters). And he began with mentioning (rainwater) because it is the origin, according to the saying of the Most High: {Do you not see that God sends down rain from the sky and makes it flow as springs in the earth} [Az-Zumar: 21], and for this reason other than rainwater is considered a counterpart to it in terms of its settling, and such a thing is not denied, and things of different realities become one by virtue of a general matter, and its completion will come in the division of fasting if God wills. And it was purifying according to the saying of the Most High: {And He sends down upon you from the sky water to purify you with it} [Al-Anfal: 11]. And what is meant by rainwater is the water of rain, and the sky is everything that is above you and covers you, and hence the ceiling of a house is called sky. And he did not mention dew water, which is moisture, because it is said that it is the breath of an animal, and it is not water, and the correct view is...
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage marks the opening of the Book of Purification (Kitab al-Taharah) in the commentary on Nur al-Idah. It begins with the author's concluding supplication and a note on the proper method of beginning a book, citing seven methods: three obligatory (basmalah, hamdalah, salawat) and four permissible (motivation, titling, praising the field, summary of approach). Then the actual fiqh text begins with definitions: 'kitab' linguistically means collection, and technically a group of independent fiqh issues; 'taharah' linguistically means cleanliness, and technically means a legal effect removing hadath (ritual impurity) or khabath (filth) from what is connected to prayer (body, garment, place). The commentary explains why taharah precedes salah in the text: it is a condition for salah, and conditions are placed before their objects. Since water is the primary purifier, the author discusses it first, defining water as a delicate flowing substance and mentioning its linguistic properties. The ruling states: the waters by which purification is permissible are seven waters. The text begins with rainwater (mā' al-samā') because it is the original type, citing Quranic verses (Az-Zumar: 21 and Al-Anfal: 11) to show its origin and purifying quality. The commentary notes that 'sky' refers to anything above covering one, and explains why dew water (al-ṭall) is not mentioned: some say it is an animal's breath and not water, though the correct view is left incomplete. This passage establishes the foundational ruling for permissible waters in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
كتاب (kitāb): A group of fiqh issues considered independent, whether including types and chapters or not.
طهارة (ṭahārah): A legal effect that appears on the place ruling-wise by the removal of hadath (ritual impurity) or khabath (filth) from that which prayer is connected to (body, garment, place).
ماء (mā’): The delicate flowing substance that takes the color of its container; sweet (fresh) water gives life to growing things.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many waters does the text state are permissible for purification (taharah)?
A) Five
B) Seven
C) Four
D) Three

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits purification with seven specific types of water, with rainwater as the original model.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
The Seven Purifying Waters: Ruling and Proofs
Defines taharah, lists seven waters with proofs, begins five-category classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven types of water that are pure and purifying in the Hanafi school and identify the dalil (proof) for each type.

Core Idea
Seven waters are pure and purifying: rain, sea, river, well, snow, hail, spring — each proven by Quran or authentic Sunnah.

This passage opens the Book of Purification in Nur al-Idah's commentary. It defines the key term 'taharah' and establishes the foundational ruling that seven specific waters are valid for purification. The author provides textual evidence for each water, emphasising that these are the primary purifying agents in Islamic law. Understanding this list and its proofs is essential before moving into the classification of waters into categories.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is purification with water. The ruling is that these seven waters are pure and purifying (tahir mutahhir). Identify what the passage is establishing: a list of valid waters.
The passage states 'al-miyah allati yajuz al-tatahhur biha sab'atu miyah' — the waters with which purification is permissible are seven.
2
List the seven waters
From the passage, list each water: rainwater, seawater, river water, well water, melted snow, melted hail, and spring water. Note the order and any special terms.
Rainwater is given precedence because it is the origin (asl). Dew is not included; the passage notes a differing opinion but the correct view is that dew is also purifying.
3
Locate the proof for each water
For rainwater: Quran 39:21 and 8:11. For seawater: Hadith of Abu Hurairah (sunan) with the Prophet's statement 'huwa al-tahur ma'uhu'. For river water: Hadith that four rivers (Sayhun, Jayhun, Euphrates, Nile) are from Paradise. For the remaining waters (well, snow, hail, spring), no explicit proof is given in this passage; they are included by general principles or analogy.
The passage mentions that the idafah (construct phrase) in 'ma' al-sama'' etc. is for definition, not restriction, meaning these are specific types but the ruling is common.
4
Note the classification beginning
After listing the seven waters, the author announces that waters are of five categories. The first category is 'pure and purifying, not disliked' which is the absolute water (al-ma' al-mutlaq) — water that has not been mixed with anything. This sets the stage for further classification.
Absolute water is the default purifying water. Mixed water will be discussed later.

وماء البحر، وماء النهر، وماء البثرِ، وَمَا ذَابَ مِنَ الثّلج والبَرَدِ، وَمَاهُ العَيْنِ، ثُمَّ المَاهُ عَلَى خَمْسَةِ أَقْسَامٍ: طاهر مطهر غيرُ مكروه، وهو : الماءُ المُطْلَقُ..
(1)
أنه ماء مطهر ، (و) مثله (ماء البحر ) الملح، لما روى مالك وأصحاب السنن الأربعة، عن أبي هريرة الله: أن رجلاً سأل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال: يا رسول الله، إنَّا نركب البحر ونحمل معنا القليلَ مِنَ المَاءِ، فإن توضأنا بِهِ عَطِشنا، أفنتوضأ من البحر؟ فقال: هو الطهور ماؤه الحل ميتته ). قال الترمذي: سألت محمـد بـن إسماعيل (۳) عن هذا الحديث، فقال : حديث صحيح. (1) أخرجه أبو داود في الطهارة، باب: الوضوء بماء البحر برقم (۸۳) ، والترمذي في الطهارة، باب ما جاء في ماء البحر أنه طهور برقم (٦٩). (۲) هو الإمام البخاري صاحب الصحيح. (۳) لقوله : « سَيْحَانُ وَجَيْحَانُ وَالْفُرَاتُ وَالنِّيلُ كُلُّ مِنْ أَنْهَارِ الْجَنَّةِ»، أخرجه مسلم في الجنة ونعيمها، باب: ما في الدنيا من أنهار الجنة (۲۸۳۹).
تنبیه هام الأولى أن يقول: سيحان وجيحان لما ورد في معجم البلدان أن سيحان وجيحان، غير سيحون وجيحون. انظر معجم البلدان (١٠٢/٥). سيحان: نهر كبير بالثغر من نواحي المصيصة، وهو نهر أذَنَّةً بين أنطاكية والروم يمر بأذنة ثم ينفصل عنها نحو ستة أميال فيصب في بحر الروم. معجم البلدان / سيحان /.
جیحان نهر بالمصيصة بالثغر الشامي، ومخرجه من بلاد الروم، ويمر حتى يصب بمدينة تعرف بكفـر بـيـا بإزاء المصيصة وعليه عند المصيصة قنطرة من حجارة رومية عجيبة قديمة عريضة فيدخل منها إلى المصيصة
وينفذ منها فيمتد أربعة أميال ثم يصب في بحر الشام. معجم البلدان / جيحان / وكلاهما في بلاد الأرمن. الفرات: نهر عظيم يخرج من أرمينية ثم من قاليقلا ثم يجيء إلى كمخ ويخرج إلى ملطية ثم إلى سميساط إلى قلعة نجم مقابل منبج إلى دوسر إلى الرقة ثم ينصب في دجلة فيصبح نهراً واحداً. وعن عبد الملك بـن عمير قال: لولا ما يخالطه من الأذى ما تداوى به مريض إلا أبرأه الله تعالى. معجم ا البلدان / فرات /

(٤) انظر ص (٣١).
(٥) ص (٣٥).
(٦) ص (٣٨).
- ۳۲ -
Book of Purification. The waters with which purification is permissible are seven waters: rainwater. Book of Purification. (2) Al-Kitab linguistically means collection, like collecting letters; technically, it is a group of fiqh issues considered independent, whether they include chapters and sections or not. At-Taharah (with fatha on Ta) is the masdar of tahara yat-hur, meaning cleanliness absolutely; with kasra it means the instrument; with damma it means the leftover of what one uses to purify. Legally: it is an effect that appears on the place, as a ruling, by removal of hadath or khabath from what is connected to prayer, to include clothing and place. The idafah here is in the sense of lam, and it is unlikely to be 'from' because its standard is the validity of its estimation along with the validity of describing the first by the second, like a silver ring, and this is lacking here, since it is not correct to say: the book is purification. And purification is mentioned before prayer, even though prayer is more important, because purification is a condition for it, and the condition is given precedence. And since water removes hadath and khabath, speech about it is given precedence, so he said: 'waters' is a plural of multitude, and the plural of few is amwah. Water is the subtle fluid substance that takes the color of its container. Fresh water gives life to every living thing. It is long and may be shortened; its origin is m-w-h, its waw moved and what preceded it opened, so it turned into an alif, except that the ha' was replaced in an irregular way in the common language. He used the plural form because the ruling of waters is one. 'Which are permissible' i.e. valid, 'to purify with' and they are 'seven waters'. He began with 'rainwater' because it is the origin, due to the saying of the Almighty: 'Do you not see that Allah sends down rain from the sky and then causes it to penetrate the earth?' [Az-Zumar: 21], thus non-rainwater is its counterpart in terms of location, and that is not deniable, and things of different realities become one by virtue of a common aspect. Its completion will come in the division of fasting if Allah wills. And it was pure and purifying due to His saying: 'And He sends down upon you from the sky water to purify you with it' [Al-Anfal: 11]. What is meant by rainwater is rain, and the sky is everything above you that shades you, from which the roof of a house is called sky. He did not mention dew because it is said it is the breath of an animal, and it is not water, but the correct view is that it is purifying water. And similarly, seawater (salty), because of what Malik and the four Sunan compilers narrated from Abu Hurairah that a man asked the Messenger of Allah, saying: O Messenger of Allah, we travel on the sea and carry little water with us; if we perform wudu with it, we become thirsty, so may we perform wudu with seawater? He said: 'Its water is purifying and its dead animals are permissible.' At-Tirmidhi said: I asked Muhammad ibn Isma'il about this hadith, and he said: It is authentic. And likewise river water, like Sayhun, Jayhun, the Euphrates, and the Nile of Egypt, because they are from Paradise, and it is absolute water. And well water is purifying, and likewise what melts from snow and hail (with Fatha on Ba' and Ra'), and he distinguishes it from what melts from salt, because it is the opposite of water: it melts in winter and freezes in summer. Before it becomes salt, it is purifying. And likewise spring water, which is water flowing on the surface of the earth from a spring, due to the textual evidence mentioned earlier. The idafah in the mentioned waters is for definition, not for restriction, and the difference between the two idafahs is the validity of calling the first water without the second, as will be mentioned. Then he mentioned the total types of waters, saying: They are of five categories, each having its own description. The first: pure and purifying, not disliked, and it is the absolute water, which was mentioned earlier, and nothing has mixed with it. If something mixes with it or an animal drinks from it, we will mention its ruling.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is the opening of Kitab al-Taharah (Book of Purification) from the commentary Sharh Nur al-Idah. The author begins by defining key terms. 'Kitab' is defined linguistically as a collection, and technically as an independent set of fiqh issues. 'Taharah' is defined linguistically as cleanliness, and legally as the effect of removing ritual impurity (hadath) or physical impurity (khabath) from the body, clothing, or place of prayer. The author explains why purification is mentioned before prayer: purification is a condition (shart) for prayer, and conditions are logically prior. Then water is introduced as the primary purifying agent. The author states that there are seven types of water that are permissible for purification: rainwater, seawater, river water, well water, melted snow, melted hail, and spring water. Each is supported by evidence: rainwater by Quranic verses (Az-Zumar 21 and Al-Anfal 11), seawater by the famous hadith narrated by Abu Hurairah (may Allah be pleased with him) where the Prophet ﷺ declared seawater purifying. River water is supported by the hadith that four rivers (Sayhun, Jayhun, Euphrates, Nile) are from Paradise, and this water is absolute water (mutlaq). Well water, melted snow/hail, and spring water are also included without specific proof in this passage, but the author notes that the addition in these terms is for definition, not restriction. Finally, the author begins to classify waters into five categories, starting with the first: pure and purifying, not disliked, which is absolute water (mutlaq) that has not been mixed with anything. This passage establishes the foundational ruling that these seven waters are valid for purification. All Hanafi scholars agree on this, based on the Zahir al-Riwayah. The commentary provides the legal reasoning and evidence for each type of water, showing how each is derived from primary sources. The classification into five categories will be further elaborated later.

Key Terms
الطهارة (at-taharah): Linguistically: cleanliness. Legally: an effect that appears on the place by removal of hadath or khabath from what relates to prayer.
الماء المطلق (al-ma' al-mutlaq): Absolute, pure water that has not been mixed with any impurity or substance that alters its original properties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the legal definition of taharah according to this passage?
A) Pure water
B) An effect that appears on the place by removal of hadath or khabath
C) The act of washing with water
D) Physical cleanliness

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school affirms seven specific waters as pure and purifying, each supported by clear textual evidence from the Quran and Sunnah.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Absolute Water and Its Proofs
Enumeration of pure purifying waters with a prophetic proof for seawater

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the types of absolute water and explain the hadith proof for seawater's purifying quality.

Core Idea
Absolute water (ma' mutlaq) is pure and purifying; the Prophet declared seawater purifying by hadith.

The text begins by listing the natural sources of water that are purifying for wudu: sea, river, well, melted snow/hail, and spring. A key proof is the well-known hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said of seawater, 'Its water is purifying and its dead animals are lawful.' This lesson examines these sources and the underlying evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the water types
List the five natural water sources mentioned: sea, river, well, snow/hail melt, and spring.
2
Examine the proof for seawater
Read the hadith from Abu Hurairah and note the phrase 'al-tahur'—the Arabic form indicates inherent purity.
The hadith is authenticated by al-Bukhari via Tirmidhi.
3
Extend the ruling to other waters
Understand why river, well, snow, and spring water are considered absolute water: they are either from Paradise (Nile, Euphrates) or unaltered natural water.
Snow/hail melt is purifying before it crystallizes into salt.
4
Differentiate idafa
Note that phrases like 'water of the sea' are for identification, not restriction—any absolute water is purifying.

(وماء البئر ) مطهر، (و) كذا (مَا ذَابَ من الثلج والبَرَدِ) بفتح الباء الموحدة والراء المهملة واحترز به عن ما يذوب من الملح؛ لأنه عكس الماء يذوب في الشتاء ويجمد في الصيف، وأما قبل انعقاده ملحاً، فهو طهور، (و) كذا (ماء العين)، وهو ما كان جارياً على وجــه الأرض من ينبوع، لما تقدم من النص . والإضافة في المياه المذكورات للتعريف لا للتقييد، والفرق بين الإضافتين صحة إطلاق الماء على الأول دون الثاني، كما سنذكره، (تم) ذكر جملة أنواع ( المياه)، فقال: هي ( عَلَى خَمْسَةِ أقسام)، لكل منها وصف يختص به. الأول: (طاهر مطهر غير مكروه، وهـو المـاء المُطلَقُ)، الذي سبق ذكره، ولم يخالطه شيء، فإن خالطه أو شرب منه حيوان، فسنذكر حكمه. وطاهرٌ مُطَهِّرٌ مَكْرُوهُ، وَهُوَ مَا شَرِبَ مِنْهُ الهِرَّةُ وَنَحْوُهَا ، وَكَانَ قَلِيلاً. وَطَاهِرٌ غَيْرُ مُطَهِّرٍ، وَهُوَ: مَا اسْتُعْمِلَ لِرَفْعِ حَدَثٍ، أَوْ لِقُرْبَةِ، كَالْوُضُوْءِ عَلَى الوُضُوْءِ بِنِيَّتِهِ، وَيَصِيرُ المَاءُ مُسْتَعْمَلَا بِمُجَرَّدِ الْفِصَالِهِ عَنِ الْجَسَدِ. وَلَا يَجُوزُ بِمَاءِ شَجَرِ وَثَمَرِ، وَلَوْ خَرَجَ بِنَفْسِهِ مَنْ غَيْرِ عَصْرِ، فِي الأَظْهَرِ، (و) الثاني: (طاهر مُطهر مكروه كراهة تنزيه على الأصح، كما ذهب إلـيـه « الـكـرخـي رحمه الله، (وهو ما شرب منه الهرةُ الأهلية، إذ الوحشية سؤرها نجس، (ونحوها) الدجاجة المخلاة، وسباع الطير، لأنها لا تتحامى عن النجاسة، وأكل الجيف وإصغاء النبي الله الإناء للهرة)، محمل فعله المقتضي عدم الكراهة، على زوال ذلك التوهم بأن كانت بمرأى منه، في زمان يمكن غسل فمها بلعابها، كما قرره بعض المحققين، وقيد الكراهة بقوله: (وَكَانَ) ما شربت منه الهرة (قليلا) وسيأتي تقديره". (و) الثالث: (طاهر غير مطهر)، يعني غير مزيل للحدث بخلاف الخبث، (وهـو مـا اسـتعمل) في الجسد، أو لاقاه بغير قصد (لرفع حَدَثٍ)، (أو) قصد استعماله (لِقُرْبَةٍ) وهي (كَالْوُضُوءِ) في مجلس آخر، عَلَى الوُضُوءِ بِنِيَّتِهِ)، أي: الوضوء تقرباً ليصير عبادة، فإن كان في مجلس واحــد كره، ويكون الماء غير مستعمل ، ومثله غسل يده للطعام، أو منه، إن قصد به القربة، لأنـه سـنة، لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : « الوضوء قَبْلَ الطَّعَامِ بَرَكَةٌ، وَبَعْدَهُ يَنْفِي اللمم -أي: الجنون- وقبلَهُ يَنْفِي الفقر ». فلو غسلها للوسخ، وهو متوضئ، ولم يقصد القربة، لا . يصير مستعملاً، كغسل ثوب ودابة مأكولة، (ويصيرُ الماءُ مُستعملاً بمجرَّدِ انفصاله عن الجسدِ)، وإن لم يستقر في محل، علـى الصحيح. لأن سقوط حكم الاستعمال قبل الانفصال لضرورة التطهير، ولا ضرورة بعد انفصاله، (وَلا يَجُوزُ) أي: لا يصح (بماء شجر وثمر)، لكمال امتزاجه، فلم يكن مطلقاً ، وَلَو خَرَجَ بِنَفْسِهِ مِنْ غَير عَصْرِ)، كالقاطر من الكرم ) ونحوه ( في الأظْهَر ) احترز به عما قيل بأنه يجوز بماء يقطر بنفسه، لأنـه ليـس
And water of the sea, and water of the river, and water of the well, and what melts from snow and hail, and water of the spring. Then water is of five categories: pure and purifying not disliked, and it is absolute water... (1) That it is purifying water, and likewise sea water (salty), due to what Malik and the authors of the four Sunan narrated from Abu Hurairah that a man asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'O Messenger of Allah, we travel by sea and carry with us a little water; if we perform ablution with it we become thirsty, so may we perform ablution with seawater?' He said: 'Its water is purifying, and its dead animals are lawful.' At-Tirmidhi said: I asked Muhammad ibn Ismail about this hadith, and he said: It is a sound hadith. (And) likewise river water, like Sayhun and Jayhun and the Euphrates and the Nile of Egypt, because they are from Paradise, and it is absolute water. (And) well water is purifying. (And) likewise what melts from snow and hail—with fatha on the ba and the ra—and it is a precaution against what melts from salt, because it is the opposite of water; it melts in winter and freezes in summer. But before it solidifies as salt, it is purifying. (And) likewise spring water, which is water flowing on the surface of the earth from a source, due to the textual evidence that preceded. The idafah (construct phrase) in the mentioned waters is for definition, not restriction, and the difference between the two idafahs is the validity of applying the name 'water' to the first but not the second, as we will mention. Then he mentioned the categories of waters, saying: They are of five categories, each having a specific description. The first: pure and purifying not disliked, and it is absolute water, which was mentioned earlier, and nothing has mixed with it. If something mixes with it or an animal drinks from it, we will mention its ruling later. And pure and purifying disliked, and it is that from which a cat and the like have drunk, and it was a small amount. And pure but not purifying, and it is what is used for removing ritual impurity or for an act of worship, like performing ablution upon ablution with the intention of worship, and the water becomes used merely by its separation from the body. And it is not permissible to perform ablution with water from trees and fruits, even if it comes out by itself without pressing, in the most apparent view. (And) the second: pure and purifying disliked with a dislike of tanzih according to the most correct view, as held by Al-Karkhi (may Allah have mercy on him), and it is that from which the domestic cat has drunk, as for a wild cat its leftover water is impure, and similar to it is the free-range chicken and birds of prey because they do not avoid impurity and eat carrion, and the Prophet's inclining the vessel for the cat—interpretation of his action indicating no dislike is based on the removal of that assumption, that it was in his sight at a time when it was possible to wash its mouth with its saliva, as some verifiers have established, and the dislike is restricted by his statement: (and it was) what the cat drank from (a small amount) and its estimation will come. (And) the third: pure but not purifying, meaning not removing ritual impurity as opposed to filth, and it is what is used on the body or contacted without intent to remove ritual impurity, or intended use for an act of worship, like ablution in another place upon ablution with its intention, i.e., performing ablution as a means of drawing closer to become worship. If it is in one place, it is disliked, and the water is not used. Similar to it is washing one's hand for food or from it if one intends worship, because it is sunnah, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Ablution before food is a blessing, and after it removes insanity, and before it removes poverty.' If he washes it for dirt while in a state of purity and does not intend worship, it does not become used, like washing a garment or an animal that is eaten. (And) the water becomes used merely by its separation from the body, even if it does not settle in a place, according to the correct view, because the ruling of being used falls before separation due to the necessity of purification, and there is no necessity after its separation. (And) it is not permissible, i.e., not valid, with water from trees and fruits, due to its complete mixture, so it is not absolute, even if it comes out by itself without pressing, like that dripping from the grapevine and the like, in the most apparent view, as a precaution against what is said that it is permissible with water that drips by itself, because it is not...
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage from the sharh explains the categories of water for ritual purification. The author first lists the types of water that are pure and purifying: sea, river, well, snow/hail melt, and spring water. The proof for sea water is the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) declared seawater purifying and its dead animals lawful, narrated by Malik and the four Sunan, and authenticated by Imam al-Bukhari. River water is included because rivers like Sayhun, Jayhun, Euphrates, and Nile are said to be from Paradise, hence they are absolute water. Well water is also purifying, and snow/hail melt is purifying as long as it hasn't turned into salt. Spring water is purifying based on earlier textual evidence. The idafa (construct phrase) in naming types of water is for definition, not restriction, so 'water of the sea' means the kind of water that is from the sea, not that only that specific water is purifying.

The text then moves to the five categories of water. The first category is pure and purifying and not disliked, which is absolute water that has not been mixed with anything. The second category is pure and purifying but disliked (makruh tanzihan), specifically water from which a domestic cat has drunk, provided the water is a small amount. The author explains that the leftover (su'r) of a domestic cat is pure but disliked because cats may have impurity on their mouths, though the Prophet's action of inclining a vessel for a cat suggests permissibility, understood as a case where the cat's mouth was clean. The dislike is restricted to a small amount, and its quantity will be defined later. The third category is pure but not purifying, which includes used water (musta'mal) for removing ritual impurity or for an act of worship, like performing ablution on top of ablution with the intention of worship. Water becomes used merely by separating from the body, and it cannot be used again for ritual purification. Also included are waters from trees and fruits, such as grape juice, even if it comes out without pressing, because it is not absolute water due to complete mixture.

The commentary emphasizes that used water remains pure in essence but loses its purifying quality for ritual purity. The ruling on tree water is that it is not valid for ablution in the most apparent view, contrary to some who deem it permissible if it flows by itself. The text also notes that washing hands for food or from food with the intention of worship does not make the water used, but if done for cleaning without intention, it remains usable.

Key Terms
ماء مطلق (ma' mutlaq): Absolute water: natural water that has not been mixed with any substance that alters its name or properties.
طاهر (tahir): Pure: ritually clean in itself, not considered najis.
مطهر (mutahhir): Purifying: able to remove ritual impurity (hadath) and physical impurity (najasah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What proof is given for seawater being purifying?
A) A verse from the Quran
B) A hadith where the Prophet says seawater is purifying
C) Consensus of the companions
D) Analogical reasoning from river water

Key Takeaway
Absolute water, including seawater, is pure and purifying for wudu, as proven by the hadith.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

The Ruling on Cat's Leftover Water (Su'r al-Hirrah)
Detailed ruling on cat's leftover water as an example of pure purifying disliked water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cat's leftover water and explain the reason for dislike.

Core Idea
Cat's leftover water is pure and purifying but disliked (makruh tanzih) when the water is little.

The second category of water in the Hanafi classification is 'pure and purifying but disliked.' The classic example is water from which a domestic cat has drunk. This lesson unpacks the evidence from the Prophet's action, the precaution due to potential impurity, and the restriction to small amounts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the second category
Recognize that water is still mutahhir but disliked due to the animal's nature.
Dislike is tanzihi (not haram).
2
Locate the evidence for the cat
The Prophet's action of inclining a vessel for a cat indicates permissibility, but the caution is due to the cat possibly having impurity on its mouth.
The hadith is referenced; the author assumes knowledge.
3
Understand the restriction
The dislike applies only when the water is a small amount (qalil). The precise measure will be given later.
Small water is more susceptible to impurity.
4
Differentiate animals
Domestic cat's su'r is disliked; wild cat's su'r is impure. Similar to free-range chicken and birds of prey.
Reason: these animals do not avoid obvious impurity.

Source Text

وماء البحر، وماء النهر، وماء البثرِ، وَمَا ذَابَ مِنَ الثّلج والبَرَدِ، وَمَاهُ العَيْنِ، ثُمَّ المَاهُ عَلَى خَمْسَةِ أَقْسَامٍ: طاهر مطهر غيرُ مكروه، وهو : الماءُ المُطْلَقُ.. (1) أنه ماء مطهر ، (و) مثله (ماء البحر ) الملح، لما روى مالك وأصحاب السنن الأربعة، عن أبي هريرة الله: أن رجلاً سأل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال: يا رسول الله، إنَّا نركب البحر ونحمل معنا القليلَ مِنَ المَاءِ، فإن توضأنا بِهِ عَطِشنا، أفنتوضأ من البحر؟ فقال: هو الطهور ماؤه الحل ميتته ). قال الترمذي: سألت محمـد بـن إسماعيل عن هذا الحديث، فقال : حديث صحيح. (وَ) كذا (ماء النهر)، كسيحون وجيحون والفــرات ونيل مصر، لأنها من الجنة، وهو ماء مطلق. (وماء البئر ) مطهر، (و) كذا (مَا ذَابَ من الثلج والبَرَدِ) بفتح الباء الموحدة والراء المهملة واحترز به عن ما يذوب من الملح؛ لأنه عكس الماء يذوب في الشتاء ويجمد في الصيف، وأما قبل انعقاده ملحاً، فهو طهور، (و) كذا (ماء العين)، وهو ما كان جارياً على وجــه الأرض من ينبوع، لما تقدم من النص . والإضافة في المياه المذكورات للتعريف لا للتقييد، والفرق بين الإضافتين صحة إطلاق الماء على الأول دون الثاني، كما سنذكره، (تم) ذكر جملة أنواع ( المياه)، فقال: هي ( عَلَى خَمْسَةِ أقسام)، لكل منها وصف يختص به. الأول: (طاهر مطهر غير مكروه، وهـو المـاء المُطلَقُ)، الذي سبق ذكره، ولم يخالطه شيء، فإن خالطه أو شرب منه حيوان، فسنذكر حكمه. وطاهرٌ مُطَهِّرٌ مَكْرُوهُ، وَهُوَ مَا شَرِبَ مِنْهُ الهِرَّةُ وَنَحْوُهَا ، وَكَانَ قَلِيلاً. وَطَاهِرٌ غَيْرُ مُطَهِّرٍ، وَهُوَ: مَا اسْتُعْمِلَ لِرَفْعِ حَدَثٍ، أَوْ لِقُرْبَةِ، كَالْوُضُوْءِ عَلَى الوُضُوْءِ بِنِيَّتِهِ، وَيَصِيرُ المَاءُ مُسْتَعْمَلَا بِمُجَرَّدِ الْفِصَالِهِ عَنِ الْجَسَدِ. وَلَا يَجُوزُ بِمَاءِ شَجَرِ وَثَمَرِ، وَلَوْ خَرَجَ بِنَفْسِهِ مَنْ غَيْرِ عَصْرِ، فِي الأَظْهَرِ، (و) الثاني: (طاهر مُطهر مكروه كراهة تنزيه على الأصح، كما ذهب إلـيـه « الـكـرخـي رحمه الله، (وهو ما شرب منه الهرةُ الأهلية، إذ الوحشية سؤرها نجس، (ونحوها) الدجاجة المخلاة، وسباع الطير، لأنها لا تتحامى عن النجاسة، وأكل الجيف وإصغاء النبي الله الإناء للهرة)، محمل فعله المقتضي عدم الكراهة، على زوال ذلك التوهم بأن كانت بمرأى منه، في زمان يمكن غسل فمها بلعابها، كما قرره بعض المحققين، وقيد الكراهة بقوله: (وَكَانَ) ما شربت منه الهرة (قليلا) وسيأتي تقديره". (و) الثالث: (طاهر غير مطهر)، يعني غير مزيل للحدث بخلاف الخبث، (وهـو مـا اسـتعمل) في الجسد، أو لاقاه بغير قصد (لرفع حَدَثٍ)، (أو) قصد استعماله (لِقُرْبَةٍ) وهي (كَالْوُضُوءِ) في مجلس آخر، عَلَى الوُضُوءِ بِنِيَّتِهِ)، أي: الوضوء تقرباً ليصير عبادة، فإن كان في مجلس واحــد كره، ويكون الماء غير مستعمل ، ومثله غسل يده للطعام، أو منه، إن قصد به القربة، لأنـه سـنة، لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : « الوضوء قَبْلَ الطَّعَامِ بَرَكَةٌ، وَبَعْدَهُ يَنْفِي اللمم -أي: الجنون- وقبلَهُ يَنْفِي الفقر ». فلو غسلها للوسخ، وهو متوضئ، ولم يقصد القربة، لا . يصير مستعملاً، كغسل ثوب ودابة مأكولة، (ويصيرُ الماءُ مُستعملاً بمجرَّدِ انفصاله عن الجسدِ)، وإن لم يستقر في محل، علـى الصحيح. لأن سقوط حكم الاستعمال قبل الانفصال لضرورة التطهير، ولا ضرورة بعد انفصاله، (وَلا يَجُوزُ) أي: لا يصح (بماء شجر وثمر)، لكمال امتزاجه، فلم يكن مطلقاً ، وَلَو خَرَجَ بِنَفْسِهِ مِنْ غَير عَصْرِ)، كالقاطر من الكرم ) ونحوه ( في الأظْهَر ) احترز به عما قيل بأنه يجوز بماء يقطر بنفسه، لأنـه ليـس
And water of the sea, and water of the river, and water of the well, and what melts from snow and hail, and water of the spring. Then water is of five categories: pure and purifying not disliked, and it is absolute water... (1) That it is purifying water, and likewise sea water (salty), due to what Malik and the authors of the four Sunan narrated from Abu Hurairah that a man asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'O Messenger of Allah, we travel by sea and carry with us a little water; if we perform ablution with it we become thirsty, so may we perform ablution with seawater?' He said: 'Its water is purifying, and its dead animals are lawful.' At-Tirmidhi said: I asked Muhammad ibn Ismail about this hadith, and he said: It is a sound hadith. (And) likewise river water, like Sayhun and Jayhun and the Euphrates and the Nile of Egypt, because they are from Paradise, and it is absolute water. (And) well water is purifying. (And) likewise what melts from snow and hail—with fatha on the ba and the ra—and it is a precaution against what melts from salt, because it is the opposite of water; it melts in winter and freezes in summer. But before it solidifies as salt, it is purifying. (And) likewise spring water, which is water flowing on the surface of the earth from a source, due to the textual evidence that preceded. The idafah (construct phrase) in the mentioned waters is for definition, not restriction, and the difference between the two idafahs is the validity of applying the name 'water' to the first but not the second, as we will mention. Then he mentioned the categories of waters, saying: They are of five categories, each having a specific description. The first: pure and purifying not disliked, and it is absolute water, which was mentioned earlier, and nothing has mixed with it. If something mixes with it or an animal drinks from it, we will mention its ruling later. And pure and purifying disliked, and it is that from which a cat and the like have drunk, and it was a small amount. And pure but not purifying, and it is what is used for removing ritual impurity or for an act of worship, like performing ablution upon ablution with the intention of worship, and the water becomes used merely by its separation from the body. And it is not permissible to perform ablution with water from trees and fruits, even if it comes out by itself without pressing, in the most apparent view. (And) the second: pure and purifying disliked with a dislike of tanzih according to the most correct view, as held by Al-Karkhi (may Allah have mercy on him), and it is that from which the domestic cat has drunk, as for a wild cat its leftover water is impure, and similar to it is the free-range chicken and birds of prey because they do not avoid impurity and eat carrion, and the Prophet's inclining the vessel for the cat—interpretation of his action indicating no dislike is based on the removal of that assumption, that it was in his sight at a time when it was possible to wash its mouth with its saliva, as some verifiers have established, and the dislike is restricted by his statement: (and it was) what the cat drank from (a small amount) and its estimation will come. (And) the third: pure but not purifying, meaning not removing ritual impurity as opposed to filth, and it is what is used on the body or contacted without intent to remove ritual impurity, or intended use for an act of worship, like ablution in another place upon ablution with its intention, i.e., performing ablution as a means of drawing closer to become worship. If it is in one place, it is disliked, and the water is not used. Similar to it is washing one's hand for food or from it if one intends worship, because it is sunnah, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Ablution before food is a blessing, and after it removes insanity, and before it removes poverty.' If he washes it for dirt while in a state of purity and does not intend worship, it does not become used, like washing a garment or an animal that is eaten. (And) the water becomes used merely by its separation from the body, even if it does not settle in a place, according to the correct view, because the ruling of being used falls before separation due to the necessity of purification, and there is no necessity after its separation. (And) it is not permissible, i.e., not valid, with water from trees and fruits, due to its complete mixture, so it is not absolute, even if it comes out by itself without pressing, like that dripping from the grapevine and the like, in the most apparent view, as a precaution against what is said that it is permissible with water that drips by itself, because it is not...
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage from the sharh explains the categories of water for ritual purification. The author first lists the types of water that are pure and purifying: sea, river, well, snow/hail melt, and spring water. The proof for sea water is the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) declared seawater purifying and its dead animals lawful, narrated by Malik and the four Sunan, and authenticated by Imam al-Bukhari. River water is included because rivers like Sayhun, Jayhun, Euphrates, and Nile are said to be from Paradise, hence they are absolute water. Well water is also purifying, and snow/hail melt is purifying as long as it hasn't turned into salt. Spring water is purifying based on earlier textual evidence. The idafa (construct phrase) in naming types of water is for definition, not restriction, so 'water of the sea' means the kind of water that is from the sea, not that only that specific water is purifying.

The text then moves to the five categories of water. The first category is pure and purifying and not disliked, which is absolute water that has not been mixed with anything. The second category is pure and purifying but disliked (makruh tanzihan), specifically water from which a domestic cat has drunk, provided the water is a small amount. The author explains that the leftover (su'r) of a domestic cat is pure but disliked because cats may have impurity on their mouths, though the Prophet's action of inclining a vessel for a cat suggests permissibility, understood as a case where the cat's mouth was clean. The dislike is restricted to a small amount, and its quantity will be defined later. The third category is pure but not purifying, which includes used water (musta'mal) for removing ritual impurity or for an act of worship, like performing ablution on top of ablution with the intention of worship. Water becomes used merely by separating from the body, and it cannot be used again for ritual purification. Also included are waters from trees and fruits, such as grape juice, even if it comes out without pressing, because it is not absolute water due to complete mixture.

The commentary emphasizes that used water remains pure in essence but loses its purifying quality for ritual purity. The ruling on tree water is that it is not valid for ablution in the most apparent view, contrary to some who deem it permissible if it flows by itself. The text also notes that washing hands for food or from food with the intention of worship does not make the water used, but if done for cleaning without intention, it remains usable.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): The leftover water remaining after an animal drinks from it.
كراهة تنزيه (karahah tanzih): Disliked but not sinful; avoidance is better but the act is still valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is cat's leftover water considered disliked?
A) Always, regardless of amount.
B) Only when the water is a small amount.
C) Only if the cat is wild.
D) Only if the cat is free-range.

Key Takeaway
Cat's leftover water is pure and purifying but disliked for small amounts due to precaution.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
6 min
Pure but Not Purifying: Used Water and Tree Water
Rulings on used water and tree water as examples of pure but not purifying water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between tahir and mutahhir, and state the rulings on used water and water from trees/fruits.

Core Idea
Used water is pure in itself but loses its purifying quality; tree water is not absolute and invalid for wudu.

The third category of water is 'pure but not purifying' (tahir ghayr mutahhir). This includes used water (musta'mal) that has been in contact with the body for purification, and water extracted from trees and fruits. The lesson clarifies how water becomes used, the effect of intention, and the reasons tree water is unsuitable.

Guided Path
1
Define used water
Water becomes musta' mal when it is used to remove ritual impurity (hadath) or for an act of worship with intention, and separates from the body.
Merely contacting the body does not make it used; it must be for purification.
2
Explore the condition of intention
If one performs wudu again on top of existing wudu with the intention of worship, the water becomes used. If done without intention (e.g., for dirt), it remains absolute.
The ruling on wudu over wudu is detailed: if done in the same session, it is disliked but water not used.
3
Identify the moment of becoming used
Water becomes used immediately upon separating from the body, even if it does not collect in a vessel.
Before separation, it is still usable for the ongoing purification.
4
Understand tree water
Water from trees (e.g., grape juice) is not absolute because it is fully mixed with the plant's essence, so it cannot purify. This holds even if it flows by itself without pressing.
The most apparent view rules it invalid for wudu.

وماء البحر، وماء النهر، وماء البثرِ، وَمَا ذَابَ مِنَ الثّلج والبَرَدِ، وَمَاهُ العَيْنِ، ثُمَّ المَاهُ عَلَى خَمْسَةِ أَقْسَامٍ: طاهر مطهر غيرُ مكروه، وهو : الماءُ المُطْلَقُ.. (وماء البئر ) مطهر، (و) كذا (مَا ذَابَ من الثلج والبَرَدِ) بفتح الباء الموحدة والراء المهملة واحترز به عن ما يذوب من الملح؛ لأنه عكس الماء يذوب في الشتاء ويجمد في الصيف، وأما قبل انعقاده ملحاً، فهو طهور، (و) كذا (ماء العين)، وهو ما كان جارياً على وجــه الأرض من ينبوع، لما تقدم من النص . والإضافة في المياه المذكورات للتعريف لا للتقييد، والفرق بين الإضافتين صحة إطلاق الماء على الأول دون الثاني، كما سنذكره، (تم) ذكر جملة أنواع ( المياه)، فقال: هي ( عَلَى خَمْسَةِ أقسام)، لكل منها وصف يختص به. الأول: (طاهر مطهر غير مكروه، وهـو المـاء المُطلَقُ)، الذي سبق ذكره، ولم يخالطه شيء، فإن خالطه أو شرب منه حيوان، فسنذكر حكمه. وطاهرٌ مُطَهِّرٌ مَكْرُوهُ، وَهُوَ مَا شَرِبَ مِنْهُ الهِرَّةُ وَنَحْوُهَا ، وَكَانَ قَلِيلاً. وَطَاهِرٌ غَيْرُ مُطَهِّرٍ، وَهُوَ: مَا اسْتُعْمِلَ لِرَفْعِ حَدَثٍ، أَوْ لِقُرْبَةِ، كَالْوُضُوْءِ عَلَى الوُضُوْءِ بِنِيَّتِهِ، وَيَصِيرُ المَاءُ مُسْتَعْمَلَا بِمُجَرَّدِ الْفِصَالِهِ عَنِ الْجَسَدِ. وَلَا يَجُوزُ بِمَاءِ شَجَرِ وَثَمَرِ، وَلَوْ خَرَجَ بِنَفْسِهِ مَنْ غَيْرِ عَصْرِ، فِي الأَظْهَرِ، (و) الثاني: (طاهر مُطهر مكروه كراهة تنزيه على الأصح، كما ذهب إلـيـه « الـكـرخـي رحمه الله، (وهو ما شرب منه الهرةُ الأهلية، إذ الوحشية سؤرها نجس، (ونحوها) الدجاجة المخلاة، وسباع الطير، لأنها لا تتحامى عن النجاسة، وأكل الجيف وإصغاء النبي الله الإناء للهرة)، محمل فعله المقتضي عدم الكراهة، على زوال ذلك التوهم بأن كانت بمرأى منه، في زمان يمكن غسل فمها بلعابها، كما قرره بعض المحققين، وقيد الكراهة بقوله: (وَكَانَ) ما شربت منه الهرة (قليلا) وسيأتي تقديره". (و) الثالث: (طاهر غير مطهر)، يعني غير مزيل للحدث بخلاف الخبث، (وهـو مـا اسـتعمل) في الجسد، أو لاقاه بغير قصد (لرفع حَدَثٍ)، (أو) قصد استعماله (لِقُرْبَةٍ) وهي (كَالْوُضُوءِ) في مجلس آخر، عَلَى الوُضُوءِ بِنِيَّتِهِ)، أي: الوضوء تقرباً ليصير عبادة، فإن كان في مجلس واحــد كره، ويكون الماء غير مستعمل ، ومثله غسل يده للطعام، أو منه، إن قصد به القربة، لأنـه سـنة، لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : « الوضوء قَبْلَ الطَّعَامِ بَرَكَةٌ، وَبَعْدَهُ يَنْفِي اللمم -أي: الجنون- وقبلَهُ يَنْفِي الفقر ». فلو غسلها للوسخ، وهو متوضئ، ولم يقصد القربة، لا . يصير مستعملاً، كغسل ثوب ودابة مأكولة، (ويصيرُ الماءُ مُستعملاً بمجرَّدِ انفصاله عن الجسدِ)، وإن لم يستقر في محل، علـى الصحيح. لأن سقوط حكم الاستعمال قبل الانفصال لضرورة التطهير، ولا ضرورة بعد انفصاله، (وَلا يَجُوزُ) أي: لا يصح (بماء شجر وثمر)، لكمال امتزاجه، فلم يكن مطلقاً ، وَلَو خَرَجَ بِنَفْسِهِ مِنْ غَير عَصْرِ)، كالقاطر من الكرم ) ونحوه ( في الأظْهَر ) احترز به عما قيل بأنه يجوز بماء يقطر بنفسه، لأنـه ليـس
And water of the sea, and water of the river, and water of the well, and what melts from snow and hail, and water of the spring. Then water is of five categories: pure and purifying not disliked, and it is absolute water... (1) That it is purifying water, and likewise sea water (salty), due to what Malik and the authors of the four Sunan narrated from Abu Hurairah that a man asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'O Messenger of Allah, we travel by sea and carry with us a little water; if we perform ablution with it we become thirsty, so may we perform ablution with seawater?' He said: 'Its water is purifying, and its dead animals are lawful.' At-Tirmidhi said: I asked Muhammad ibn Ismail about this hadith, and he said: It is a sound hadith. (And) likewise river water, like Sayhun and Jayhun and the Euphrates and the Nile of Egypt, because they are from Paradise, and it is absolute water. (And) well water is purifying. (And) likewise what melts from snow and hail—with fatha on the ba and the ra—and it is a precaution against what melts from salt, because it is the opposite of water; it melts in winter and freezes in summer. But before it solidifies as salt, it is purifying. (And) likewise spring water, which is water flowing on the surface of the earth from a source, due to the textual evidence that preceded. The idafah (construct phrase) in the mentioned waters is for definition, not restriction, and the difference between the two idafahs is the validity of applying the name 'water' to the first but not the second, as we will mention. Then he mentioned the categories of waters, saying: They are of five categories, each having a specific description. The first: pure and purifying not disliked, and it is absolute water, which was mentioned earlier, and nothing has mixed with it. If something mixes with it or an animal drinks from it, we will mention its ruling later. And pure and purifying disliked, and it is that from which a cat and the like have drunk, and it was a small amount. And pure but not purifying, and it is what is used for removing ritual impurity or for an act of worship, like performing ablution upon ablution with the intention of worship, and the water becomes used merely by its separation from the body. And it is not permissible to perform ablution with water from trees and fruits, even if it comes out by itself without pressing, in the most apparent view. (And) the second: pure and purifying disliked with a dislike of tanzih according to the most correct view, as held by Al-Karkhi (may Allah have mercy on him), and it is that from which the domestic cat has drunk, as for a wild cat its leftover water is impure, and similar to it is the free-range chicken and birds of prey because they do not avoid impurity and eat carrion, and the Prophet's inclining the vessel for the cat—interpretation of his action indicating no dislike is based on the removal of that assumption, that it was in his sight at a time when it was possible to wash its mouth with its saliva, as some verifiers have established, and the dislike is restricted by his statement: (and it was) what the cat drank from (a small amount) and its estimation will come. (And) the third: pure but not purifying, meaning not removing ritual impurity as opposed to filth, and it is what is used on the body or contacted without intent to remove ritual impurity, or intended use for an act of worship, like ablution in another place upon ablution with its intention, i.e., performing ablution as a means of drawing closer to become worship. If it is in one place, it is disliked, and the water is not used. Similar to it is washing one's hand for food or from it if one intends worship, because it is sunnah, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Ablution before food is a blessing, and after it removes insanity, and before it removes poverty.' If he washes it for dirt while in a state of purity and does not intend worship, it does not become used, like washing a garment or an animal that is eaten. (And) the water becomes used merely by its separation from the body, even if it does not settle in a place, according to the correct view, because the ruling of being used falls before separation due to the necessity of purification, and there is no necessity after its separation. (And) it is not permissible, i.e., not valid, with water from trees and fruits, due to its complete mixture, so it is not absolute, even if it comes out by itself without pressing, like that dripping from the grapevine and the like, in the most apparent view, as a precaution against what is said that it is permissible with water that drips by itself, because it is not...
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage from the sharh explains the categories of water for ritual purification. The author first lists the types of water that are pure and purifying: sea, river, well, snow/hail melt, and spring water. The proof for sea water is the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) declared seawater purifying and its dead animals lawful, narrated by Malik and the four Sunan, and authenticated by Imam al-Bukhari. River water is included because rivers like Sayhun, Jayhun, Euphrates, and Nile are said to be from Paradise, hence they are absolute water. Well water is also purifying, and snow/hail melt is purifying as long as it hasn't turned into salt. Spring water is purifying based on earlier textual evidence. The idafa (construct phrase) in naming types of water is for definition, not restriction, so 'water of the sea' means the kind of water that is from the sea, not that only that specific water is purifying.

The text then moves to the five categories of water. The first category is pure and purifying and not disliked, which is absolute water that has not been mixed with anything. The second category is pure and purifying but disliked (makruh tanzihan), specifically water from which a domestic cat has drunk, provided the water is a small amount. The author explains that the leftover (su'r) of a domestic cat is pure but disliked because cats may have impurity on their mouths, though the Prophet's action of inclining a vessel for a cat suggests permissibility, understood as a case where the cat's mouth was clean. The dislike is restricted to a small amount, and its quantity will be defined later. The third category is pure but not purifying, which includes used water (musta'mal) for removing ritual impurity or for an act of worship, like performing ablution on top of ablution with the intention of worship. Water becomes used merely by separating from the body, and it cannot be used again for ritual purification. Also included are waters from trees and fruits, such as grape juice, even if it comes out without pressing, because it is not absolute water due to complete mixture.

The commentary emphasizes that used water remains pure in essence but loses its purifying quality for ritual purity. The ruling on tree water is that it is not valid for ablution in the most apparent view, contrary to some who deem it permissible if it flows by itself. The text also notes that washing hands for food or from food with the intention of worship does not make the water used, but if done for cleaning without intention, it remains usable.

Key Terms
مستعمل (musta'mal): Used water: water that has been used for ritual purification (wudu or ghusl) and has separated from the body.
طاهر غير مطهر (tahir ghayr mutahhir): Pure but not purifying: ritually clean in itself but cannot remove ritual impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on using water that drips from a grapevine for wudu?
A) Permissible, it is pure and purifying.
B) Makruh tanzih.
C) Not valid (ghayr mutahhir) according to the most apparent view.
D) Valid only if it is a large amount.

Key Takeaway
Used water and tree water are pure but cannot be used for wudu; they lack the quality of being mutahhir.

Pure Purifying Disliked Water: The Domestic Cat's Leftover
Defines the second category of water: pure purifying disliked.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on water drunk by a domestic cat and identify the conditions that make it disliked (makruh tanzih) according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A domestic cat's leftover water is pure and purifying but disliked only when little.

In the Hanafi school, water is categorized into pure purifying, pure purifying but disliked, and impure. This lesson focuses on the second category: water that is pure and purifying but disliked (makruh tanzih). The primary example is water left after a domestic cat drinks, provided the water is little. We will explore why it is disliked, what types of animals share this ruling, and how the Prophet's ﷺ action sheds light on the matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category of water
Understand that this passage introduces the second category: pure purifying disliked water (طاهر مطهر مكروه). It is not impure, but its use is discouraged under specific conditions.
The first category is pure purifying water without dislike (e.g., rainwater, river water).
2
Pinpoint the primary example: domestic cat's leftover
The domestic cat (الهرة الأهلية) is the main example. Contrast this with the wild cat whose leftover is impure. Why the difference? Domestic cats live with humans and may have cleaner mouths, but there is still doubt about impurity.
Wild cats (وحشية) are considered likely to have impure mouths from consuming carrion.
3
Recognize the condition for dislike: water must be little
The text explicitly adds 'and it was little' (وكان قليلا). The dislike only applies when the water is a small quantity. The exact measure of 'little' (تقدير القلة) will be discussed later in the text.
If water is abundant (e.g., a large pond), the cat's leftover does not render it disliked due to the principle of water purity.
4
Understand the basis for dislike and the Prophetic action
The dislike is due to the possibility of impurity from the cat's mouth. However, the Prophet ﷺ tilted a vessel for a cat to drink, indicating that the leftover is not impure. This action is interpreted as removing the dislike when the cat is in sight and its mouth is likely clean (e.g., after it has licked itself clean).
This shows the dislike is not severe (tanzih) and can be lifted if the doubt is removed.
5
Extend the ruling to similar animals
Animals that do not avoid impurity and eat carrion (e.g., unsupervised hen, birds of prey) have the same ruling: their leftover is disliked when little. This is analogy (qiyas) to the domestic cat.
The hen is 'unsupervised' (مخلاة) meaning free-ranging and likely to eat impure things.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطاهرٌ مُطَهِّرٌ مَكْرُوهُ، وَهُوَ مَا شَرِبَ مِنْهُ الهِرَّةُ وَنَحْوُهَا ، وَكَانَ قَلِيلاً. (و) الثاني: (طاهر مطهر مكروه كراهة تنزيه على الأصح، كما ذهب إليه الكرخي رحمه الله، (وهو ما شرب منه الهرةُ الأهلية، إذ الوحشية سؤرها نجس، (ونحوها) الدجاجة المخلاة، وسباع الطير، لأنها لا تتحامى عن النجاسة، وأكل الجيف وإصغاء النبي الله الإناء للهرة)، محمل فعله المقتضي عدم الكراهة، على زوال ذلك التوهم بأن كانت بمرأى منه، في زمان يمكن غسل فمها بلعابها، كما قرره بعض المحققين، وقيد الكراهة بقوله: (وَكَانَ) ما شربت منه الهرة (قليلا) وسيأتي تقديره.
And pure purifying disliked, and it is what the cat and the like drank from, and it was little. (And) the second: pure purifying disliked with karaha tanzih on the most correct view, as held by al-Karkhi, (and it is what the domestic cat drank from, for the wild cat its leftover is impure, (and similar to it) the unsupervised hen, and birds of prey, because they do not avoid impurity, and they eat carcasses, and the Prophet's tilting the vessel for the cat), interpreting his action indicating lack of dislike, as removing that assumption by being in his sight, at a time when washing its mouth with its saliva is possible, as some verifiers determined, and he restricted the dislike by his saying: (And it was) what the cat drank from (little) and its estimation will come.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage defines the second category of water: pure and purifying but disliked (makruh tanzihan). The main example is water drunk by a domestic cat, but only if the water is little. The wild cat's leftover is impure. Similar animals include unsupervised chickens and birds of prey because they do not avoid impurities. The hadith of the Prophet tilting the vessel for the cat shows that the dislike is not severe; it can be removed if the cat is in sight and its mouth is likely clean. The dislike is conditional upon the water being little; the estimation of 'little' will come later. Key point: The cat's leftover is not impure, only disliked, and only when the water is scarce.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): The leftover water in a vessel after an animal has drunk from it.
الهرة الأهلية (al-hirrat al-ahliyyah): The domestic cat that lives with humans.
مكروه كراهة تنزيه (makruh karahatan tanzih): Disliked but not sinful; avoiding it is better but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is impure (najis).
B) It is pure and purifying without any dislike.
C) It is pure and purifying but disliked (makruh tanzih) if the water is little.
D) It is pure but not purifying.

Key Takeaway
Domestic cat leftover is pure but disliked (makruh tanzih) only when the water is little; the Prophet's action shows it is not impure.

Musta'mal Water: Pure but Not Purifying
Defines musta'mal water and its conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define musta'mal water, state its ruling (tahir ghayr mutahhir), and identify the conditions that make water musta'mal according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Water used for removing hadath or for qurbah becomes pure but no longer purifying.

In the Hanafi school, water is classified into three categories: pure and purifying, pure but not purifying, and impure. The second category, musta'mal water, is the focus here. Understanding when water becomes musta'mal is crucial for determining its permissibility in acts of worship, especially wudu and ghusl. This lesson defines musta'mal water, its causes, and its ruling, with attention to the role of intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the water category
Recognize that water can be tahir (pure) but not mutahhir (purifying), meaning it is clean but cannot remove ritual impurity.
This is the third of three water categories in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Understand the causes of musta'mal
Water becomes musta'mal when used for removing hadath (raf' hadath) or for an act of worship (qurbah), such as wudu performed with the intention of worship.
Intention matters for qurbah; washing hands for food without intention does not make water musta'mal.
3
Note the timing of ruling
Water becomes musta'mal upon separation from the body, even if it does not settle on a limb, according to the correct view.
This is a key point that differs from some opinions.
4
Distinguish exceptions
If wudu on wudu is performed in the same session, it is makruh and the water does not become musta'mal. Similarly, washing hands for dirt without qurbah intention does not affect the water.
The ruling depends on intention and context.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab difference
Unlike the Hanafi school, the Shafi'i school holds that musta'mal water remains tahir and mutahhir, so it can be reused for purification.
This difference affects practice in mixed-madhhab contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَطَاهِرٌ غَيْرُ مُطَهِّرٍ، وَهُوَ: مَا اسْتُعْمِلَ لِرَفْعِ حَدَثٍ، أَوْ لِقُرْبَةٍ، كَالْوُضُوْءِ عَلَى الوُضُوْءِ بِنِيَّتِهِ، وَيَصِيرُ المَاءُ مُسْتَعْمَلَا بِمُجَرَّدِ الْفِصَالِهِ عَنِ الْجَسَدِ. (و) الثالث: (طاهر غير مطهر)، يعني غير مزيل للحدث بخلاف الخبث، (وهو ما استعمل) في الجسد، أو لاقاه بغير قصد (لرفع حدث)، (أو) قصد استعماله (لقربة) وهي (كالوضوء) في مجلس آخر، على الوضوء بنيته)، أي: الوضوء تقرباً ليصير عبادة، فإن كان في مجلس واحد كره، ويكون الماء غير مستعمل، ومثله غسل يده للطعام، أو منه، إن قصد به القربة، لأنه سنة، لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : « الوضوء قبل الطعام بركة، وبعده ينفي اللمم -أي: الجنون- وقبله ينفي الفقر » (). فلو غسلها للوسخ، وهو متوضئ، ولم يقصد القربة، لا . يصير مستعملاً، كغسل ثوب ودابة مأكولة، (ويصير الماء مستعملاً بمجرد انفصاله عن الجسد)، وإن لم يستقر في محل، على الصحيح.
And pure not purifying, and it is: what has been used for removing hadath, or for qurbah, like wudu on wudu with its intention, and water becomes musta'mal by mere separation from the body. (And) the third: (pure not purifying), meaning not removing hadath contrary to khabath, (and it is what is used) on the body, or contacted it without intention (for removing hadath), (or) intention to use it (for qurbah) which is (like wudu) in another session, wudu on wudu with its intention), i.e., wudu to draw near to become worship, for if it is in one session it is disliked, and the water is not musta'mal. And like it is washing his hand for food, or from it, if he intends qurbah with it, because it is sunnah, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Wudu before food is blessing, and after it removes insanity, and before it removes poverty.' So if he washes it for dirt, while he has wudu, and does not intend qurbah, it does not become musta'mal, like washing a garment and a permissible-to-eat animal. (And water becomes musta'mal by mere separation from the body), even if it did not settle on a limb, according to the correct view.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage defines the third category of water: pure (tahir) but not purifying (ghayr mutahhir) for removing hadath. This includes water that has been used for removing ritual impurity (hadath) or for an act of worship (qurbah), such as performing wudu again on top of existing wudu with the intention of worship. The water becomes musta'mal (used) upon separation from the body, regardless of whether it settled on a limb. However, if one performs wudu on wudu in the same session, it is disliked and the water does not become musta'mal. Similarly, washing one's hands for food with the intention of qurbah (because it is sunnah) causes the water to become musta'mal, but if washed for dirt without qurbah intention, it does not. The hadith cited supports the sunnah of wudu before food.

Key Terms
مستعمل (musta'mal): Water that has been used for removing hadath or for qurbah; it is pure but cannot be used for purification again.
قربة (qurbah): An act done to draw near to Allah, such as wudu performed with the intention of worship.
رفع حدث (raf' hadath): Removing ritual impurity that prevents valid prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Upon separation from the body after being used for hadath or qurbah, even if it did not settle.
C) Only if used for removing hadath, not for qurbah.
D) It never becomes musta'mal; all water remains mutahhir.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, water becomes musta'mal (tahir but not mutahhir) upon separation from the body after being used for hadath or qurbah, and cannot be reused for wudu or ghusl.

Water Permissibility for Wudu: The Hanafi Criterion
Explains impermissible water: from trees/fruits, and water changed by cooking or mixing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which types of water are impermissible for wudu and apply the Hanafi criterion of thinness and fluidity to determine validity.

Core Idea
Water from trees/fruits and water that lost its fluidity is impermissible for wudu; thinness and flow are the key.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah details two categories of water that are not valid for wudu: water extracted from trees and fruits (even without pressing), and water whose natural thinness and fluidity have been removed by cooking or mixing with solids. The core principle is that water must remain absolute (mutlaq) and retain its flowing nature; mere changes in color, taste, or smell do not harm permissibility as long as the water remains thin and flows.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of impermissible water
Read the text and distinguish the first ruling (water from trees and fruits) from the second (water changed by cooking or mixing). Note the key phrases: 'ماء شجر وثمر' and 'ماء زال طبعه'.
The passage also covers mixed water with solids that remain fluid.
2
Understand the criterion: thinness and fluidity (al-riqqah wa al-sayalan)
The Hanafi school defines absolute water (mā' muṭlaq) as water that is naturally thin and flows. When a substance (solid or cooked food) changes the water so that it becomes thick and no longer flows, it becomes restricted (muqayyad) and invalid for wudu.
The passage explains that 'al-tab'' (nature) of water is thinness and fluidity.
3
Distinguish between cases where the water remains permissible
If water is cooked with cleaning agents (e.g., soap) and remains thin, wudu is valid. Similarly, if a pure solid (e.g., saffron) is mixed without cooking and the water remains fluid, it remains permissible even if color/taste change.
The key is whether the water loses its ability to flow and be wrung from a garment.
4
Apply the criterion to examples
Practice with scenarios: grape juice (impermissible), water with cooked beans that thickens (impermissible), water with saffron that stays thin (permissible), well water with mineral taste (permissible).
The text explicitly mentions that change of all attributes (color, taste, smell) by a solid that does not remove fluidity is harmless.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلا يَجُوزُ بِمَاءِ شَجَرِ وَثَمَرِ، وَلَوْ خَرَجَ بِنَفْسِهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ عَصْرِ، فِي الأَظْهَرِ، لخروجه بلا عصر تأثير في نفي القيد، وصحة نفي الاسم عنه، ولا يصح إلحاق المقيد بالمطلق في إزالة الحكمية، كما ألحقه أبو حنيفة به في إزالة الحقيقية لفوات شرطه، فإن حكم الأصل، أعني إزالة الحكمية غير معقول، إذ لا نجاسة على أعضاء المحدث محسوسة يزيلها الماء ليلحق به المقيد، بل الكائن اعتبار شرعي محض له حكم النجاسة، لمنع الصلاة معه، وقد عين لإزالته شرعاً آلة)، فلا يمكن إلحاق غيرها بها، بخلاف تعليق ذلك الاعتبار نفسه بخروج النجاسة، فإنه لما عقل اعتبار خروجها مؤثراً في ذلك دار معه، سواء كانت من السبيلين أو غيرهما، وكان الاقتصار على الأعضاء الأربعة غير معقول، (وَلا) يجوز الوضوء بماء زال طَبْعُهُ) ، وهو الرقة والسيلان بأن صار ثخيناً (بالطَّبخ) بما يقصد به النظافة كالسدر والصابون والأشنان)، وإن بقي على رقته وسيلانه، بطبخه بما يقصد به التنظيف جاز به الوضوء، وأما إذا طبخ به نحو الباقلاء، والحمص ونضج فإنه لا يجوز به الوضوء، لكمال الامتزاج، وبه يخرج الماء عن طبعه، لأنه إذا برد ثخن غالباً، ولما كان تقييد الماء يحصل بأحد أمرين: كمال الامتزاج بتشرب النبات أو الطبخ بالذي قدمه، ذكر الثاني، وهو غلبة الممتزج بقوله: (أو بغَلَبَةِ غَيْرِهِ)، أي: غير الماء (عليه)، أي: الماء. ولما كانت الغلبة مختلفة باختلاف المخالط بغير طبخ، ذكر ملخص ما جعله المحققون ضابطاً في ذلك فقال: (والغلَبَةُ) تكون (في مُخالَطَةِ الجَامِدَات) الطاهرة (بِإخْرَاجِ المَاءِ عَنْ رِقْتِهِ)، فلا ينعصر عن الثوب (و) إخراجه عن ( سيلانِهِ)، فلا يسيل على الأعضاء سيلان الماء. وأما إذا بقي على رقته وسيلانه فإنه ( لا يَضُرُّ ) صحة التوضؤ بـه، أي: ولا يمنع جواز التوضؤ به (تَغَيُّرُ أَوصَافِهِ كُلَّهَا بجامد) خالطه بدون طبخ، كزَعفران، وفاكهة، وورق شجر). وإضافته إلى الزعفران ونحوه لتعريف نوع من الماء، كماء البئر، فلا تفيد التقييد، ولذا صح إطلاق الماء عليه بدون قيده.
And it is not permissible with water of tree and fruit, even if it comes out by itself without pressing, in the most apparent view, because its coming out without pressing has an effect in negating the restriction, and correct is negating the name from it, and it is not correct to analogize the restricted to the unrestricted in removing the legal impurity, as Abu Hanifa analogized it to removing physical impurity due to absence of its condition, for the ruling of the original, meaning removing legal impurity, is not rationally understood, since there is no tangible impurity on the limbs of the person with hadath that water removes to analogize the restricted to it, rather it is a pure legal consideration having the ruling of impurity, to prevent prayer with it, and for its removal an instrument has been legally designated, so it is not possible to analogize others to it, unlike attaching that same consideration to the exit of impurity, for when the consideration of its exit being effective in that was understood, it revolves with it, whether it is from the two passages or other than them, and restricting to the four limbs is not rationally understood. (And) it is not permissible to perform wudu with water whose nature has changed, i.e., thinness and fluidity so that it becomes thick, by cooking with what is intended for cleaning like lote-tree, soap, and ash, and if it remains in its thinness and fluidity, having been cooked with what is intended for cleaning, wudu with it is permissible. But if it is cooked with something like broad beans, chickpeas, and matures, then wudu with it is not permissible, due to complete mixing, and thereby the water leaves its nature, because when it cools it thickens often. And since the restriction of water is achieved by one of two things: complete mixing by saturation of the plant or cooking by what was presented, he mentioned the second, which is the predominance of the mixed substance by his saying: (or by the predominance of other than it), i.e., other than water (over it), i.e., water. And since predominance varies with the difference of the mixer without cooking, he mentioned a summary of what the verifiers made as a criterion in that, saying: (And predominance) occurs (in mixing with solids) that are pure (by taking the water out of its thinness), so it cannot be wrung from the garment (and) taking it out of (its fluidity), so it does not flow over the limbs like water. But if it remains in its thinness and fluidity, then it does not harm the correctness of wudu with it, i.e., it does not prevent the permissibility of wudu with it, (the change of all its attributes by a solid) mixed with it without cooking, like saffron, fruit, and tree leaves. And its addition to saffron and the like is to define a type of water, like well water, so it does not confer restriction, and therefore it is correct to apply the name water to it without its restriction.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage discusses water that is not permissible for wudu. First, water extracted from trees and fruits (like grape juice) is not valid, even if it drips without pressing, because it is not absolute water (mā' muṭlaq). Abu Hanifa's analogy to physical cleaning is rejected because legal impurity (hadath) is a legal fiction, not a tangible stain. Second, water that has been cooked with cleaning agents (like soap) remains permissible if it retains its fluidity, but if cooked with foods (like beans) and becomes thick, it is impermissible. Third, water mixed with pure solids (like saffron) is still permissible for wudu as long as it remains thin and flows; the change in color, taste, or smell does not harm permissibility. The criterion for solid mixtures is whether they remove the water's thinness and flow; if they do, the water is restricted (muqayyad) and not absolute.

Key Terms
الماء المقيد (al-mā' al-muqayyad): Water that is not absolute (mutlaq), e.g., water mixed with a substance that changes its nature or water from trees/fruits.
الغلبة (al-ghalabah): Predominance of a solid substance over water such that the water loses its thinness and fluidity.
الطبع (al-ṭab'): The natural quality of water: thinness and fluidity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT permissible for wudu according to the Hanafi school?
A) Water from a spring that has turned yellow due to fallen leaves but still flows.
B) Water that has been cooked with soap and is still thin.
C) Water extracted from grapes by pressing.
D) Water from a well that has a slight change in taste due to minerals.

Key Takeaway
Water is valid for wudu only if it is absolute (mutlaq) and retains its natural thinness and fluidity; mere changes in color, taste, or smell are harmless.
