Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Water Changed by Cooking or Mixing: Rulings for Wudu
Commentary on water's change through cooking or mixing and its effect on wudu validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi criteria for when water mixed with a solid or liquid remains valid for wudu and identify which change invalidates it.

Core Idea
Water remains purifying unless it loses its fluidity or a mixed liquid's attribute predominates.

In this passage from Imdad al-Fattah, the author explains the crucial distinction between water that is merely changed in color or smell and water that has lost its essential fluidity. Understanding this difference is key to applying the Hanafi ruling on mixed water for wudu. The passage also clarifies the legal difference between 'additive for definition' and 'additive for restriction'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Locate the main ruling: water is invalid for wudu if its natural property (tab') is removed by cooking or if the mixed substance predominates. Note the exception: mere change of properties by a solid without loss of fluidity does not invalidate.
The term tab' refers to thinness (riqqa) and flowing (sayalan).
2
Distinguish solids vs. liquids
For solids, predominance is determined by removal of water's fluidity (no longer thin and flowing). For liquids, predominance is determined by the appearance of one attribute (e.g., color or taste) of a liquid that has two attributes.
Example: Milk has color and taste; if either appears, water is invalid.
3
Understand the role of tab'
Water's natural property (tab') is its fluidity. If cooking removes fluidity (e.g., beans make water thick), wudu is invalid. If cooking with cleaning agents (e.g., soap) does not remove fluidity, wudu is valid.
Cooking with broad beans or chickpeas typically thickens the water.
4
Analyze the hadith evidence
Review the cited hadith: Prophet ordered ghusl with water and lotus (a solid) for a muhrim and for Qays ibn 'Asim. He also performed ghusl with water containing dough traces and with marsh mallow. These prove that water mixed with pure solids remains purifying as long as fluidity remains.
The lotus is a solid that changes water's properties but does not remove fluidity.
5
Apply the ruling to examples
Test scenarios: saffron water (valid if fluid), rose water (restricted, not valid for wudu), milk mixed water (invalid if color or taste appears), watermelon juice (invalid if single attribute appears).
Restricted water like rose water cannot be called 'water' absolutely.

(والغَلَبَةُ) تحصل (في) مخالطة (المائِعَاتِ بِظُهُورِ وَصْفِ وَاحِدٍ) كلون فقط، أو طعم (من مائع له وصفانِ فَقَط)، ومثل ذلك بقوله : ( كاللَّبَنِ: لَهُ اللّونُ والطَّعم)، فإن لم يوجدا جاز به التوضؤ، وإن وجد أحدهما لم يجز، كما لو كان المخالط له وصف واحد، فظهر ذلك الوصف، كبعض البطيخ
And not with water whose natural property (fluidity) has been removed by cooking, or by the predominance of something else over it. And predominance in mixing with solids: by removing the water from its thinness and flowing. And it does not harm if all its properties change by a solid, like saffron, fruit, and tree leaves. [Because it comes out without pressing, having an effect in negating the restriction, and the validity of negating the name from it.] And it is not valid to analogize the restricted to the absolute in removing the legal impurity, as Abu Hanifa analogized it to it in removing the real impurity due to the lack of its condition. For the ruling of the original, meaning removal of legal impurity, is not rational, since there is no tangible impurity on the limbs of the person in minor impurity that water removes to analogize the restricted to it. Rather, what exists is a pure legal consideration having the ruling of impurity, to prevent prayer with it, and a tool has been specified by law for its removal, so it is not possible to analogize others to it. Unlike the attachment of that same consideration to the removal of impurity, for when the consideration of its removal was rationally understood as effective in that, it revolves with it, whether it is from the two passages or other than them, and restricting to the four limbs is not rational. And it is not permissible to perform wudu with water whose natural property has been removed, which is thinness and flowing, such that it becomes thick, by cooking with what is intended for cleaning, like lotus leaves, soap, and saltwort. And if it remains in its thinness and flowing, by cooking it with what is intended for cleaning, wudu with it is permissible. As for if one cooks with it something like broad beans and chickpeas and they become cooked, then wudu with it is not permissible, due to complete mixing, and thereby the water leaves its natural property, because when it cools it mostly thickens. And since the restriction of water occurs by one of two things: complete mixing by absorption of the plant or cooking with what was mentioned, he mentioned the second, which is the predominance of the mixed substance by his saying: 'or by the predominance of something else over it', meaning other than water over it, i.e., water. And since predominance differs according to the mixing substance without cooking, he mentioned a summary of what the verifiers made as a rule in that, saying: 'And predominance occurs in mixing with pure solids by removing the water from its thinness and from its flowing.' And if it remains in its thinness and flowing, then the change of all its properties by a solid mixed without cooking, like saffron, fruit, and tree leaves, does not harm the validity of wudu with it. And its addition to saffron and the like is to define a type of water, like well water, so it does not effect restriction, and therefore it is valid to apply the name water to it without its restriction. In watermelon and rose water it is for restriction, and it is called restricted water, because like its name it is restricted, its essence is not known except by restriction. For example, rose water, a person is not able to call it water absolutely, but he must restrict it, saying: rose water so that it is understood. And this is the difference between the additive of restriction and the additive of definition. The sign of the additive of definition is the deficiency of the essence in the added word, which is water. For its deficiency restricts it, so that it does not enter into what is not restricted at all. This is clarified: if he swears not to pray, he breaks the oath by praying Zuhr prayer, because it is absolute, and its addition to Zuhr is for definition, and he does not break it by praying funeral prayer, because it is not prayer absolutely, so its addition to funeral is for restriction. If it is said: the absolute refers to the perfect, not the deficient, and the water changed by something like saffron is deficient, we say: the absolute refers to the perfect in essence, not in description, and water changed by a pure substance is perfect in essence, so the absolute name of water applies to it. If it is said: if he swears not to drink water, and he drinks this water changed by something like saffron, he does not break his oath; and if a pilgrim in ihram uses water mixed with saffron, he owes a fidyah; and if he appoints an agent to buy him water, and he buys this water, it is not binding on the principal; thus it is known that this changed water is not absolute water. We say: the basis of oaths and agency is custom, and the obligation of fidyah is due to the perfume in the water, and that does not remove the water from being purifying. In al-Bukhari and Muslim that the Prophet ﷺ ordered to wash the one whom his she-camel threw and he was in ihram with water and lotus leaves. And he ordered Qays ibn 'Asim when he became Muslim to perform ghusl with water and lotus leaves. And he ﷺ performed ghusl with water containing traces of dough. And from 'A'ishah that he ﷺ used to perform ghusl and wash his head with marsh mallow while he was junub, and he would suffice with that and not pour water on it. And predominance occurs in mixing with liquids by the appearance of one attribute, like color only or taste, of a liquid that has only two attributes, and he gave an example of that by saying: like milk: it has color and taste. If neither is present, then wudu with it is permissible; if one of them appears, it is not permissible, as if the mixed substance has one attribute and that attribute appears, like some watermelon.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of water that has been changed by cooking or mixing, and its validity for wudu. The author explains that water loses its purifying quality if its natural fluidity (tab') is removed by cooking (e.g., cooked with cleaning agents like lotus, soap, saltwort) or by the predominance of a solid substance that makes it thick and non-flowing. However, if the water remains fluid (thin and flowing), mere change in its properties (color, taste, smell) due to mixing with a pure solid without cooking does not affect its validity for wudu. For example, water mixed with saffron, fruit, or leaves is still valid for wudu as long as it remains fluid. The commentary then delves into the distinction between additive for definition (idafat al-ta'rif) and additive for restriction (idafat al-taqyid) using examples: well water is defined but not restricted; rose water is restricted because it cannot be called 'water' absolutely. The passage also addresses objections regarding oaths, agency, and ihram, clarifying that custom ('urf) governs those matters, and the purifying quality remains. Finally, hadith evidence is cited: the Prophet ordered ghusl with water and lotus for a muhrim who died, and for Qays ibn 'Asim upon conversion, and he himself performed ghusl with water containing traces of dough and with marsh mallow. These hadiths show that water mixed with pure substances (like lotus, marsh mallow) is permissible for ghusl and wudu. The ruling for liquids like milk: if the mixing liquid has two attributes (color and taste), wudu is invalid if one of them appears; if neither appears, it is valid. For a liquid with one attribute (e.g., watermelon juice), the appearance of that attribute invalidates wudu.

Key Terms
الطبع (al-tab'): The natural property of water: thinness (riqqa) and flowing (sayalan).
الغلبة (al-ghalaba): Predominance of a mixed substance over water, determined by removing water's fluidity (for solids) or appearing in one attribute (for liquids).
إضافة التقييد (idafat al-taqyid): A genitive construction that restricts the meaning, e.g., 'maw' al-ward' (rose water), where the added word specifies a type that is not considered water absolutely.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If water is mixed with solid saffron and becomes yellow, but remains thin and flows, is wudu valid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Yes, because the water retains its fluidity.
B) No, because the color changed.
C) Yes, but only if the saffron is removed.
D) No, because saffron is a liquid when dissolved.

Key Takeaway
Water mixed with pure solids remains valid for wudu as long as it retains its fluidity; for liquids, any appearance of the liquid's attribute invalidates it.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Muqayyad Water and the Evidence for Taharah
Discussing the definition of muqayyad water and responding to objections using hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on muqayyad water and cite the hadith evidence proving it is tahur.

Core Idea
Muqayyad water is tahur but not mutlaq; wudu requires mutlaq water.

This passage clarifies the crucial distinction between mutlaq (absolute) and muqayyad (restricted) water in Hanafi fiqh. It defines ghalaba (overwhelming), distinguishes between restrictive and definitional genitives, and responds to objections. The author then provides explicit hadith proofs that water mixed with pure substances like lotus leaves, dough, and marshmallow remains tahur (purifying), though it is not mutlaq and thus invalid for wudu.

Guided Path
1
Define ghalaba and muqayyad
Understand the concept of ghalaba in liquids: when a pure substance's description dominates, the water becomes muqayyad. The author gives examples of milk, watermelon, and rose.
Ghalaba is determined by the appearance of one description (e.g., color or taste) in a liquid that originally has two descriptions.
2
Distinguish between idafat al-taqyid and idafat al-ta'rif
Notice the linguistic difference: a restrictive genitive (like 'rose water') limits the essence, while a definitional genitive (like 'Zuhr prayer') identifies a specific instance of a general category.
The sign of definitional genitive is that the annexed word (e.g., water) is deficient and needs specification.
3
Analyze the objections and responses
The author presents objections concerning oaths, ihram, and agency, and responds by grounding these rulings in custom (urf) and the fact that perfume does not negate taharah.
This shows that legal rulings may differ based on context, but the fundamental property of taharah remains.
4
Cite the hadith evidence
The Prophet ﷺ ordered washing a deceased pilgrim with water and sidr, ordered Qays ibn 'Asim to bathe with water and sidr, bathed in water with traces of dough, and used marshmallow for ghusl. These demonstrate that muqayyad water is tahur.
The hadith are from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim, but are ahad (zanni al-thubut), yet their authenticity is strong.
5
Derive the Hanafi ruling
From the hadith, the Hanafi school concludes that muqayyad water is tahur (purifying) but not mutlaq. For wudu and ghusl, mutlaq water is required, so muqayyad water is insufficient.
The Shafi'i school disagrees, holding that muqayyad water is valid for wudu as long as it is still called water.

والغَلَبَةُ في المائِعَاتِ بِظُهُورِ وَصْفِ وَاحِدٍ من مائع لهُ وصفانِ فَقَط، كاللَّبَنِ: لَهُ اللّونُ والطَّعم . البطيخ والورد للتقييد، وسمي . ماء مقيداً، لأنه كاسمه مقيد، لا تعرف ذاته إلا بالقيد، فإن ماء الورد مثلاً، لا يقدر الإنسان على أن يسميه ماء على الإطلاق، بل لا بد له من أن يقيده، فيقول: ماء الورد حتى يفهم، وكذا ما كان مثله، وهذا هو الفرق بين إضافة التقييد، وإضافة التعريف، فعلامة إضافة التعريف قصور الماهية في المضاف، الذي هو الماء، فإن قصورها قيده؛ لئلا يدخل فيما ليس مقيداً بالمرة، يوضحه لو حلف لا يصلي، حنث بصلاة الظهر، لأنها مطلقة، وإضافتها إلى الظهر للتعريف، ولا يحنث بصلاة الجنازة، لأنها ليست صلاة مطلقاً، فإضافتها للجنازة للتقييد، فإن قيل: المطلق ينصرف إلى الكامل دون الناقص، والماء المتغير بنحو زعفران قاصر، قلنا المطلق ينصرف إلى الكامل ذاتاً لا وصفاً، والماء المتغير بطاهر كامل ذاتاً، فيتناوله مطلق اسم الماء، فإن قيل: لـو حـلـف لا يشرب ماء، فشرب هذا المتغير بنحو ،زعفران، لم يحنث، ولو استعمل المحرم الماء المختلط بزعفران لزمته الفدية، ولو وكَّل وكيلاً ليشتري له ماء، فاشترى هذا الماء لا يلزم الموكل، فعلم بهذا أن ذلك المتغير ليس ماء مطلقاً، قلنا: مبنى الإيمان والوكالة على العرف، ولزوم الفدية، لما في الماء من الطيب، وذلك لا يخرج الماء عن كونه مطهراً. وفي ( البخاري» و «مسلم» أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم « أمر بغسل الذي وقصته ناقته وهو محرم بماء وسدرٍ » . « وأمر قيس بن عاصم حينَ أسلم أن يغتسل بماء وسدر » . ( واغتسل عليه الصلاة والسلام بماءٍ فيه أثر العجين ) (۳). وعن عائشة ، أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام ( كان يغتسل ويغسلُ رَأسَهُ بالخطمي، وهو جنب ويجتزى بذلك ولا يصب عليه الماء )
And overwhelming in liquids [occurs] by the appearance of one description from a liquid that has only two descriptions, like milk: it has color and taste. Watermelon and rose are for restriction, and it is called restricted water because, as its name indicates, it is restricted; its essence is not known except by restriction. For example, rose water, a person cannot call it water absolutely, but must restrict it and say 'rose water' to be understood, and likewise for similar things. This is the difference between a restrictive genitive and a definitional genitive: the sign of a definitional genitive is the deficiency of the essence in the annexed word, which is water; its deficiency restricts it so that it does not enter into that which is not restricted at all. This is clarified by the example: if one swears not to pray, he would be breaking his oath by praying Zuhr prayer because it is absolute, and its attribution to Zuhr is for definition; he would not break his oath by praying the funeral prayer because it is not prayer absolutely, so its attribution to the funeral is for restriction. If it is said: the absolute refers to the perfect, not the deficient, and water changed by something like saffron is deficient, we say: the absolute refers to perfection of essence, not description; water changed by a pure substance is perfect in essence, so the absolute name of water includes it. If it is said: if one swears not to drink water, and he drinks this water changed by something like saffron, he does not break his oath; if a pilgrim in ihram uses water mixed with saffron, he owes a fidyah; if one appoints an agent to buy water for him, and he buys this water, it does not bind the principal; it is thus known that such changed water is not absolute water. We say: the basis of oaths and agency is custom, and the obligation of fidyah is due to the perfume in the water; that does not remove the water from being purifying. And in al-Bukhari and Muslim, that the Prophet ﷺ ordered to wash the one whose camel killed him while in ihram with water and lotus leaves, and ordered Qays ibn 'Asim when he became Muslim to bathe with water and lotus leaves, and he ﷺ bathed with water containing traces of dough, and from 'A'ishah that he ﷺ would bathe and wash his head with marshmallow while in janabah and suffice with that without pouring water over himself.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof from the Sharh of Nur al-Idah. It explains the concept of ghalaba (overwhelming) in liquids and the distinction between muqayyad (restricted) and mutlaq (absolute) water. The author begins by stating that ghalaba in liquids occurs when one description (e.g., color or taste) appears from a liquid that has only two descriptions, like milk (color and taste). The example of watermelon and rose is given to illustrate that water becomes muqayyad when it takes on the description of what is mixed with it. The author distinguishes between two types of idafah (genitive construction): idafat al-taqyid (restrictive) and idafat al-ta'rif (definitional). In the restrictive type, the annexed word (e.g., water) cannot be known except by restriction (e.g., rose water). The author then uses examples from oaths and agency to clarify that the absolute name applies to essence, not description. A series of objections are raised and answered: (1) The claim that the absolute refers to the perfect, not the deficient, is rebutted by saying that perfection relates to essence, not description. (2) Objections based on oaths, ihram, and agency are answered by noting that these are based on custom (urf) and that the presence of perfume does not remove water's purifying quality. The passage then provides explicit hadith proofs: the Prophet ﷺ ordered washing a deceased pilgrim with water and sidr (lotus leaves), ordered Qays ibn 'Asim to bathe with water and sidr upon embracing Islam, bathed himself in water containing traces of dough, and used marshmallow (khatmi) for bathing. These hadith demonstrate that water mixed with pure substances remains purifying (tahur), even if it becomes muqayyad.

Key Terms
غَلَبَة (ghalaba): Overwhelming, i.e., when a mixed substance's description dominates the water such that it loses its absolute character.
مُطْلَق (mutlaq): Absolute water, i.e., water that is not mixed with anything else, retaining its original name 'water' without qualification.
مُقَيَّد (muqayyad): Restricted water, i.e., water mixed with a pure substance such that it is called by a compound name like 'rose water'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on wudu with water in which a pure substance's description dominates (ghalaba)?
A) Wudu is valid because the water remains tahur.
B) Wudu is invalid because the water is muqayyad and not mutlaq.
C) Wudu is valid only if the change is by color alone.
D) Wudu is invalid only if the change is by taste.

Key Takeaway
Muqayyad water is purifying (tahur) but not absolute (mutlaq); thus it cannot be used for wudu, as per the Hanafi school, but the hadith confirm its taharah.

Ruling on Ghalaba by Weight and the Definition of Najis Water
Rules of ghalaba by weight and definition of najis water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for ghalaba by weight to liquids with no description and state the conditions that make water najis.

Core Idea
Water with no visible description is judged by weight; small stagnant water becomes najis instantly on impurity contact.

This lesson continues the Sharh of Nur al-Idah, explaining how to determine overwhelming (ghalaba) when a liquid has no distinguishing traits like colour, taste, or smell. The author then defines the fourth type of water: najis water, which depends on the water being stagnant and smaller than ten by ten cubits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of liquid mixture
Determine if the liquid mixing with water has two, three, or no descriptions. For liquids with no description, such as used water or rose water without smell, ghalaba is judged by weight.
This is the third category; previous categories used visible descriptions.
2
Apply the weight test
If the restricted water (muqayyad) outweighs the absolute water (mutlaq), wudu is invalid. If mutlaq is heavier, wudu is valid. If equal, follow the overcome (mughlab) as a precaution.
The ruling for equal parts is not in Zahir al-Riwayah; later scholars provided the precautionary view.
3
Define najis water conditions
Najis water requires: (a) certainty or strong presumption of impurity falling in, (b) water is stagnant (rakid), and (c) the water body is small (less than 10x10 common cubits).
Small water becomes najis even without visible change; large water requires a trace of impurity.
4
Recognize the threshold
The boundary is ten by ten common cubits (approx. 4.6 m x 4.6 m) for a square tank, or thirty-six for a circular one. Below that, any impurity makes the water najis.
This is a Hanafi specific ruling; the Shafi'i school uses the qullatayn measure instead.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والغَلَبَةُ) تحصل (في) مخالطة (المائِعَاتِ بِظُهُورِ وَصْفِ وَاحِدٍ) كلون فقط، أو طعم (من مائع له وصفانِ فَقَط)، ومثل ذلك بقوله : ( كاللَّبَنِ: لَهُ اللّونُ والطَّعم)، فإن لم يوجدا جاز به التوضؤ، وإن وجد أحدهما لم يجز، كما لو كان المخالط له وصف واحد، فظهر ذلك الوصف، كبعض البطيخ، وقوله: (ولا رائحةَ لَهُ زيادة إيضاح لعلمه من بيان الوصفين. (وَ) الغلبة توجد (بظُهُورِ وَصَفَيْنِ مِنْ مَائِع، له) أوصاف (ثَلاثَةٌ)، وذلك ( كالخَلّ)، له لون وطعم وريح، فأي وصفين منهما ظهرا منعا صحـة التوضؤ، والواحد منها لا يضر لقلته، (والغَلَبَةُ في مخالطة (المَائِعِ الَّذِي لا وَصْفَ لَهُ) مخالف للماء، وذلك (كالماءِ المُسْتَعْمَل)، فإنه طاهر على الصحيح، وماء الورد المنقطع الرائحة، تـكـون بالوزن)، لعدم التمييز بالوصف لفقده، فإن اختلطَ رِطلانِ)) مثلاً مِنَ المَاءِ المُسْتَعْمَل)، أو ماء الورد المنقطع الرائحة، (برطل من الماء (المُطْلَق، لا يَجُوزُ بِهِ الوُضُوءُ)، لغلبة المقيد، (وبعكسه). وهو لو كان الأكثر المطلق (جَازَ) به الوضوء، وإن استويا لم يذكر حكمه في ظـاهـر الرواية، وقالوا: حكمه حكم المغلوب احتياطاً، لما طال الفصل. قال: (والرابع) من أنواع المياه: (مَاءٌ نَجِسٌ ، وَهُوَ الَّذِي حَلَّتْ فِيهِ نَجَاسَةٌ)، وعلـم وقوعـهـا فيـه يقيناً، كالمشاهدة، وكذا إذا غلب على ظننا ذلك كما في «السراج الوهاج»، وهـذا فـي غيـر قلـيـل الأرواث لأنه معفو عنه كما سنذكره، (وَكانَ رَاكداً قليلاً)؛ (وَ) ذلك ( القَلِيلُ مَا ) مساحة محله دُونَ عَشْرِ فِي عَشْرِ ) بذراع العامة، والذراع في الأصل اسم للساعد، وهو يذكر ويؤنث، وأنثوه في قولهم: عشراً في عشر، بحذف التاء إيثاراً للتخفيف، فَيَنْجُسُ وإِنْ لَمْ يَظْهَرْ أَثَرُهَا)، أي: النجاسة (فيه)، وأما إذا كان عشراً في عشر، بحوض مربع، أو ستة وثلاثين في مدور، ولا تنحسر أرضه
And overwhelming occurs, in mixing of liquids, by the appearance of one description, like only color or taste, from a liquid that has only two descriptions; and its example is his saying: like milk: it has color and taste. If neither are found, wudu with it is permissible; if one of them is found, it is not permissible. Likewise if the mixed thing has one description, and that description appears, like some watermelon. And his saying: 'and it has no smell' is an additional clarification because it is known from the explanation of two descriptions. And overwhelming is found by the appearance of two descriptions from a liquid that has three descriptions, like vinegar: it has color, taste, and smell. Any two of them appearing prevent the validity of wudu; one does not harm due to its scarcity. And overwhelming in mixing of a liquid that has no description (different from water), like used water (al-musta'mal) which is pure according to the correct view, and rose water with the smell gone, it is by weight, due to the lack of distinction by description because of its absence. For example, if two ratls of used water or rose water with no smell are mixed with one ratl of absolute water, wudu with it is not valid due to the predominance of the restricted; and in the opposite case, if the majority is absolute, wudu is valid. If they are equal, its ruling is not mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah, and they said: its ruling is like that of the overcome, out of precaution, because the discussion has been lengthy. He said: And the fourth type of water: najis water, which is that in which an impurity has fallen, and its occurrence is known with certainty, like by witnessing; likewise if it is our predominant opinion, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. This applies to other than small amounts of animal droppings, because it is pardoned, as we will mention. And it was stagnant and small; and that small is what the area of its place is less than ten by ten cubits by the common cubit. The cubit originally denotes the forearm, and it is masculine and feminine; they feminized it in their statement 'ten by ten' by dropping the ta' to prefer lightening. Then it becomes impure even if its trace, i.e., the impurity, does not appear in it. As for if it is ten by ten, in a square tank, or thirty-six in a round one, and its base does not recede.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof that continues the Sharh on the rules of ghalaba and defines najis water. The author details the rules for ghalaba in three categories of liquids: (1) For liquids with two descriptions (like milk), if one of the two descriptions appears, wudu is invalid; if neither appears, wudu is valid. (2) For liquids with three descriptions (like vinegar), the appearance of any two descriptions invalidates wudu; one description does not. (3) For liquids with no description (like used water or rose water without smell), ghalaba is determined by weight, not by visible descriptions. If the muqayyad water outweighs the mutlaq, wudu is invalid; if mutlaq outweighs, wudu is valid; if equal, the rule is not explicitly stated in Zahir al-Riwayah, but scholars said it follows the rule of the overcome (mughlab) out of precaution. The author then defines the fourth type of water: najis water. It occurs when impurity falls into a small stagnant water body that is less than 10x10 cubits (common cubit). The impurity must be known with certainty or by predominant opinion. Such water becomes najis even if no trace of impurity appears. If the water is 10x10 cubits or more, it does not become najis unless a trace changes. This ruling is based on the principle that large quantities of water are not easily overcome by impurity.

Key Terms
ماء مستعمل (ma' musta'mal): Used water, i.e., water that has been used for wudu or ghusl and is considered pure but not purifying according to some, though the author says it is pure on the correct view.
راكد (rakid): Stagnant, i.e., water that is not flowing. This is a condition for water to become najis from impurity contact.
عشر في عشر ('ashr fi 'ashr): Ten by ten cubits, the minimum dimension for a large water basin that does not become najis without visible change.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a stagnant pool that is 8x8 cubits when a drop of impurity falls into it?
A) The water remains pure because no trace appears.
B) The water becomes najis because it is less than 10x10 cubits.
C) The water remains pure because the impurity is minimal.
D) The water becomes najis only if the impurity changes its taste.

Key Takeaway
Small stagnant water (less than 10x10 cubits) becomes najis immediately upon contact with impurity, regardless of observable changes; liquids with no description are judged by weight, not visible traits.

Water Classification and Rulings in Hanafi Fiqh
Commentary on water types: used, mixed, najis, and doubtful

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five categories of water in Hanafi fiqh and apply the rules of dominance and impurity to determine whether water is suitable for purification.

Core Idea
Small standing water becomes impure even without a trace; mixed water's ruling depends on dominance by attribute or weight.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah classifies water for ritual purification. It clarifies how to assess mixed water—whether by attribute or by weight—and defines when standing water becomes impure. We will walk through the key categories, their conditions, and their practical implications for wudu and daily use.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five water categories
List the five types: absolute (mutlaq), used (musta'mal), mixed with a pure substance, impure (najis), and doubtful (mashkuk). Understand the base ruling for each type.
Use the terms in the passage: mutlaq is tahur, musta'mal is tahir, mixed depends on dominance, najis cannot be used, mashkuk is doubtful in purifying quality.
2
Analyze mixed water: rule of dominance
For a liquid with three attributes (like vinegar), dominance is by appearance of two attributes. For a liquid without attributes (like used water or rosewater), dominance is by weight. Apply: if the mixed substance dominates, the water loses its purifying quality.
Equal quantities: ruling is like the dominated out of precaution (the matn does not specify, but the sharh says it's treated as the dominated).
3
Define impure standing water
Impure (najis) water is that into which impurity has fallen, the water is standing, and its area is less than 10x10 cubits (common cubit). It becomes impure even if no trace of impurity appears.
If the water is 10x10 or larger, it does not become impure unless a trace (taste, color, smell) appears. This is the relied-upon fatwa.
4
Distinguish running water and special cases
Running water becomes impure only if a trace of impurity appears. Also note: water from wells and basins commonly used by people is presumed pure unless certainty of impurity. The scholars of Balkh and Bukhara allowed leniency for large water if depth is considered.
Practical fatwa: do not ask or investigate unless you are certain. This is the basis for the general permissibility of using community water sources.
5
Understand doubtful water
Water from which a donkey or mule (whose mother is a donkey) has drunk is doubtful in its purifying quality (mashkuk), not in its purity. It is considered pure but whether it can be used for wudu is uncertain.
The full discussion is deferred to another chapter (al-usara).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا رائحة له. وبظهورِ وَصَفَيْن من مَائِع له ثلاثة كالخَل. والغلبة في المائع الذي لا وصف له، كالماء المُسْتَعْمَلِ، وماء الورد المنقطع الرائحة، تكون بالوزن: فإن اختلط رطلانِ من الماء المستعمل، برطل مِنَ المطلق، لا يجوز به الوضوء، وبِعَكْسِهِ جَازَ. والرَّابع: ماءٌ نَجِس. وهو الذي حَلَّتْ فِيهِ نَجَاسَةٌ، وَكَانَ رَاكِداً قليلاً، والقليلُ ما دُونَ عَشْرِ في عَشْرِ، فَيَنْجُسُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَظْهَرْ أَثَرُهَا فِيهِ.
(ولا رائحةَ لَهُ زيادة إيضاح لعلمه من بيان الوصفين. (وَ) الغلبة توجد (بظُهُورِ وَصَفَيْنِ مِنْ مَائِع، له) أوصاف (ثَلاثَةٌ)، وذلك ( كالخَلّ)، له لون وطعم وريح، فأي وصفين منهما ظهرا منعا صحـة التوضؤ، والواحد منها لا يضر لقلته، (والغَلَبَةُ في ) مخالطة (المَائِعِ الَّذِي لا وَصْفَ لَهُ) مخالف للماء، وذلك (كالماءِ المُسْتَعْمَل)، فإنه طاهر على الصحيح، وماء الورد المنقطع الرائحة، تـكـون بالوزن)، لعدم التمييز بالوصف لفقده، فإن اختلطَ رِطلانِ)) مثلاً مِنَ المَاءِ المُسْتَعْمَل)، أو ماء الورد المنقطع الرائحة، (برطل من الماء (المُطْلَق، لا يَجُوزُ بِهِ الوُضُوءُ)، لغلبة المقيد، (وبعكسه). وهو لو كان الأكثر المطلق (جَازَ) به الوضوء، وإن استويا لم يذكر حكمه في ظـاهـر الرواية، وقالوا: حكمه حكم المغلوب احتياطاً، لما طال الفصل. قال: (والرابع) من أنواع المياه: (مَاءٌ نَجِسٌ ، وَهُوَ الَّذِي حَلَّتْ فِيهِ نَجَاسَةٌ)، وعلـم وقوعـهـا فيـه يقيناً، كالمشاهدة، وكذا إذا غلب على ظننا ذلك كما في «السراج الوهاج»، وهـذا فـي غيـر قلـيـل الأرواث لأنه معفو عنه كما سنذكره، (وَكانَ رَاكداً قليلاً)؛ (وَ) ذلك ( القَلِيلُ مَا ) مساحة محله دُونَ عَشْرِ فِي عَشْرِ ) بذراع العامة، والذراع في الأصل اسم للساعد، وهو يذكر ويؤنث، وأنثوه في قولهم: عشراً في عشر، بحذف التاء إيثاراً للتخفيف، فَيَنْجُسُ وإِنْ لَمْ يَظْهَرْ أَثَرُهَا)، أي: النجاسة (فيه)، وأما إذا كان عشراً في عشر، بحوض مربع، أو ستة وثلاثين في مدور، ولا تنحسر أرضه بالغرف منه، على الصحيح، وقيل: يقدر عمقه بذراع أو شبر، فلا ينجس إلا بظهور وصف للنجاسة فيه حتى موضع الوقوع. وبه أخذ مشايخ بلخ وبخارى، توسعة على الناس. والتقديـر بـعـشـر في عشر هو المفتى به ولا بأس بالوضوء والشرب من حب يوضع كوزه في نواحي الدار، مـا لـم يعلم تنجسه، ومن حوض يخاف أن يكون فيه قذر ، ولا يتيقن ولا يجب أن يسأل عنه، ومن البئر التي تدلى الدلاء والجرار الدنسة فيها، ويحملها الصغار والإماء، ويمسها الرستاقيون بأيد دنسة، ما لم يتيقن النجاسة. (أو) كان (جَارِيَاً)، عطف على راكد، (وَظَهَرَ فِيهِ)، أي: الجاري (أثَرُهَا) فيـكـون نجساً. (وَالأثَرُ : طَعْمٌ) النجاسة، أوْ لَوْنٌ، أو ريح لها، لوجود عين النجاسة بأثرها. (و) النوع ( الخَامِس) : ( ماءً مَشْكُوكٌ فِي طَهُورِيَّتِهِ)، لا في طهارته، وهُوَ مَا شَربَ مِنْهُ حِمَارٌ، أو بغل) وكانت أمه أتانا لا رمكة؛ لأن العبرة للأم، وسنذكر تتمة الكلام عليه في الأسار إن شاء الله تعالى.
And it has no smell. And by the appearance of two attributes from a liquid that has three, like vinegar. And dominance in a liquid that has no attribute, like used water and rosewater whose smell is gone, is by weight: if two ratls of used water mix with one ratl of absolute water, wudu is not permissible with it, and by its opposite it is permissible. And the fourth: impure water. It is that into which impurity has fallen, and it is standing, small (qalil), and small is what is less than ten by ten cubits, so it becomes impure even if its trace does not appear in it.
(And "no smell" is additional clarification, known from the explanation of the two attributes. And dominance occurs by the appearance of two attributes from a liquid that has three attributes, like vinegar: it has color, taste, and smell. So whichever two attributes appear prevent the validity of wudu, but one does not harm due to its smallness. And dominance in the mixture of a liquid that has no attribute contradictory to water, like used water (which is pure according to the correct view) and rosewater whose smell is gone, is by weight, because there is no distinction by attribute due to its absence. So if two ratls, for example, of used water or rosewater whose smell is gone mix with one ratl of absolute water, wudu is not permissible with it due to the dominance of the restricted (muqayyad) water. And by its opposite: if the majority is absolute water, wudu is permissible with it. And if they are equal, its ruling is not mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah, and they said: its ruling is like the ruling of the dominated, out of precaution, because the chapter is long. He said: (And the fourth) of the types of water: (impure water, and it is that into which impurity has fallen), and its occurrence is known with certainty, like by sight, and likewise if it is our predominant opinion, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And this applies to other than small amounts of animal dung, because it is excused as we will mention. (And it was standing, small); and that small (is what) the area of its place is (less than ten by ten cubits) by the common cubit. The cubit originally is the name for the forearm, and it is masculine and feminine, and they made it feminine in their saying: ten ('ashran) in ten, by omitting the ta (tā') for ease of pronunciation. So it becomes impure even if its trace does not appear in it, meaning the impurity. As for if it is ten by ten, in a square basin, or thirty-six in a circular one, and its ground is not uncovered by scooping from it, according to the correct view. And it was said: its depth is estimated by a cubit or a span, so it does not become impure except by the appearance of a trace of impurity in it, even at the place of occurrence. And the scholars of Balkh and Bukhara adopted this to make things easy for the people. And the estimation by ten by ten is the relied-upon fatwa. And there is no harm in performing wudu and drinking from a jar whose water-skin is placed in the corners of the house, as long as one does not know it is impure; and from a basin that one fears may contain filth, but one is not certain and one is not obligated to ask about it; and from a well into which impure buckets and jars are lowered, and which children and slave girls carry, and which villagers touch with impure hands, as long as one is not certain of impurity. (Or) it was (running), a conjunction to standing (and its trace appeared in it), meaning the running water, so it is impure. (And the trace: taste) of impurity, or color, or smell, due to the existence of the substance of impurity by its trace. (And) the (fifth) type: (water doubted in its purifying quality), not in its purity, and it is water from which a donkey or a mule has drunk, and its mother was a female donkey (atan) not a mare (ramaka), because consideration is given to the mother. And we will mention the remainder of the discussion on it in the section on prisoners (al-usara), God willing.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) from Imdad al-Fattah on Maraqi al-Falah, explaining the categories of water in Hanafi fiqh. The author clarifies how to determine when a pure liquid like vinegar or used water dominates by weight, and specifies the ruling for small standing water (less than 10x10 cubits) — it becomes impure even without visible trace. He also discusses the practical fatwa of the later scholars (mutakhkhirin) allowing leniency about wells and basins unless impurity is certain. Finally, he introduces the fifth type: water from which a donkey or mule has drunk, which is doubtful in its purifying ability only, not its purity. The passage emphasizes that in daily life, one should not assume impurity without certainty.

Key Terms
مطلق (mutlaq): Absolute water, which is pure and purifying (tahur) and has no added attribute.
مستعمل (musta'mal): Used water, which has been used in a minor ritual purification; it is tahir (pure) but not tahur (purifying) by the correct view.
قليل (qalil): Small quantity of water, defined as less than 10x10 cubits area (for standing water).
نجس (najis): Impure water, which cannot be used for purification and must be avoided.
طهور (tahur): Purifying water, meaning it is both pure and can be used for ritual purification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does standing water become najis (impure) without the appearance of any trace of impurity?
A) When it is less than 10x10 cubits and a known impurity falls into it.
B) When it is more than 10x10 cubits and a known impurity falls into it.
C) Only when the taste, color, or smell changes.
D) When it is running water and a known impurity falls into it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of water is based on its source (mutlaq), use, mixture, and impurity, with quantity and dominance as key factors determining suitability for purification.

The Fifth Type of Water and Impure Traces in Flowing Water
Classifies water types with rulings based on impurity traces and animal consumption.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on the fifth type of water (water drunk by donkey/mule) and explain the conditions under which flowing water becomes impure due to traces.

Core Idea
Water doubted in purificatory power is pure but not certainly purifying; traces of impurity make water impure.

In this passage, the author continues the classification of water types from Nur al-Idah. He first clarifies that flowing water becomes impure if a trace (taste, color, smell) of impurity appears. Then he introduces the fifth type: water drunk by a donkey or mule, which is pure in itself but its ability to purify other things is doubtful. The passage provides practical concessions for daily use, based on the principle of certainty not being removed by doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Locate in the passage the ruling on flowing water when a trace of impurity appears, and the ruling on water drunk by a donkey or mule (the fifth type). Note the distinction between impurity (najis) and doubtful purificatory power.
The trace is taste, color, or smell.
2
Determine the legal basis for each ruling
For flowing water, the basis is the presence of the substance of impurity (ayn al-najis). For the fifth type, the basis is doubt about the animal's mother: if the mother is a donkey, the water's tahuriyyah is doubtful; if a mare, it is fully purificatory.
The mother's species is decisive.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle of certainty vs doubt
The passage applies the principle 'certainty is not removed by doubt' (al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk). Therefore, water remains pure unless impurity is certain. This leads to concessions for wells and basins in daily use.
One does not need to ask about potential impurities.
4
Note the mufta bihi position and differences
The estimation of ten by ten cubits for a pool is the fatwa-worthy position. The view of the scholars of Balkh and Bukhara is taken for ease, emphasizing that water remains pure until a trace is certain.
This is based on istihsan (juristic preference).

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the classification of water types from the matn. It discusses two points: the ruling on flowing water when traces of impurity appear, and the fifth type of water. The author, commenting on the matn, explains that flowing water is impure if taste, color, or smell of impurity is detected. This is because the substance of impurity is present with its trace. The fifth type is water drunk by a donkey or mule, but only if the mother is a donkey (atan); if the mother is a mare (ramakah), the water is pure because mules from horses are considered different. This water is doubted in its tahuriyyah (purificatory power), not in its own purity—meaning it is pure itself but its ability to purify other things is uncertain. The author also notes practical concessions regarding wells and basins in daily use, stating that as long as impurity is not certain, the water remains pure, and one does not need to ask about potential impurities. This is based on the principle of 'certainty is not removed by doubt' and ease for the people.

The First Category of Su'r: Human and Horse
Ruling on the first category of su'r with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the su'r of a human and a horse, and identify the conditions that change its purity status.

Core Idea
The leftover water from a human or horse is pure and purificatory by consensus, with limited exceptions.

This lesson begins the chapter on su'r, focusing on the first of four categories. The su'r (leftover water) of a human and a horse is ruled pure and purificatory by default. However, certain conditions, such as contamination of the mouth, can affect this ruling. Understanding these nuances is essential for correct practice in wudu and purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The su'r (leftover water) after a human or horse drinks. The ruling: it is pure (tahir) and purificatory (mutahhir) by consensus.
This is the default ruling for the first category.
2
Locate the dalil
What proofs are cited? Two hadith: the Prophet drinking after a Bedouin, and after Aishah while menstruating. Also, the Prophet housing disbelievers in the mosque.
The hadith show the Prophet's action, which indicates permissibility and purity.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the dalil prove the ruling? The Prophet's drinking from the same vessel indicates that the leftover water is pure. His statement 'the rightmost' shows no concern for impurity. The housing of disbelievers implies their bodies are not impure.
The proof is strong (qati' dalala) even though the hadith are ahad (zanni thubut).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there a dispute? Yes, within the Hanafi school: if a human has an impure mouth and drinks after managing saliva, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say the su'r is pure but makruh; Muhammad says it is impure.
The dispute hinges on whether saliva can purify impurity.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
Which position is relied upon? The view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (pure but makruh) is the mufta bihi. For horse su'r, the correct opinion is that it is pure and purificatory.
The author states 'at the correct opinion' for horse, indicating the preferred view.

Chapter on clarifying the rulings of su'r. And a small amount of water, if an animal drinks from it, it is of four categories, and it is called su'r. The first: pure and purificatory, and it is: that from which a human or horse drinks. Chapter on clarifying the rulings of su'r and the small amount of water, which is less than ten by ten and not flowing, if an animal drinks from it, it is of one of four categories, and what it leaves behind is called su'r, with a hamzah in its 'ayn, and the noun is used metaphorically for the remainder of food, and the plural is as'ar, and the verb is as'ara, meaning he left something from what he drank, and the adjective from it is sa'ar, irregularly, because its regular form would be mus'ir, and its parallel is ajbarahu fahuwa jabbar. The first of the categories: su'r that is pure and purificatory by consensus, without aversion, and it is that from which a human drinks who has no impurity in his mouth, because of what Malik narrated from the chain of al-Zuhri from Anas ibn Malik that the Messenger of Allah peace be upon him was brought milk mixed with water, and on his right was a Bedouin, and on his left was Abu Bakr, so he drank then gave it to the Bedouin and said: 'The rightmost, the rightmost.' And Muslim narrated from Aishah, she said: 'I used to drink while menstruating, then I would give it to the Prophet peace be upon him, and he would place his mouth on the spot where I had placed my mouth.' And because the peace be upon him housed the delegation of Thaqif while they were disbelievers in the mosque, so the impurity of the disbeliever is in his belief, so it does not affect the impurity of his limbs. So there is no difference between whether he is Muslim or polytheist, young or old, male or female, pure or junub, or menstruating or postpartum. However, if his mouth is contaminated with impurity, such as wine, carrion, or other, and he drinks water or similar immediately, then his su'r becomes impure. And if he drinks after the saliva circulated in his mouth and he spat it out or swallowed it before drinking, then his su'r is not impure according to Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf, but it is disliked, due to Muhammad's saying that impurity is not purified by saliva according to him. Or horse, for its su'r is pure by consensus according to the correct opinion, and we guarded by it against narrations of aversion and impurity like its urine and doubt in its su'r about...
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on the rulings of su'r (leftover water). The author defines su'r as the water left after an animal drinks, and clarifies the pronunciation. The first category is the su'r of a human and a horse. The su'r of a human is pure and purificatory by consensus, regardless of the person's state—Muslim or non-Muslim, young or old, male or female, in a state of purity or janabah, menstruation or postpartum. The author provides proof from hadith: the Prophet drank from the same vessel as a Bedouin, and Aishah reported that the Prophet would drink from the spot where she had drunk while menstruating. Also, the Prophet housed disbelievers in the mosque, implying their bodies are not impure. The only exception is if the person's mouth is contaminated with an actual impurity (like wine or carrion) and they drink immediately; then the su'r becomes impure. If they swallow or spit out their saliva first, there is a dispute: Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf consider the su'r pure but makruh, while Muhammad considers it impure because saliva cannot purify impurity. For a horse, the su'r is pure and purificatory by consensus, unlike other animals like donkeys or mules which will be discussed later.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): The leftover water after an animal drinks from it, or metaphorically the remainder of food.
بالاتفاق (bi-al-ittifaq): By consensus, meaning all scholars agree on the ruling.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked, but not sinful; a category between halal and haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the su'r of a horse according to the correct Hanafi position?
A) It is impure (najis) because horses eat impurities.
B) It is pure and purificatory (tahir mutahhir), with consensus.
C) It is pure but not purificatory.
D) It is purified only if the horse is a mare.

Key Takeaway
The su'r of a human and horse is pure and purificatory by default, with the exception of immediate drinking after mouth contamination, which requires caution.

The First Category of Su'r: Pure and Purifying (Human and Horse)
Defines the first category of su'r and provides proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the su'r of a human and a horse, identify the conditions that affect its purity, and explain the Hanafi proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
The su'r of a human and a horse is pure and purifying, even if the person is in a state of ritual impurity.

In this lesson, we explore the first of the four categories of su'r (leftover water). The Hanafi school holds that the leftover water of a human and a horse is pure and can be used for purification. We will examine the evidence from the Sunnah and the conditions that may affect this ruling, such as the presence of impurity in the mouth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is drinking from little water by a human or horse, and the left over (su'r) is ruled pure and purifying (tahir mutahhir).
The text states 'first: pure and purifying by agreement'.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proofs cited: the hadith of Anas (milk drinking) and the hadith of Aisha (menstruation).
Both are ahad hadith but accepted by the Hanafis.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Determine how each hadith indicates purity: the Prophet drank after the Bedouin and placed his mouth where Aisha had drunk, showing no concern for ritual impurity.
The act of the Prophet is evidence of permissibility and purity.
4

Observe the disagreement when the drinker's mouth is contaminated with visible impurity: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say the su'r is not impure but makruh, while Muhammad says it is impure.
The mufta bihi is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that su'r of a human is pure, but if the mouth has impurity, it is makruh (disliked) but not impure. The su'r of a horse is pure by consensus on the correct view.
The text explicitly says 'the correct view' for the horse.

(وَ) القسم (الثاني): سؤر (نجس) نجاسة غليظة)، وقيل: خفيفة ( لا يَجُوزُ استِعمالُهُ)، أي: لا يصح التطهير بـه بحـال، ولا يحــل شــربـه إلا حال الاضطرار كالميتة) ، (وَهُوَ) أي: السؤر النجس، ما شَربَ منهُ الكَلْبُ) سواء كان كلب صيد، أو ماشية أو غيرهما، أوِ الخِنْزِيرُ)، أما نجاسة الخنزير فبالنص، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِنَّهُ رِجْسٌ الان : ١٤٥] وأما نجاسة الكلب فبدلالة قوله : ( طُهُورُ إِنَاءِ أَحَدِكُمْ إِذَا وَلَغَ فِيهِ الْكَلْبُ أَنْ يَغْسِلَهُ سَبْعَ مَرَاتِ » (). وهو يفيد النجاسة، لأن الطهور مصدر بمعنى الطهارة، فيستدعي سابقة التنجس، لكن السبع تعبد واستحباب، لما روى الدارقطني عن أبي هريرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: ( في الكَلْبِ يَلعُ في الإِنَاءِ، أَنَّهُ يُغْسَلُ ثَلاثَاً أَوْ خَمْسَاً أَوْ سَبْعَاً ، فلو كان السبع واجباً لمـا خـيـره. (أو شَيء) بمعنى: حيوان ( منْ سِبَاعِ البهائِمِ احترز به عن سباع الطيور، وسيأتي حكمها. والسبع: حيوان مختطف منتهب عاد عادة، (كَالفَهْدِ، والذئب والضبع والنمر والسبع والقرد، لما روي أن عمر وعمرو بن العاص ، وردا حوضاً فقال عمرو بن العاص : ( يَا صَاحِبَ الْحَوْضِ، أَتَرِدُ السَّبَاعُ مَاءَكُم هذا؟ فَقَالَ
Chapter on the rulings of su'r. And little water, if an animal drinks from it, it is of four categories, and it is called su'r. The first: pure and purifying, and it is what a human drank from, or a horse. He said: Little water, which is less than ten cubits by ten cubits and not flowing, if an animal drinks from it, it is of one of four categories, and what remains is called su'r (with hamza on the 'ayn). The name is also borrowed for the remainder of food. The plural is asar, the verb as'ara, meaning he left something from what he drank. The adjective is sa'ar on an irregular pattern because the regular pattern would be mus'ir; its analogy is jabbar from ajbarahu. The first category: su'r that is pure and purifying by agreement, without dislike, and it is what a human drank from whose mouth has no impurity, due to the hadith reported by Malik from az-Zuhri from Anas ibn Malik that the Prophet was brought milk mixed with water, and on his right was a Bedouin and on his left Abu Bakr; he drank then gave to the Bedouin and said: the rightmost, then the rightmost. And Muslim narrated from Aisha: 'I used to drink while menstruating, then I would give the vessel to the Prophet, and he would place his mouth where I had placed it.' And because the Prophet lodged the delegation of Thaqif, who were disbelievers, in the mosque; the impurity of the disbeliever is in his belief, so it does not affect the impurity of his body parts. So there is no difference between whether he is Muslim or polytheist, young or old, male or female, pure or junub, menstruating or postpartum. As for if his mouth is polluted with impurity, like wine, carrion, or other, then he drinks water or similar from the same, then his su'r becomes impure. But if he drinks after saliva has circulated in his mouth, and he spat it out or swallowed it before drinking, then his su'r is not impure according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but it is disliked, because Muhammad holds that impurity does not become pure by saliva. Or a horse: its su'r is pure by agreement on the correct view, and we guard by this against reports of dislike and impurity like its urine and doubt about its su'r. Or what is eaten for its meat. And the second: impure, not permissible to use, and it is what a dog, pig, or something from beasts of prey drank: like leopard, wolf... Imam Muhammad: his view that its meat is disliked is due to respect not impurity, like a human, because the apparent narration is that its su'r is pure like its meat, and that is the narration of Abu Yusuf from the Imam, and it is the correct view, and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad both hold it as a single narration. Or what is eaten for its meat, like camels, cows, and sheep: their su'r is pure because it is generated from their meat, and there is no dislike in it if they are not jalalah, meaning those that eat filth. The original: Fath occurs here. As for the jalalah, its su'r is of the third category, disliked, as we will mention. And the second category: su'r that is impure (severe impurity, it is said: light) not permissible to use, meaning purification with it is invalid in any case, and drinking it is not permissible except in necessity like carrion. And it is the su'r of a dog, whether hunting dog, sheepdog, or other, or a pig. As for the impurity of the pig, it is by text: He said: 'Indeed it is filth.' As for the impurity of the dog, it is indicated by the hadith: 'The purification of one's vessel when a dog drinks from it is to wash it seven times.' And this indicates impurity because tuhur is a verbal noun meaning purification, so it presupposes prior impurity. But the seven times are devotional and recommended, because ad-Daraqutni narrated from Abu Huraira from the Prophet: 'Regarding the dog drinking in the vessel, it is washed three, five, or seven times.' If seven were obligatory, he would not have given a choice. Or something (meaning animal) from beasts of prey (to exclude birds of prey, whose ruling will come). The sabu' is an animal that habitually snatches and seizes. Like leopard, wolf, hyena, tiger, sabu', and monkey, because it is narrated that Umar and Amr ibn al-As came to a pond, and Amr said: 'O owner of the pond, do the beasts come to this water?' He said...
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is a commentary expanding on the matn of Nur al-Idah, and it covers the rulings of su'r (leftover water or liquid after a person or animal drinks). The author begins by defining little water (qalil), which is water less than ten cubits by ten cubits and not flowing. The leftover after an animal drinks from such water is called su'r. The su'r is classified into four categories; this passage discusses the first two in detail.

The first category is su'r that is pure and purifying (tahir mutahhir) by consensus, without dislike (karaha). This applies to the leftover of a human, regardless of whether the human is Muslim or non-Muslim, young or old, male or female, in a state of purity, janabah, menstruation, or postpartum. The only condition is that the person's mouth is free from visible impurity (like wine, carrion). The proof includes the hadith where the Prophet drank milk and then gave the leftover to the Bedouin on his right, and the hadith of Aisha where she would drink while menstruating and then give the cup to the Prophet, who placed his mouth where she had placed hers. Also, the Prophet lodged polytheists from Thaqif in the mosque, indicating that their bodies are not considered impure by contact. If the mouth is contaminated with impurity, the su'r becomes impure. There is a difference of opinion among the Hanafi imams: if a person has impurity in his mouth, then swallows or spits out saliva before drinking, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say the su'r is not impure but is disliked (makruh), while Muhammad considers it impure because saliva does not purify impurity. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that it is pure but disliked if from a person with impurity in the mouth. The su'r of a horse is pure by agreement on the correct view, though there are weak narrations of dislike or impurity. Also, the su'r of animals whose meat is eaten (e.g., camel, cow, sheep) is pure, provided they are not jalalah (animals that eat feces). If they are jalalah, the su'r falls into the third category (makruh).

The second category is su'r that is impure (najis) and not permissible to use for purification, except in cases of extreme necessity. This includes the leftover of a dog—whether trained, herding, or otherwise—and a pig. The impurity of the pig is established by the Quranic verse 'Indeed it is filth' (rijs). For the dog, the proof is the hadith requiring washing a vessel seven times if a dog drinks from it. The Hanafis interpret the seven times as recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory, because a narration from al-Daraqutni gives a choice of three, five, or seven washes. The impurity of dogs and pigs is considered severe (najis ghaliz). Additionally, the su'r of beasts of prey (siba' al-baha'im) such as leopards, wolves, hyenas, tigers, and monkeys is impure. The term 'beast' (sabu') refers to an animal that habitually snatches and attacks. Birds of prey are excluded and will be treated separately; their su'r is pure. This ruling is based on a narration of Umar and Amr ibn al-As about beasts drinking from a water source.

Key Terms
سُؤْر (su'r): The leftover water or liquid in a vessel after a person or animal has drunk from it.
جَلَّالَة (jalalah): An animal that eats feces (jalla) predominantly, making its meat disliked and its su'r of the third category (makruh).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the su'r of a horse?
A) It is impure (najis).
B) It is pure and purifying (tahir mutahhir).
C) It is pure but disliked (makruh).
D) It is impure unless the horse is a mare.

Key Takeaway
The su'r of a human (without visible mouth impurity) and a horse is pure and purifying, and the Prophet's practice confirms it.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
The Second Category of Su'r: Impure (Dog, Pig, Beasts of Prey)
Defines the second category of su'r and provides proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the su'r of a dog, pig, and beasts of prey, and explain the Hanafi proof from the hadith of the dog's vessel.

Core Idea
The su'r of a dog, pig, and beasts of prey is impure and cannot be used for purification except in dire necessity.

In this lesson, we examine the second category of su'r: that which is impure (najis). The Hanafi school classifies the leftover water of dogs, pigs, and beasts of prey as impure, based on clear textual evidence. We will analyze the proof from the hadith requiring washing the vessel seven times and the Quranic verse for the pig.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animals and the ruling
Recognize that the su'r of a dog (any type), a pig, and any beast of prey (sibaa') is ruled impure (najis) and cannot be used for purification.
Beasts of prey include leopard, wolf, hyena, tiger, monkey, etc. Birds of prey are excluded.
2
Locate the dalil for each
For the pig: Quranic text 'Indeed it is filth' (rijs). For the dog: the hadith 'The purification of one's vessel when a dog drinks from it is to wash it seven times.' For beasts of prey: the narration of Umar and Amr indicating the beasts drink from water, implying impurity.
The dog hadith is ahad but accepted. The beast narration is a practice of the Companions.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For the dog: the command to wash the vessel presupposes impurity because purification (tuhur) is only needed after defilement. The optionality of three, five, or seven washes (from another narration) shows the seven are not wajib but recommended, but the impurity remains.
The Hanafis do not consider the seven washes obligatory, but the impurity is established.
4
Note the scope of the ruling
The impurity applies to all dogs (hunting, herding, etc.) and all beasts of prey. The su'r is impure and cannot be used for wudu or ghusl, except in cases of extreme necessity (like carrion).
The text specifies 'severe impurity' (najis ghaliz) for these.
5
Understand the cross-madhhab difference
While the Hanafis consider the su'r of beasts of prey impure, the Shafi'is consider the su'r of all animals impure except humans and cats. The Malikis consider the su'r of dogs and pigs impure but beasts of prey pure. This difference stems from different usul interpretations.
The Hanafi proof for beasts relies on the practice of Umar and Amr.

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is a commentary expanding on the matn of Nur al-Idah, and it covers the rulings of su'r (leftover water or liquid after a person or animal drinks). The author begins by defining little water (qalil), which is water less than ten cubits by ten cubits and not flowing. The leftover after an animal drinks from such water is called su'r. The only condition is that the person's mouth is free from visible impurity (like wine, carrion). The proof includes the hadith where the Prophet drank milk and then gave the leftover to the Bedouin on his right, and the hadith of Aisha where she would drink while menstruating and then give the cup to the Prophet, who placed his mouth where she had placed hers. Also, the su'r of animals whose meat is eaten (e.g., camel, cow, sheep) is pure, provided they are not jalalah (animals that eat feces). If they are jalalah, the su'r falls into the third category (makruh).

The second category is su'r that is impure (najis) and not permissible to use for purification, except in cases of extreme necessity. This includes the leftover of a dog—whether trained, herding, or otherwise—and a pig. The impurity of the pig is established by the Quranic verse 'Indeed it is filth' (rijs). For the dog, the proof is the hadith requiring washing a vessel seven times if a dog drinks from it. The Hanafis interpret the seven times as recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory, because a narration from al-Daraqutni gives a choice of three, five, or seven washes. The impurity of dogs and pigs is considered severe (najis ghaliz). Additionally, the su'r of beasts of prey (siba' al-baha'im) such as leopards, wolves, hyenas, tigers, and monkeys is impure. The term 'beast' (sabu') refers to an animal that habitually snatches and attacks. Birds of prey are excluded and will be treated separately; their su'r is pure. This ruling is based on a narration of Umar and Amr ibn al-As about beasts drinking from a water source.

Key Terms
سِبَاع (sibaa'): Beasts of prey that habitually attack and snatch; includes leopard, wolf, hyena, tiger, monkey, etc. Excludes birds of prey.
رِجْس (rijs): Filth, impurity; used in the Quran for the pig.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the evidence for the impurity of the dog's su'r?
A) A Quranic verse.
B) The hadith that the vessel must be washed seven times.
C) The narration of Umar and Amr.
D) Consensus (ijma).

Key Takeaway
The su'r of dogs, pigs, and beasts of prey is impure, and the Hanafi school relies on strong textual evidence (Quran, hadith, and Companion practice).

The Impure Su'r of Dogs, Pigs, and Beasts of Prey
Defining the second category of su'r as impure with textual proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the su'r of dogs, pigs, and beasts of prey and cite the primary textual evidence for each.

Core Idea
The su'r of dogs, pigs, and beasts of prey is impure, proven by Quranic text, hadith indication, and companion practice.

In this lesson, we examine the second category of su'r (leftover water) – that which is impure and cannot be used for purification. The author presents a clear taxonomy: the pig's impurity is established by the Quran itself, the dog's by a hadith that implies prior contamination, and beasts of prey by a narration from the Companions. Understanding these proofs is essential for correctly applying rulings of purity in daily worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the second category and its scope
Locate the defining statement: 'the second [category]: impure, its use is not permissible, and it is what a dog, or a pig, or something from the beasts of prey drank from.' This tells you the animals covered.
Note that 'beasts of prey' includes examples like leopard, wolf, hyena, tiger, lion, and monkey.
2
Find the proof for the pig
The text says 'as for the impurity of the pig, it is by the text, and it is His statement: Indeed it is an abomination (Al-An'am 6:145).' Identify this as a direct Quranic proof (nass).
3
Analyze the proof for the dog
The hadith 'The purification of the vessel…' indicates impurity because the word 'tahur' (purification) presupposes that the vessel became impure. The number seven is not obligatory, as shown by the alternate narration allowing three, five, or seven washes.
This is a dalalah (indication) proof, not a direct text.
4
Understand the proof for beasts of prey
The narration about Umar and Amr ibn al-As shows that the Companions considered water visited by beasts of prey as disliked to use, implying impurity. The underlying reason (ta'lil) is that these animals themselves are filthy, so their saliva is also impure.
This is an example of istidlal bi al-athar (inference from companion practice).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني: نَجِس لا يَجُوزُ استعماله، وهُوَ ما شَربَ منهُ الكَلْبُ، أو الخِنْزِيرُ، أَوْ شَيء من سبَاعِ البهائِمِ: كَالفَهْدِ، والذئب... أَمَّا نَجَاسَةُ الخِنْزِيرِ فَبِالنَّصِّ، وَهُوَ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: ﴿فَإِنَّهُ رِجْسٌ﴾ [الأنعام: 145]، وأَمَّا نَجَاسَةُ الكَلْبِ فَبِدَلَالَةِ قَوْلِهِ: «طُهُورُ إِنَاءِ أَحَدِكُمْ إِذَا وَلَغَ فِيهِ الْكَلْبُ أَنْ يَغْسِلَهُ سَبْعَ مَرَاتٍ» وَهُوَ يُفِيدُ النَّجَاسَةَ، لِأَنَّ الطَّهُورَ مَصْدَرٌ بِمَعْنَى الطَّهَارَةِ، فَيَسْتَدْعِي سَابِقَةَ التَّنَجُّسِ، لَكِنَّ السَّبْعَ تَعَبُّدٌ وَاسْتِحْبَابٌ، لِمَا رَوَى الدَّارَقُطْنِيُّ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «فِي الكَلْبِ يَلَغُ فِي الإِنَاءِ، أَنَّهُ يُغْسَلُ ثَلَاثاً أَوْ خَمْساً أَوْ سَبْعاً» فَلَوْ كَانَ السَّبْعُ وَاجِباً لَمَا خَيَّرَهُ. (أَوْ شَيْءٌ) بِمَعْنَى: حَيَوَانٌ (مِنْ سِبَاعِ البَهَائِمِ) احْتِرَازٌ بِهِ عَنْ سِبَاعِ الطَّيْرِ، وَسَيَأْتِي حُكْمُهَا. وَالسَّبُعُ: حَيَوَانٌ مُخْتَطِفٌ مُنْتَهِبٌ عَادَ عَادَةً، (كَالفَهْدِ، والذِّئْبِ، والضَّبُعِ، والنَّمِرِ، والسَّبُعِ، والقِرْدِ) لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ عُمَرَ وَعَمْرَو بْنَ العَاصِ وَرَدَا حَوْضاً فَقَالَ عَمْرُو بْنُ العَاصِ: يَا صَاحِبَ الحَوْضِ، أَتَرِدُ السِّبَاعُ مَاءَكُمْ هَذَا؟ فَقَالَ: يَا صَاحِبَ الحَوْضِ لا تُخْبِرْنَا، فَلَوْلَا أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَتَعَذَّرُ عَلَيْهِمُ اسْتِعْمَالُ مَاءِ الحَوْضِ بِإِخْبَارِهِ بِالوُرُودِ لَمَا نَهَاهُ عَنْ ذَلِكَ، وَالمَعْنَى فِيهِ: أَنَّ عَيْنَ هَذِهِ الحَيَوَانَاتِ مُسْتَخْبَثٌ غَيْرُ طَيِّبٍ فَسُؤْرُهَا كَذَلِكَ، لِأَنَّهُ كَلَبَنِهَا، يَنْحَلِبُ مِنْ عَيْنِهَا.
And the second [category]: impure, its use is not permissible, and it is what a dog, or a pig, or something from the beasts of prey like the leopard, the wolf... drank from. As for the impurity of the pig, it is by the text, and it is His statement: 'Indeed it is an abomination.' [Al-An'am 6:145]. As for the impurity of the dog, it is by the indication of his statement: 'The purification of the vessel of one of you when a dog laps from it is to wash it seven times.' This indicates impurity because 'tahur' is a verbal noun meaning purification, so it presupposes prior contamination. However, the seven [times] is devotional and recommended, because al-Daraqutni narrated from Abu Huraira from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Concerning the dog lapping in the vessel, that it is washed three, or five, or seven times.' If seven were obligatory, he would not have given him a choice. [Or] 'something' meaning an animal 'from the beasts of prey' – a precaution to exclude birds of prey, and its ruling will come. 'Sabu' is an animal that snatches and plunders habitually, 'like the leopard, the wolf, the hyena, the tiger, the lion, and the monkey' because it is narrated that Umar and Amr ibn al-As came to a pond, and Amr ibn al-As said: 'O owner of the pond, do beasts of prey visit your water this?' He said: 'O owner of the pond, do not tell us.' If it were not that using the water would be difficult for them by his informing them of the visitation, he would not have forbidden him from that. And the meaning of it is that the substance of these animals is considered filthy and not good, so their leftover water is likewise, because it is like their milk, derived from their substance.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage defines the second category of su'r (leftover water/drink) as impure (najis) and impermissible to use. The commentator explains that this includes water drunk by dogs, pigs, and any beast of prey (siba' al-baha'im) such as leopards, wolves, hyenas, tigers, lions, and monkeys. The impurity of the pig is established by the Quranic verse 'Indeed it is an abomination.' For the dog, the proof is the hadith that a vessel lapped by a dog must be washed seven times. The commentator notes that the word 'tahur' (purification) implies prior contamination, so the hadith indicates impurity. However, the number seven is recommended, not obligatory, based on another hadith allowing three, five, or seven washes. For beasts of prey, the proof is a narration about Umar and Amr ibn al-As, where the owner of a pond was told not to inform them of animals visiting, implying the water would be considered impure if known. The underlying reason is that these animals themselves are considered filthy, so their saliva and leftover water are also impure, analogized to their milk which comes from their impure substance.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): The leftover water or drink in a vessel after an animal has drunk from it.
سباع البهائم (siba' al-baha'im): Predatory beasts of prey among land animals, such as lions, wolves, leopards, etc.
نجاسة غليظة (najasah ghaleezah): Severe impurity, about which there is consensus on its filth, e.g., urine, blood, feces, and su'r of dogs and pigs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The su'r of dogs, pigs, and beasts of prey is impure, with each animal proven by a different type of evidence: Quranic text, hadith indication, and companion practice.
