The Ruling on the Su'r of Cats, Free-Range Chickens, and Birds of Prey
Explaining the third category of su'r that is disliked (makruh) to use when other water is available.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the su'r of domestic cats, free-range chickens, and birds of prey, and explain why each is considered pure but disliked (makruh tanzih).

Core Idea
Cat su'r is pure by hadith but disliked; chicken and bird of prey su'r are pure by istihsan but disliked when contamination is likely.

In this passage, we learn that not all su'r (residual water left after an animal drinks) are treated the same. The Hanafi school classifies the su'r of domestic cats, free-range chickens, and birds of prey as pure in substance yet disliked to use when other water is available. This balance between purity and caution arises from the animals' habits and the strength of the evidence. Let us examine the proof for each.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three animals and their common ruling
The passage states that the su'r of domestic cats, free-range chickens, and birds of prey is makruh tanzihan (disliked but not sinful) to use when other water exists. Note that the underlying su'r is pure (not najis).
Makruh tanzih means avoidance is recommended, not obligatory.
2
Trace the proof for the cat's su'r
The hadith 'It is not impure; it is among those who go around you' establishes purity. However, dislike (karahah) arises because cats do not avoid impurities, similar to a child dipping their hand in water.
The hadith is hasan sahih according to Tirmidhi.
3
Distinguish between domestic and wild cat
The domestic cat benefits from the 'cause of circumambulation' (ta'weef) mentioned in the hadith; the wild cat does not, so its su'r is impure.
The wild cat lacks the habitation-based connection that the hadith addresses.
4
Examine the ruling for free-range chicken
A free-range chicken (mukhallah) roams in filth, so its beak may be contaminated. Since purity is uncertain, the su'r is disliked to use. If the chicken is confined and its beak never reaches filth, no dislike.
The ruling hinges on the likelihood of impurity contacting the beak.
5
Analyze the ruling for birds of prey and the role of istihsan
Strict analogy (qiyas) with beasts of prey would make their su'r impure due to haram meat. However, istihsan (juristic preference) rules it pure because birds drink with their beak (pure bone) rather than a tongue wetted with impure saliva. Dislike applies only when contamination is certain.
Istihsan overrides qiyas here due to a subtle difference in the cause of impurity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثَّالِثُ مَكَرُوهُ اسْتِعْمَالُهُ مَعَ وُجُودِ غَيْرِهِ وَهُوَ سُؤْرُ الهِرَّةِ الأَهْلِيَّةِ؛ لِسُقُوطِ حُكْمِ النَّجَاسَةِ اتِّفَاقاً؛ بِعِلَّةِ الطَّوَافِ المَنْصُوصِ عَلَيْهِ بِقَوْلِهِ: إِنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ بِنَجَسَةٍ، إِنَّهَا مِنَ الطَّوَّافِينَ عَلَيْكُمْ وَالطَّوَّافَاتِ. قَالَ التِّرْمِذِيُّ: حَدِيثٌ حَسَنٌ صَحِيحٌ. وَأَمَّا كَرَاهَةُ سُؤْرِهَا كَرَاهَةَ تَنْزِيهٍ عَلَى الأَصَحِّ؛ فَلِأَنَّهَا لَا تَتَحَامَى النَّجَاسَةَ، كَمَاءِ غَمْسِ صَغِيرٍ يَدَهُ فِيهِ. وَالهِرَّةُ البَرِّيَّةُ سُؤْرُهَا نَجِسٌ لِفَقْدِ عِلَّةِ الطَّوَافِ فِيهَا. (وَ) سُؤْرُ (الدَّجَاجَةِ المُخْلَاةِ) وَهِيَ الَّتِي تَجُولُ فِي القَاذُورَاتِ، لِتَلْتَقِطَ الحَبَّ، وَلَكِنْ لَمْ يُعْلَمْ طَهارَةُ مِنْقَارِهَا مِنْ نَجَاسَتِهِ، فَلِذَا لَمْ يُحْكَمْ بِنَجَاسَةِ سُؤْرِهَا بِالشَّكِّ فَيُكْرَهُ. فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ كَذَلِكَ، فَلَا كَرَاهَةَ فِي سُؤْرِهَا، كَالَّتِي حُبِسَتْ وَلا يَصِلُ مِنْقَارُهَا إِلَى قَذَرٍ. (وَ) سُؤْرُ (سِبَاعِ الطَّيْرِ) وَكَرَاهَةُ سُؤْرِهَا، لِأَنَّهَا تُخَالِطُ المَيْتَاتِ وَالنَّجَاسَاتِ فَأَشْبَهَتِ الدَّجَاجَةَ المُخْلَاةَ، حَتَّى لَوْ تَيَقَّنَ أَنَّهُ لَا نَجَاسَةَ عَلَى مِنْقَارِهَا، لَا يُكْرَهُ. وَكَانَ القِيَاسُ نَجَاسَةَ سُؤْرِهَا كَسِبَاعِ البَهَائِمِ بِجَامِعِ حُرْمَةِ لَحْمِهَا، وَلَكِنْ طَهَارَتُهُ اسْتِحْسَاناً؛ لِأَنَّهَا تَشْرَبُ بِمِنْقَارِهَا، وَهُوَ عَظْمٌ طَاهِرٌ، وَسِبَاعُ البَهَائِمِ تَشْرَبُ بِلِسَانِهَا، وَهُوَ مُبْتَلٌ بِلُعَابِهَا المُتَوَلِّدِ مِنْ لَحْمِهَا، وَهُوَ نَجِسٌ، فَيَسِيلُ مِنْهُ شَيْءٌ فِي المَاءِ. وَقَوْلُهُ: (كالصَّقْرِ، وَالشَّاهِينِ)
And the third [category]: its use is disliked (makruh) when other [water] is available, and it is the su'r of the domestic cat; because the ruling of impurity is dropped by consensus, due to the cause of circumambulation mentioned in his statement: 'It is not impure; it is among those who go around you and go around [the house].' Al-Tirmidhi said: hasan sahih hadith. As for the dislike (karahah) of its su'r as tanzihi (disliked but not sinful) according to the most correct view; it is because it does not avoid impurity, like water in which a child has dipped his hand. And the wild cat's su'r is impure due to the absence of the cause of circumambulation in it. And the su'r of the free-range chicken, which roams in filth to pick up grain, but the purity of its beak from impurity is not known, so due to doubt its su'r is not judged impure and thus is disliked. If it is not like that, then there is no dislike in its su'r, like one that is confined and its beak does not reach filth. And the su'r of birds of prey, and the dislike of their su'r because they mix with carcasses and impurities, so they resemble the free-range chicken, such that if one is certain that there is no impurity on its beak, it is not disliked. And analogy (qiyas) would require its su'r to be impure like beasts of prey due to the commonality of the prohibition of their meat, but its purity is by istihsan (juristic preference) because they drink with their beak, which is pure bone, while beasts of prey drink with their tongue, which is wet with their saliva generated from their meat, and it is impure, so something flows from it into the water. And his statement: 'like the falcon and the shahin.'
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage explains the third category of su'r: disliked (makruh tanzihan) to use when other water is available. The domestic cat's su'r is pure by consensus due to the hadith that cats are not impure as they 'go around you.' However, it is disliked because cats do not avoid impurities. If the cat is wild, its su'r is impure. For free-range chickens that roam in filth, their su'r is disliked due to doubt about the purity of their beaks; if they are confined, no dislike. For birds of prey, qiyas would make them impure like beasts of prey, but istihsan rules them pure because they drink with beaks (pure bone) rather than tongues. Their su'r is disliked only when they are known to have impurities on their beaks.

Key Terms
كراهة تنزيه (karahah tanzih): A level of dislike that is not sinful or impermissible, but recommended to avoid for caution.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference, a method of reasoning that sets aside strict analogy (qiyas) for a more suitable ruling based on ease, custom, or subtle evidence.
مخلاة (mukhallah): A chicken that is left free to roam in search of food, potentially coming into contact with filth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the su'r of a domestic cat considered pure but disliked?
A) Because its meat is halal but its saliva is impure
B) Because the hadith declares it pure, but it does not avoid impurities
C) Because it is a predator like beasts of prey
D) Because it was specifically mentioned in the Quran

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school balances proof and caution: cat su'r is pure by explicit text but disliked due to habit; chicken and bird of prey su'r are pure by istihsan but disliked when contamination is likely.

Makruh Water Leftover: Cat, Chicken, and Predatory Birds
Explaining the third category: makruh water leftover from cat, chicken, and birds of prey.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for water leftover from a domestic cat, free-ranging chicken, and predatory birds, and explain the reasoning using the hadith and istihsan.

Core Idea
Cat's leftover is pure but disliked; birds' leftover is pure by istihsan overriding qiyas.

Water leftover (su'r) from some animals is pure but its use in wudu is disliked when better water exists. This lesson examines the third category: animals whose su'r is makruh tanzihan. The ruling blends a clear hadith about cats with analogical reasoning and istihsan for predatory birds, illustrating core Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Animals and Ruling
Read the passage and list the animals whose leftover water is makruh tanzihan. Note the hukm: pure but disliked for wudu when other pure water is available.
The ruling applies only when other water without dislike exists.
2
Examine the Proof for Cats
Locate the hadith about the cat. Understand why it proves purity (taharah) but not complete absence of dislike. Note the distinction between domestic and wild cats.
The hadith explicitly negates impurity; dislike is due to habits, not impurity.
3
Apply Analogy and Istihsan for Birds
Compare the qiyas (analogy with predatory mammals) and the istihsan that overrides it. Understand why predatory birds' leftover is ruled pure but disliked.
Birds drink with beaks (bone), not tongues, so the illa of impurity is absent.
4
Extend to Chicken and House Dwellers
See why free-ranging chicken's leftover is disliked (uncleanness uncertain) and how domestic animals with flowing blood (mice, snakes) are included. Note exceptions for confined chicken and bloodless creatures.
Certainty of purity removes dislike; doubt keeps dislike.
5
Summarize the Legal Principle
Formulate the overarching principle: su'r of animals that are not impure but frequently contact impurity is makruh tanzihan due to caution, unless necessity dictates.
The ruling balances textual proof (hadith) and practical reasoning (istihsan).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثَّالِثُ مَكَرُوهُ اسْتِعْمَالُهُ مَعَ وُجُودِ غَيْرِهِ وَهُوَ سُؤْرُ الهَرَةِ، والدَّجَاجَةِ المُخَلاةِ، وسباعِ الطَّيرِ: كالصَّقْرِ، والشاهين. (و) القسم :((الثَّالِثُ): سؤر (مَكرُوهُ اسْتِعْمَالُهُ) أي: التوضؤ به كراهة تنزيه (مع وُجُودِ غَيْره) مما لا كراهة فيه، ولا يكره عند عدم الماء لأنه طاهر، لا يجوز المصير إلى التيمـم مـع وجوده، ( وَهُوَ سُؤْرُ الهَرَةِ الأهلية؛ لسقوط حكم النجاسة اتفاقاً؛ بعلة الطواف المنصوص عليه بقوله : إنها لَيْسَتْ بِنَجسة، إنهَا مِنَ الطَّوافِينَ عَلَيْكُمْ والطَّوَافَاتِ ». قال الترمذي: حديث حسن صحيح. وأما كراهة سؤرها كراهة تنزيه على الأصح؛ فلأنها لا تتحامى النجاسة، كماء غمس صغير يده فيه، وحمل إصغاء النبي ا ل ل ل ل لها الإناء على زوال ذلك الوهم، لعلمه بحالها في زمان لا يتوهم نجاسة فمها بمنجس تناولته والهرة البرية سؤرها نجس لفقد علة الطواف فيها، ويكره أن تلحس الهرة كف إنسان، ثم يصلي قبل غسله، أو يأكل من بقية الطعام التي أكلت منه؛ لقيام ريقها بذلك، إذا كان غنياً يجد غيره، أما الفقير فلا يكره له للضرورة. (وَ) سؤر ( الدَّجَاجَةِ) بتثليث الدال، وتاؤها للوحدة، لا للتأنيث، كذا في «الصحاح وقال في المصفى من باب أبي حنيفة الدجاج مشترك بين الذكر والأنثى، والدجاجة الأنثى خاصة. ولهذا قال في ( الجامع الكبير ) : لو حلف لا يأكل لحم دجاجة، لا يحنث بأكل لحم الديك. ( المُخَلاةِ) وهي التي تجول في القاذورات، لتلتقط الحب، ولكــن لـم يُعلم طهارة منقارها من نجاسته، فلذا لم يحكم بنجاسة سؤرها بالشك فيكره، فإن لم يكن كذلك، فلا كراهة في سؤرها، كالتي حبست، ولا يصل منقارها إلى قذر. (وَ) سؤر (سـبـاع الـطـيـر ) وكراهة سؤرها، لأنها تخالط الميتات والنجاسات فأشبهت الدجاجة المخلاة، حتى لو تيقن أنه لا نجاسة على منقارها، لا يكره، وكان القياس نجاسة سؤرها ، كسباع البهائم بجامع حرمة لحمها، ولكن طهارته استحساناً؛ لأنها تشرب بمنقارها ، وهو عظم طاهر وسباع البهائم تشرب بلسانها، وهو مبتل بلعابها المتولد من لحمها، وهو نجس، فيسيل منه شيء في الماء، وقوله: (كالصقر، والشاهين) ( والحِدَأَةِ) مثال لسباع الطير ويلحق بها الغراب الأبقع والرخم ) ؛ لمخالطتها النجاسة. (وَ) سؤر (سَوَاكِنِ البُيُوتِ) مما له دم سائل ( كالفأرة) والحية والوزغة، لأن الضرورة التي وقعت الإشـارة إليها في الهرة موجودة فيها، فإنها تسكن البيوت وطوافها ألزم، وهـو الـعـلـة فـي البـاب لسقوط النجاسة، فبقيت الكراهة لحرمة لحمها، وقوله : (لا) يكره سؤر ما يسكن البيوت، فما لا دم لـه كالخنفس والصرصر، وبنات وردان، و (العَقْرَبِ) نفي لإلحاقها بسواكن البيوت التي لها دم في ذلك، إذ ليس لها لعاب متولد من لحم نجس، فإنها لا نفس لها سائلة، ولا ينجس الماء بموتها فيه. وقد وقع في بعض الكتب، كالبدائع» و « شرح منية المصلي ، ذكر العقرب من جملة سواكن البيوت التي يكره سؤرها، وفيه ما قد علمته وفي غيرها اقتصر في تمثيله ما يكره سوره من سواكن البيوت على قوله كالحية والفأرة. وهو واضح فليتنبه له، وهذا مما منَّ الله علي به، ولم أره مسطوراً.
The third is that the usage of which is disliked when other [water] is present, and it is the leftover of the cat, the free-ranging chicken, and predatory birds: like the falcon and the shahin. (And) the section: the third: the leftover which usage is disliked, i.e., performing ablution with it as a tanzihan dislike, when other [water] without such dislike is present. It is not disliked when water is absent because it is pure; one may not resort to tayammum while it exists. It is the leftover of the domestic cat because the ruling of impurity is removed by consensus, due to the cause of circumambulation mentioned in his saying: 'It is not impure; it is among those that go around you.' At-Tirmidhi said: hasan sahih hadith. As for the dislike of its leftover being tanzihan in the most correct view, it is because it does not guard against impurity, like water in which a child dips his hand, and the interpretation of the Prophet causing it to drink from the vessel is that such a notion is removed, for his knowledge of its state in a time when the impurity of its mouth due to something impure it might have taken is not imagined. The wild cat's leftover is impure due to the absence of the cause of circumambulation. It is disliked for a cat to lick a person's hand and then he prays before washing it, or eats from the remainder of food from which it ate, because its saliva remains on that, if he is rich and finds other [food]; but for the poor it is not disliked due to necessity. (And) the leftover of the chicken (with three pronunciations of the dal, and its ta is for the unit, not for femininity) as in as-Sihah, and said in al-Mustafa from the chapter of Abu Hanifah: ad-dajaj is common between male and female, and ad-dajajah specifically the female. Hence he said in al-Jami' al-Kabir: if he swore not to eat the meat of a chicken, he does not break his oath by eating the meat of a rooster. (The free-ranging one) which roams in filth to pick up grains, but the purity of its beak from its impurity is not known, so its leftover is not ruled impure due to doubt, thus it is disliked. If not so, then there is no dislike in its leftover, like one that is confined and its beak does not reach filth. (And) the leftover of predatory birds. The dislike of their leftover is because they come into contact with carrion and impurities, thus they resemble the free-ranging chicken. If one is certain that there is no impurity on its beak, it is not disliked. The analogy was for its leftover to be impure, like predatory animals, due to the common cause of the prohibition of their meat, but its purity is by istihsan because they drink with their beak, which is pure bone, whereas predatory animals drink with their tongue, which is wet with their saliva generated from their impure meat, so something flows from it into the water. And his saying: like the falcon and the shahin (and the kite) is an example of predatory birds, and joined to them are the piebald crow and the carrion crow due to their contact with impurity. (And) the leftover of domestic animals that have flowing blood, like the mouse, the snake, and the gecko, because the necessity pointed out in the case of the cat exists in them, for they inhabit houses and their going around is more pressing, and that is the cause in this chapter for removal of impurity, so the dislike remains due to the prohibition of their meat. And his saying: (no) the leftover of domestic animals that have no flowing blood is not disliked, like the dung beetle, the cricket, the little bugs, and the scorpion, is a negation of joining them to domestic animals that have blood in that respect, since they have no saliva generated from impure meat, for they have no flowing blood, nor does water become impure by their death in it. It has occurred in some books, like al-Bada'i' and Sharh Munyat al-Musalli, to mention the scorpion among domestic animals whose leftover is disliked, but there is in that what you have known; and in other books, they limited the example of what is disliked among domestic animals to his saying: like the snake and the mouse. This is clear, so let one pay attention to it. This is something with which Allah has favored me, and I have not seen it written.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage explains the third category of water according to the Hanafi school: water leftover (su'r) from specific animals is pure but disliked (makruh tanzihan) to use when other pure water is available. The animals discussed are the domestic cat, free-ranging chicken, and predatory birds. The ruling is based on the principle that while these animals are not impure, they often come into contact with impurities, so their leftover water is avoided out of caution, though it is not impure. For the cat, the hadith indicates it is not impure (tahir), but it is disliked because cats do not avoid impurities. The free-ranging chicken is disliked because its beak may be contaminated; if confined and clean, no dislike. Predatory birds are given the same ruling by istihsan, even though analogy with predatory animals would suggest impurity; the difference is that birds drink with their beaks (bone) while predatory mammals drink with their saliva-moistened tongues (impure meat). Domestic animals with flowing blood (like mice, snakes) are also included, but those without flowing blood (like scorpions) are not disliked. The author notes a correction regarding scorpions mentioned in some texts.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): Water leftover after an animal drinks from it, or water that remains after a person or animal drinks.
مكروه تنزيه (makruh tanzihi): Disliked but not prohibited; its avoidance is commendable but not sinful.
هرة (hirah): Domestic cat, as opposed to the wild cat (al-hirah al-bariyyah) whose su'r is impure.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides a strict analogy (qiyas) for a stronger reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition is the water leftover from a domestic cat makruh tanzihan?
A) When other pure water is available
B) When the cat is wild
C) When the person is in a state of janabah
D) When the water is more than two qullahs

Key Takeaway
Water leftover from a domestic cat, free-ranging chicken, and predatory birds is pure but makruh tanzihan when other pure water is available, blending hadith proof and istihsan.

Water Leftover from Mule and Donkey: Doubtful but Pure
Explaining the fourth category and the basis for doubt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the water leftover from mule and donkey, explain why it is classified as doubtful (mashkuk), and apply the practical consequence regarding wudu.

Core Idea
The leftover water of mule and donkey is ruled pure despite conflicting hadith about their meat.

In this lesson, we examine the fourth category of water in Hanafi fiqh: the water leftover (su'r) from mules and donkeys. While the purity of this water is classified as doubtful (mashkuk) due to conflicting narrations about their meat, the correct and operative view is that the water is pure (tahir) and purifying (tahur). We will explore the reasoning behind this classification and the practical implication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The water leftover from a mule or donkey. What is the hukm? It is classified as mashkuk, but the correct view is that it is tahur (purifying).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? The conflicting hadith about the permissibility of donkey meat: one hadith permitting, another prohibiting.
The hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the conflict create doubt? The prohibition of meat might imply impurity of the animal, and thus impurity of saliva. But the permissive hadith suggests purity. This contradiction makes the water doubtful.
The Hanafi school resolves this doubt by preferring purity based on practical consequences.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there disagreement? Yes, other schools may consider the water impure. The Hanafi school acknowledges the doubt but rules purity.
The text says 'mukhtalaf fih' (disputed).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon? The correct view (al-sahih) is that the water is pure and purifying. This is the mufta bihi.
The evidence for the preferred view: if one uses this water for wudu and later finds pure water, no repetition is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والرَّابِعُ: مَشكُوكٌ فِي طَهُورِيَّتِهِ، وهو: سُؤْرَ البَغْلِ، وَالحِمَارِ. وصُرِّحَنَا بِأَنَّ الشَّكَّ فِي طُهُورِيَّتِهِ بِنَاءً عَلَى رِوَايَةِ طَهَارَةِ لِعَابِهِ، وَهُوَ الصَّحِيحُ، لِأَنَّهُ لَوْ وَجَدَ مَاءً بَعْدَ الْوُضُوءِ بِهِ لَا يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ غَسْلُ رَأْسِهِ، وَلَوْ كَانَ الشَّكُّ فِي طَهَارَتِهِ، لَوَجَبَ غَسْلُهُ احْتِيَاطًا لِتَوَهُمِ النَّجَاسَةِ. وَسَبَبُ الشَّكِّ فِيهِ قِيلَ: تَعَارُضُ الْخَبَرَيْنِ فِي إِبَاحَةِ لَحْمِهِ، وَحُرْمَتِهِ لِقَوْلِهِ ( أَطْعِمْ أَهْلَكَ مِنْ سَمِينِ حُمُرِكَ ) وَأَمَرَ مُنَادِيًا فَنَادَى فِي النَّاسِ، إِنَّ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ يَنْهَاكُمْ عَنْ لَحْمِ الْحُمُرِ الأَهْلِيَّةِ. فَأُكْفِئَتِ الْقُدُورُ، وَإِنَّهَا لَتَفُورُ بِاللَّحْمِ. وَقِيلَ: تَعَارُضُ الأَثَرَيْنِ.
The fourth is what is doubtful regarding its purifying quality, and it is the leftover of the mule and the donkey. And we have stated clearly that the doubt about its purifying quality is based on the narration of the purity of its saliva, and that is the correct [view]. Because if he finds water after performing ablution with it, he is not required to wash his head; if there were doubt about its purity, he would have to wash it as a precaution due to the presumption of impurity. The cause of the doubt is said to be the contradiction between the two reports regarding the permissibility of its meat and its prohibition: his saying 'Feed your family from the fat of your donkeys' and he commanded a caller to call out among the people: 'Indeed Allah and His Messenger forbid you [the meat of] domestic donkeys.' So the pots were overturned while they were boiling with meat. And it is said: the contradiction of the two effects.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage explains the fourth category of water: the water leftover from mules and donkeys is considered doubtful (mashkuk) regarding its ability to purify (tahuriyyah). The correct view (sahih) is that it is pure (tahir) and can be used for purification, because if someone performs wudu with it and later finds other water, they do not have to repeat wudu. However, it is classified as doubtful because there are conflicting hadith about the permissibility of donkey meat: one hadith permits it, another prohibits it. Since the prohibition of meat is linked to impurity in some analogy, this creates doubt about the status of the animal's saliva and therefore its leftover water. Nevertheless, the predominant Hanafi view is that the water is pure and purifying (tahur), as indicated by the practical consequence mentioned.

Key Terms
مشكوك (mashkuk): Doubtful; a ruling that is not definitively established due to conflicting evidence.
طهورية (tahuriyyah): The quality of being purifying (i.e., capable of removing ritual impurity).
البغل والحمار (al-baghl wa al-himar): Mule (offspring of horse and donkey) and donkey; their meat is disputed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because they drink from impure sources
B) Because of conflicting hadith about the permissibility of their meat
C) Because they are hybrids
D) Because they are rarely found

Key Takeaway
The leftover water of mule and donkey is ruled pure (tahur) by the Hanafi school, despite being classified as doubtful due to conflicting hadith about their meat.

The Ruling on the Doubtful Su'r of Donkeys and Mules
Ruling and proof for the fourth category of residual water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the su'r of donkeys and mules, explain the cause of doubt, and apply the practical ruling of performing both wudu and tayammum when only this water is available.

Core Idea
The su'r of donkeys and mules is doubtfully purifying; one must do both wudu and tayammum to ensure valid prayer.

In Hanafi fiqh, residual water (su'r) is classified based on the animal's nature. The su'r of donkeys and mules falls into the fourth category: doubtful in its purifying quality. This lesson examines the evidence, the reason for doubt, and the practical ruling derived from the conflict of two hadiths on the permissibility of donkey meat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fourth category of su'r
Recognize that the su'r of donkeys and mules is classified as mashkuk (doubtful) in its purifying quality, meaning it is neither definitively purifying nor impure.
This category applies also to the su'r of the mule because it is born from a donkey.
2
Understand the cause of doubt
The doubt arises from two conflicting hadiths: one permitting feeding donkey meat and another prohibiting it. This conflict creates uncertainty about the legal status of the animal and, by extension, its saliva and su'r.
The text records two false explanations for the doubt and refutes them via Kharazadah's analysis.
3
Critically analyze the false explanations
Kharazadah rejects (1) that conflict between a prohibitor and permitter creates doubt (it creates prohibition), and (2) that disagreement among jurists creates doubt (the original principle of purity prevails).
The correct cause is the ambiguity in whether the necessity (darurah) that drops impurity is fully realized in the donkey.
4
Derive the practical ruling
Since the su'r is doubtful, it does not remove ritual impurity with certainty. Therefore, if no other water is available, one must perform both wudu with this water and tayammum, then pray.
The conjunction 'waw' indicates choice of order; it is best to perform wudu first.
5
Note intra-Hanafi differences and the preferred position
Imam Zafar held that wudu must be performed first; some distinguished between male and female donkeys, but the text rejects this. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the combined requirement.
It is recommended to wash the limbs afterwards with pure water to remove any trace.

(۹) أخرجه البخاري في المغازي، باب: غزوة خيبر (٤٢١٦)، ومسلم في الصيد والذبائح، باب: تحريم أكل لحم الحمر الأنسية (١٤٠٧).

فَإِنْ لم يَجِدْ غَيْرَهُ تَوَضَأَ به، وتيمم، ثُمَّ صَلَّى. لَمْ
الماء
فعن ابن عمر نجاسته، وعن ابن عباس طهارته. وليس أحدهما أولى من الآخر، فبقي مشكلاً. وقد زيف شيخ الإسلام خواهر زاده الأول، بأن تعارض المحرم والمبيــح لا يـوجـب شـكـا، بـل حرمة، وكذا زيف الثاني، بأن الاختلاف أيضاً لا يوجب الشك، كما لو أخبر عدلان أحدهما بطهارة الماء، والآخر بنجاسته، فإنهما يتهاتران ) ، ويعمل بالأصل وهو طهارة الماء. والصواب عنده أن سببه التردد في تحقق الضرورة المسقطة للنجاسة وعدمها، فإن له شبهاً بالهرة لمخالطته الناس في الدور والأفنية، وشربه من الأواني المستعملة، وشبهاً بالكلب لمجانبته وعدم ولوجه المضائق ولوج الهــرة والفأرة، فلو انتفت الضرورة أصلاً كان سؤره نجساً كسؤر الكلب، ولو تحققت فيه كتحققها في الهرة، لو جب الحكم ببقائه على الطهورية، فإذا تحققت من وجه دون وجه، بقي مشكلاً، فلا ينجس بالشبهة، ولم يزل الحدث به، ولا يؤكل لحمه للشبهة، والبغل متولد من الحمار، فأخذ حكمه. (فَإِنْ لمْ يَجِدْ ) المحدث (غَيْرَهُ) أي: غير سؤر الحمار أو البغل (توضـاً بـه وتيمم) عطف بالواو، ليفيـد التخيير في تقديم أياً شاء، والأفضل تقديم الوضوء رعاية لقول زفــر رحمه الله بلزوم تقديمه، والأحوط أن ينوي، للاختلاف في لزوم النية في الوضوء بسؤر الحمار (ثُمَّ صلّى) فتكون صلاته صحيحة بيقين، لأن التوضؤ به لو جاز لا يضره التيمم وكذا عكسه، ثم من مشايخنا مــن جـعـل هـذا في سؤر الأتان، وقال في سؤر الفحل إنه نجس لأنه يشم البول، فينجس شفتاه، وهذا غير سديد، لأنه أمر موهوم لا يغلب وجوده، ولا يؤثر في إزالة الثابت، ويستحب غسل أعضائه بعد بالماء الطيب عن أثر الماء المشكوك، والمكروه.
The fourth: doubtful regarding its purifying quality, and it is: the residual water (su'r) of the mule and the donkey. (And the kite) is an example of birds of prey, and the piebald crow and the carrion crow are attached to it due to their mixing with impurity. And the su'r of house-dwellers having flowing blood, like the mouse, the snake, and the gecko, because the necessity indicated for the cat exists in them, for they inhabit houses and their movement is more frequent, and this is the effective cause ('illa) in this chapter for dropping the impurity, so dislike remains due to the prohibition of their flesh. And his statement: (not) disliked is the su'r of what inhabits houses, so those without blood, like the beetle, the cricket, the 'banat wardan', and the scorpion, is a negation of attaching them to the house-dwellers that have blood in that regard, since they have no saliva generated from impure flesh, for they have no flowing blood, and water does not become impure by their death in it. It occurs in some books, like al-Bada'i' and Sharh Munyat al-Musalli, that the scorpion is included among house-dwellers whose su'r is disliked, and in it is what you know, and in others the example of disliked su'r among house-dwellers is restricted to the snake and the mouse. This is clear, so let one pay attention, and this is something God has granted me and I have not seen it written. (And) the (fourth) section: su'r of (doubtful), meaning suspended in its ruling of purifying quality. So it is not ruled definitively purifying, nor is it negated from purifying quality. And it is: the su'r of the mule whose mother was a she-ass, and the donkey, which applies to male and female. And we have explicitly stated that the doubt regarding its purifying quality is based on the narration of the purity of its saliva, and this is correct, because if he finds water after performing wudu with it, he is not required to wash his head, but if there were doubt about its purity, he would have to wash it as a precaution due to the suspicion of impurity. The cause of doubt is said to be the conflicting of the two reports regarding the permissibility of its meat and its prohibition, according to his statement: 'Feed your family from the fat of your donkeys' and 'he commanded a caller to announce among the people: Verily Allah and His Messenger forbid you the meat of domestic donkeys,' so the pots were overturned, though they were boiling with meat. And it is said: the conflicting of the two traditions. (A) Footnote: (1) The piebald crow: the one whose whiteness and blackness are mixed, so it is not known which is more, hence the crow is called piebald if it has whiteness, and it is the worst kind of crows, thus it becomes a proverb for everything vile. (2) The carrion crow: a bird that eats filth and is among the abominations. (3) The gecko: a house lizard. (4) The beetle: a black bug. (5) Banat wardan: a bug like a beetle, reddish in color, most often found in bathrooms and latrines. (6) i.e., it has no blood. (7) The anan: see p. (37). (8) Narrated by Abu Dawud in al-At'imah, chapter on the prohibition of meat of domestic donkeys (3809), and al-Bayhaqi in his Sunan, book of sacrifices, chapter on meat of domestic donkeys (9/332). (9) Narrated by al-Bukhari in al-Maghazi, chapter: expedition of Khaybar (4216), and Muslim in al-Sayd wa al-Dhaba'ih, chapter: prohibition of eating meat of domestic donkeys (1407). So if he does not find other than it, he performs wudu with it and tayammum, then prays. There are narrations from Ibn 'Umar of its impurity and from Ibn 'Abbas of its purity. And neither is more preponderant than the other, so it remains problematic. Shaykh al-Islam Kharazadah rejected the first, saying that conflict between a prohibitor and a permitter does not produce doubt, rather prohibition; and he also rejected the second, saying that disagreement also does not produce doubt, as if two trustworthy persons report, one the purity of water and the other its impurity, then they are neutralized, and one acts on the original principle which is the purity of the water. The correct opinion according to him is that its cause is the hesitation regarding the realization of the necessity that drops impurity and its absence. For it has similarity to the cat in its mixing with people in houses and courtyards and drinking from used vessels, and similarity to the dog in its shunning and not entering narrow passages like the cat and mouse. So if the necessity were absent entirely, its su'r would be impure like the dog's su'r; if it were realized in it as in the cat, the ruling would necessarily remain that it is purifying. Since it is realized from one aspect and not from another, it remains problematic. So it is not impure due to the doubt, nor does it remove ritual impurity, nor is its meat eaten due to the doubt. And the mule is born from the donkey, so it takes its ruling. (So if) the person in minor ritual impurity (does not find) other than it, i.e., other than the su'r of the donkey or mule (he performs wudu with it and tayammum) with the conjunction 'waw' to indicate choice in whichever he prefers, and the best is to perform wudu first, honoring the statement of Zafar (may Allah have mercy on him) that it must be performed first. And the most precautionary is to intend (the wudu) due to the disagreement regarding the necessity of intention in wudu with the su'r of the donkey. (Then he prays) so his prayer is certainly valid, because if the wudu with it is permissible, the tayammum does not harm him, and vice versa. Then, some of our scholars applied this to the su'r of the she-ass, and said regarding the su'r of the stallion that it is impure because it sniffs urine, so its lips become impure. But this is not sound, for it is a matter presumed but not predominantly occurring, and it does not affect the removal of what is established. And it is recommended that he wash his limbs afterwards with pure water to remove any trace of the doubtful water, and the disliked aspect.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the fourth category of residual water (su'r) in Hanafi fiqh: the su'r of donkeys and mules. The author begins by defining this category as doubtful (mashkuk) in its purifying quality, meaning it is neither definitively purifying nor definitively impure. He then explains the reason for the doubt: two conflicting reports about the meat of domestic donkeys—one permitting it and one prohibiting it. The commentary includes a critique of two false explanations: (1) that the conflict between a prohibitor and a permitter creates doubt (Shaykh al-Islam Kharazadah says it creates prohibition, not doubt), and (2) that disagreement among jurists creates doubt (he gives the analogy of two trustworthy witnesses contradicting each other, in which case the original principle of purity prevails). Instead, Kharazadah argues that the doubt arises from the ambiguity of whether the necessity (darurah) that causes the impurity to be dropped exists in the donkey. The donkey resembles the cat in its mixing with humans (necessity present) but also resembles the dog in its avoidance of narrow places (necessity absent). Hence the su'r remains doubtful: it does not become impure due to the doubt, nor does it remove ritual impurity. The practical ruling: if a person has no other water, he must perform both wudu with this water and tayammum, then pray, ensuring his prayer is valid. The commentary also notes that the mule takes the same ruling as the donkey. There is a discussion about whether the ruling applies to both the male and female donkey (the text says the she-ass is included) and refutes the opinion that the stallion's su'r is impure due to sniffing urine. Finally, it is recommended to wash the limbs afterwards with pure water to remove any trace of the doubtful water.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): The residual water left in a vessel after an animal drinks from it, or the moisture left on its mouth.
طَهُورِيَّة (tahuriyyah): The quality of being purifying (mutahhir), i.e., capable of removing ritual impurity.
مَشكُوك (mashkuk): Doubtful; a legal category where the ruling is uncertain due to conflicting evidence.
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity; here, the unavoidable mixing of domestic animals with humans in houses, which justifies dropping the impurity ruling for their su'r.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should a person do if the only water available is the su'r (residual water) of a donkey?
A) Perform wudu with it and pray, as it is pure.
B) Perform tayammum only, as the water is impure.
C) Perform both wudu with it and tayammum, then pray.
D) Seek another water source even if it requires travel.

Key Takeaway
If only the su'r of a donkey or mule is available, one must perform both wudu and tayammum to guarantee the validity of prayer.

The Legal Uncertainty of Su'r of Donkey and Mule
Ruling on su'r of donkey/mule with proof via qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the su'r of donkey and mule and explain the reasoning behind its classification as legally doubtful (mushkik).

Core Idea
The su'r of donkey/mule is neither pure nor impure—it is a legal doubt demanding both wudu and tayammum.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on the leftover water (su'r) of a donkey or mule. Because this animal shares traits with both the cat (pure) and the dog (impure), its su'r falls into a category of legal doubt (shubha). The solution is to combine wudu with that water and tayammum to ensure your prayer is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the passage is ruling on: the use of water leftover by a donkey or mule for wudu. The ruling is that the water is legally doubtful (mushkik), so one must perform both wudu with it and tayammum.
The ruling is a combination of actions, not a simple purity classification.
2
Locate the dalil
The author provides a qiyas (analogy) citing two animals: the cat (pure su'r) and the dog (impure su'r). The donkey/mule shares resemblance (shabah) with both.
This is a qiyas shabah, not qiyas jali.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The resemblance causes doubt: the donkey/mule mixes with humans like a cat (indicating purity) but avoids narrow places like a dog (indicating impurity). Since the necessity that would render the su'r pure is partially realized, it remains doubtful.
The doubt is based on the balance of two opposing characteristics.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is disagreement among early scholars: Ibn Umar considered it impure, Ibn Abbas considered it pure. Also, within the Hanafi school, Imam Zufar held that wudu should precede tayammum.
The author refutes both Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas using Kharzadeh's reasoning.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is to combine wudu and tayammum, with wudu first being preferred. Intention (niyyah) is recommended due to disagreement on its necessity.
This ensures the prayer is valid regardless of the actual status of the water.

Source Text

فَإِنْ لم يَجِدْ غَيْرَهُ تَوَضَأَ به، وتيمم، ثُمَّ صَلَّى. الماء فعن ابن عمر نجاسته، وعن ابن عباس طهارته. وليس أحدهما أولى من الآخر، فبقي مشكلاً. وقد زيف شيخ الإسلام خواهر زاده الأول، بأن تعارض المحرم والمبيــح لا يـوجـب شـكـا، بـل حرمة، وكذا زيف الثاني، بأن الاختلاف أيضاً لا يوجب الشك، كما لو أخبر عدلان أحدهما بطهارة الماء، والآخر بنجاسته، فإنهما يتهاتران ) ، ويعمل بالأصل وهو طهارة الماء. والصواب عنده أن سببه التردد في تحقق الضرورة المسقطة للنجاسة وعدمها، فإن له شبهاً بالهرة لمخالطته الناس في الدور والأفنية، وشربه من الأواني المستعملة، وشبهاً بالكلب لمجانبته وعدم ولوجه المضائق ولوج الهــرة والفأرة، فلو انتفت الضرورة أصلاً كان سؤره نجساً كسؤر الكلب، ولو تحققت فيه كتحققها في الهرة، لو جب الحكم ببقائه على الطهورية، فإذا تحققت من وجه دون وجه، بقي مشكلاً، فلا ينجس بالشبهة، ولم يزل الحدث به، ولا يؤكل لحمه للشبهة، والبغل متولد من الحمار، فأخذ حكمه. (فَإِنْ لمْ يَجِدْ ) المحدث (غَيْرَهُ) أي: غير سؤر الحمار أو البغل (توضـاً بـه وتيمم) عطف بالواو، ليفيـد التخيير في تقديم أياً شاء، والأفضل تقديم الوضوء رعاية لقول زفــر رحمه الله بلزوم تقديمه، والأحوط أن ينوي، للاختلاف في لزوم النية في الوضوء بسؤر الحمار (ثُمَّ صلّى) فتكون صلاته صحيحة بيقين، لأن التوضؤ به لو جاز لا يضره التيمم وكذا عكسه، ثم من مشايخنا مــن جـعـل هـذا في سؤر الأتان، وقال في سؤر الفحل إنه نجس لأنه يشم البول، فينجس شفتاه، وهذا غير سديد، لأنه أمر موهوم لا يغلب وجوده، ولا يؤثر في إزالة الثابت، ويستحب غسل أعضائه بعد بالماء الطيب عن أثر الماء المشكوك، والمكروه.
If one finds no other (water), he performs wudu with it, and tayammum, then prays. Water: from Ibn Umar (it is) najis, and from Ibn Abbas (it is) pure. Neither is more preferable than the other, so it remains doubtful. Shaykh al-Islam Kharzadeh refuted the first (view) by saying that the contradiction of the prohibiting and permitting does not necessitate doubt, but rather prohibition. Likewise, he refuted the second (view) because disagreement also does not necessitate doubt, just as if two trustworthy persons inform, one of the purity of water and the other of its impurity, they cancel each other out, and the principle (of purity of water) is acted upon. The correct view according to him is that its cause is the hesitation regarding the realization of the necessity that drops impurity and its absence. For it has resemblance to the cat due to its mixing with people in houses and courtyards, and its drinking from used vessels, and resemblance to the dog due to its aloofness and not entering narrow passages as the cat and mouse do. So if necessity were entirely absent, its leftover would be najis like the dog's leftover; and if it were realized in it like in the cat, the ruling of its remaining purifying would be necessary. So when it is realized in one way but not in another, it remains doubtful. Thus it is not judged impure due to doubt, nor does it remove hadath, and its meat is not eaten due to doubt. The mule is born from the donkey, so it takes its ruling. (Then if one does not find) the person in need of purification (any other) meaning other than the leftover water of the donkey or mule (he performs wudu with it and tayammum) the conjunctive 'and' gives the choice of which to precede, and the best is to precede wudu in observance of Zufar's view that it must be preceded. The most cautious is to intend (the wudu) due to the disagreement on the necessity of intention in wudu with the donkey's leftover. (Then he prays) so his prayer is certainly valid, because if wudu with it is permissible, tayammum does not harm it, and vice versa. Then among our scholars are those who applied this to the leftover of the female donkey, and said regarding the leftover of the male donkey that it is najis because he sniffs urine, so his lips become impure. This is unsound, because it is imaginary, not predominant, and does not affect the removal of the established (purity). It is recommended that he wash his limbs afterward with pure water to remove the trace of the doubtful water, and (the water) is disliked.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the leftover water (su'r) of a donkey and a mule. The author first presents the disagreement between Ibn Umar (saying it is impure) and Ibn Abbas (saying it is pure). Neither view is stronger, so the matter remains doubtful. Shaykh al-Islam Kharzadeh refutes both sides: conflicting evidence does not create doubt but rather prohibition, and mere disagreement also does not create doubt (like two contradicting witnesses). The correct cause of doubt, according to Kharzadeh, is the uncertainty about whether the necessity that removes impurity (the animal's closeness to humans) is fully realized. The donkey/mule has two aspects: it mixes with people like a cat (whose su'r is pure), but it also avoids narrow places like a dog (whose su'r is impure). Since the necessity is partially realized, the su'r remains doubtful: it is not ruled impure, but it also does not remove the state of ritual impurity (hadath). Therefore, one must perform both wudu with it and tayammum. The conjunctive 'and' gives choice of order, but the best is to do wudu first, following Imam Zufar. The prayer performed after that is certainly valid. Some later scholars distinguish between male and female donkey, considering the male's leftover impure due to imagined urine on its lips, but the author rejects this as fanciful. It is recommended to wash the limbs afterward with pure water to remove any trace of the doubtful water. The su'r itself is disliked.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): Leftover water that remains after an animal drinks from a vessel, or the water touched by the animal's mouth.
شبهة (shubha): Legal doubt or uncertainty about the ruling of a matter, here specifically the purity of the water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Perform tayammum only.
C) Perform both wudu with it and tayammum, then pray.
D) Seek out another water source; if none, they are excused from prayer.

Key Takeaway
The su'r of donkey/mule is a legal doubt (mushkik); therefore, one must combine wudu and tayammum to ensure the validity of prayer.

Taharrī for Mixed Water Vessels and Garments
Explains rules of taharrī for mixed water vessels and garments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for taharrī when water vessels or garments are mixed, and apply the principle that the minority in the face of the majority is like non-existent.

Core Idea
Taharrī relies on the majority: when most vessels are pure, guess; when most are impure, pour and do tayammum.

When pure and impure items are mixed and you cannot tell them apart, Islamic law provides a method called taharrī—legal discretion based on probability. In this passage, the text explains how taharrī applies to water vessels that are mixed by juxtaposition and to garments. You will learn when you can perform taharrī for wudu, when you must resort to tayammum, and why garments are treated differently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Taharrī is a method to choose between mixed pure and impure items. The ruling: it is permissible (mubah) when conditions are met. For wudu, it is allowed only when most vessels are pure; for drinking, always; for garments, always.
The act is the process of using one's best guess to determine which item is pure.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the principle 'al-maghlub fi muqabilat al-ghalib ka al-ma'dum' (the minority in the face of the majority is like non-existent). This is a qiyas based on general legal maxims.
This principle justifies treating the minority as legally non-existent when the majority clearly outweighs it.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
When most vessels are impure, the pure ones are considered non-existent, so all water is legally impure. Therefore taharrī for wudu is not allowed because the water is not mutahhir; instead, tayammum is required.
The same principle when most are pure means the impure are negligible, so taharrī for wudu is valid.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: the majority of mashayikh say to pour away the impure majority, while al-Tahawi says mix them for livestock water.
Both views are within the Hanafi school; the text favors the majority.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the majority view: pour away the vessels and perform tayammum. The text states 'inda aammat al-mashayikh (according to the general body of mashayikh).
For garments, there is no dispute: taharrī is always allowed because there is no substitute for covering the 'awrah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في التحري (لو اختلط اختلاط مجاورة لا ممازجة، (أَوَان) جمع إناء (أكثرُهَا طَاهِرُ) وأقلها نجس، (تَحَرِّى للتَّوَضُوْ) والاغتسال، وقيدنا بالأكثر ، لأنه لا . يجوز التحري عند التساوي ولكن يتيمم، والأفضل أن يريق الأواني أو يمزجها، ثم يتيمم، وإن وجد ثلاثة رجال ثلاث أوان، أحدها نجس وتحرى كل إناء جازت صلاتهم وحدانـا ) كما في «البحر » ، (وَ) تحرى عند إرادة (الشرب) والاحتياج إليه، فيريق ما غلب على ظنه نجاسته، ويستعمل ما غلب على ظنه طهارته، إذ المغلوب في مقابلة الغالب كالمعدوم، وإن اختلط إناء ان، ولم يتحرّ، وتوضأ بالماءين وصلى، جازت صلاته إذا مسح في موضعين من الرأس، وإن مسح في مكان واحد لا يجوز، لأنه إن توضأ بالطاهر أولاً زال الحدث، ثم إذا توضأ بالنجس تنجس أعضاؤه، وفاقد ما يزيل النجس تصح صلاته، وإن توضأ بالنجس أولاً تنجس أعضاؤه، ثم بالطاهر زال الحدث والنجاسة الحقيقية عنها، إلا أنه إن مسح في موضع واحد لا يجوز، لأن المسح إن كان بالطاهر أولاً يجوز، وإن كان بالطاهر آخراً لا يجوز، لأن البلل تنجس بأول الملاقاة، فلا يتأدى به المسح فدار بين أن يجوز وأن لا يجوز، فلا يجوز بالشك احتياطاً ) ، وإن مسح في مكانين جاز، وإنْ كانَ أكثرُهَا ) أي: الأواني المختلطة بالمجاورة، (نَحِسَـاً لا يَتَحَرَّى إلا للسُّرْبِ)؛ لأن الحكم للغالب، فكان الكل نجساً حكماً، فيريقه عـنــد عـامـة المشايخ، ويمزج بعضه ببعض لسقي الدواب عند الطحاوي، ثم يتيمم، (وَفي) حال (النِّيَابِ المُخْتَلِطَةِ يَتَحَرَّى) مطلقاً، (سَوَاءٌ كَانَ أَكْثَرُهَا طَاهِرَاً أَوْ نَجِسَاً)، إذ لا خلف للثوب في ســر الـــورة، بخلاف الماء، فإن التراب يخلفه كما في «مجمع الروايات»، فإذا تحرى وصلى الظهر في أحد ثوبين، أحدهما نجس، ثم وقع تحريه على الثاني، فصلى فيه العصر، لم تجز، لأنــا حكمنا بطهارة الأول بالاجتهاد، وكل حكم أمضى باجتهاد لا ينقض باجتهاد مثله، إلا في القبلة، لأنـه أمـر شـرعي، يحتمل الانتقال من جهة إلى جهة عند تبدل التحري، والنجاسة أمر حسي، لا يصير طاهراً
Chapter on Taharrī (legal discretion). (If vessels mix) with mixture of juxtaposition, not mingling, (vessels) plural of container, (most of them are pure) and a few are impure, (he performs taharrī for wudu) and ghusl. And we restrict to the majority because taharrī is not permissible when equal, but he performs tayammum, and the best is that he pours out the vessels or mixes them, then performs tayammum. And if three men find three vessels, one of which is impure, and each performs taharrī for a vessel, their prayer is valid, and they are alone (praying individually) as in al-Bahr. (And) he performs taharrī when intending (drinking) and needing it: he pours out what he strongly suspects to be impure and uses what he strongly suspects to be pure, because the minority in the face of the majority is like non-existent. And if two vessels mix and he does not perform taharrī, and performs wudu with both waters and prays, his prayer is valid if he wipes two places of the head; if he wipes one place, it is not valid. Because if he performs wudu with the pure first, the hadath is removed, then when he performs wudu with the impure, his limbs become impure; and one who lacks (water) that removes impurity, his prayer is valid. And if he performs wudu with the impure first, his limbs become impure, then with the pure, the hadath and true impurity are removed from them; except that if he wipes one place, it is not valid, because the wiping: if it was with the pure first, it is valid; if with the pure last, it is not valid, because the moisture becomes impure upon first contact, so wiping is not performed with it. Thus it oscillates between being valid and not, so it is not valid out of caution. And if he wipes two places, it is valid. And if most of them (i.e., vessels mixed by juxtaposition) are impure, he does not perform taharrī except for drinking, because the ruling is for the majority, so all are considered impure legally. So he pours them out according to the general body of mashayikh, and mixes some with some to water livestock according to al-Tahawi, then performs tayammum. (And in) the case of (mixed garments he performs taharrī) absolutely, (whether most of them are pure or impure), because there is no substitute for a garment in covering the private parts, unlike water, for soil substitutes for it as in Majma' al-Riwayat. So if he performs taharrī and prays Zuhr in one of two garments, one of which is impure, then his taharrī falls on the second and he prays Asr in it, it is not valid, because we have ruled the first pure by ijtihad, and every ruling made by ijtihad is not overturned by another similar ijtihad, except in the qibla, because it is a shar'i matter, allowing change from one direction to another when taharrī changes, while impurity is a sensory matter, it does not become pure.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof discussing the rules of taharrī (legal discretion) when water vessels are mixed by juxtaposition (not mingling). The key distinction is based on the majority: if most vessels are pure, one can perform taharrī for wudu and ghusl; if most are impure, taharrī is only allowed for drinking (because there's no alternative like tayammum). If equal, one must do tayammum. The best is to pour away or mix the vessels then do tayammum. If three men each perform taharrī on different vessels, each can pray individually. The text then discusses the case of two vessels without taharrī: using both waters and wiping the head in two places to ensure validity. The ruling for garments is different: taharrī is always allowed because there is no substitute for covering the 'awrah (unlike water where tayammum can replace wudu). However, once a taharrī ruling is made, it cannot be changed by another taharrī, except for qibla direction. This is because impurity is a sensory reality, not a juristic determination like direction.

Key Terms
تحري (taharrī): Legal discretion based on high probability (ghalabat al-zann) to choose between mixed pure and impure items.
مجاورة (mujawara): Juxtaposition; vessels placed near each other but their contents are not mixed.
نياب (niyab): Garments (likely a misOCR for ثياب).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When can one perform taharrī for wudu in the case of mixed water vessels?
A) When most vessels are impure.
B) When most vessels are pure.
C) Always, regardless of majority.
D) Only when there are exactly two vessels.

Key Takeaway
Taharrī for water is governed by the majority: use it for wudu only when most are pure; otherwise tayammum. For garments, taharrī is always valid.

Ruling on Mixed Vessels (Awān) in Cases of Doubt
Commentary on Nur al-Idah about taharrī for mixed vessels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for performing taharrī when vessels are mixed and apply the ruling when the majority is pure vs impure.

Core Idea
Taharrī is only valid when the majority of vessels are pure; otherwise, all are impure for purification.

This lesson from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies the Hanafi ruling on mixed vessels of water. The key is the principle of majority (ghalaba): when most vessels are pure, you must perform taharrī to identify the pure water; when most are impure, all are treated as impure and tayammum becomes necessary. The commentary also addresses a subtle case where two vessels are mixed and no taharrī is performed, showing the precision of Hanafi fiqh in balancing purity and practicality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Condition of Majority
The passage begins by stating that if vessels are mixed by adjacency (not blending), and most are pure, you must perform taharrī for wudū' and ghusl. If the number is equal, taharrī is not allowed and tayammum is performed.
Taharrī means legal estimation to determine the pure vessel.
2
Distinguish Between Pure Majority and Impure Majority
When the majority is impure, all vessels are considered impure for purposes of purification. Taharrī is only performed for drinking water, not for wudū'. The ruling follows the dominant state.
The overcome (maghlub) is treated as nonexistent.
3
Analyze the Scenario of Two Vessels Without Taharrī
If someone has two vessels (one pure, one impure) and performs wudū' with both without taharrī, the validity of prayer depends on the order of wiping the head. If he wipes in two places, it is valid; if one place, invalid. This is due to the uncertainty of which water was pure first.
The rationale involves the sequence of purification and impurity transmission.
4
Apply the Ruling for Drinking
When needing to drink, taharrī is always allowed regardless of majority, but when majority is impure, the person pours out what he thinks is impure and uses the rest. According to al-Tahawi, mixing all is permissible for animals.
This distinguishes between ritual purification (ibada) and worldly needs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في التحري (لو اختلط اختلاط مجاورة لا ممازجة، (أَوَان) جمع إناء (أكثرُهَا طَاهِرُ) وأقلها نجس، (تَحَرِّى للتَّوَضُوْ) والاغتسال، وقيدنا بالأكثر ، لأنه لا . يجوز التحري عند التساوي ولكن يتيمم، والأفضل أن يريق الأواني أو يمزجها، ثم يتيمم، وإن وجد ثلاثة رجال ثلاث أوان، أحدها نجس وتحرى كل إناء جازت صلاتهم وحدانـا ) كما في «البحر » ، (وَ) تحرى عند إرادة (الشرب) والاحتياج إليه، فيريق ما غلب على ظنه نجاسته، ويستعمل ما غلب على ظنه طهارته، إذ المغلوب في مقابلة الغالب كالمعدوم، وإن اختلط إناء ان، ولم يتحرّ، وتوضأ بالماءين وصلى، جازت صلاته إذا مسح في موضعين من الرأس، وإن مسح في مكان واحد لا يجوز، لأنه إن توضأ بالطاهر أولاً زال الحدث، ثم إذا توضأ بالنجس تنجس أعضاؤه، وفاقد ما يزيل النجس تصح صلاته، وإن توضأ بالنجس أولاً تنجس أعضاؤه، ثم بالطاهر زال الحدث والنجاسة الحقيقية عنها، إلا أنه إن مسح في موضع واحد لا يجوز، لأن المسح إن كان بالطاهر أولاً يجوز، وإن كان بالطاهر آخراً لا يجوز، لأن البلل تنجس بأول الملاقاة، فلا يتأدى به المسح فدار بين أن يجوز وأن لا يجوز، فلا يجوز بالشك احتياطاً ) ، وإن مسح في مكانين جاز، وإنْ كانَ أكثرُهَا ) أي: الأواني المختلطة بالمجاورة، (نَحِسَـاً لا يَتَحَرَّى إلا للسُّرْبِ)؛ لأن الحكم للغالب، فكان الكل نجساً حكماً، فيريقه عـنــد عـامـة المشايخ، ويمزج بعضه ببعض لسقي الدواب عند الطحاوي، ثم يتيمم
Chapter on Taharrī: If vessels are mixed by adjacency not blending, and most are pure, one performs taharrī for ablution and bathing. We restricted to majority because taharrī is not permissible when equal, but one performs tayammum. It is better to pour out the vessels or mix them then perform tayammum. If three men find three vessels, one impure, and each performs taharrī for a vessel, their prayers with each as imam are valid. And one performs taharrī when wanting to drink and in need of it; he pours out what he predominantly thinks is impure and uses what he predominantly thinks is pure, for the overcome is like nonexistent in comparison to the dominant. If two vessels are mixed and he did not perform taharrī, and he performed ablution with both waters and prayed, his prayer is valid if he wiped two places of the head; if he wiped one place, it is not valid. Because if he first performed ablution with the pure, the ritual impurity is removed, then when he performs ablution with the impure, his limbs become impure, and one who lacks what removes impurity, his prayer is valid. If he first performed ablution with the impure, his limbs become impure, then with the pure, the ritual impurity and physical impurity are removed from them. Except that if he wiped one place, it is not valid, because if the wipe was with the pure first, it is valid; if with the pure last, it is not valid because the moisture becomes impure at first contact, so the wipe is not performed. Thus there is doubt between permissibility and impermissibility, so it is not permissible out of precaution. And if he wiped two places, it is permissible. If most of them (the mixed vessels) are impure, he only performs taharrī for drinking, because the ruling follows the majority, so all are considered impure. He pours them out according to the majority of scholars, and according to al-Tahawi, he mixes some with each other for giving to beasts, then performs tayammum.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah's commentary explains the Hanafi ruling on performing taharrī (legal estimation) when vessels of water are mixed, some pure and some impure. The key principle is that taharrī is applicable only when the majority of vessels are pure, because the minority is treated as nonexistent. When the majority is impure, all are considered impure for purposes of purification, and taharrī is only for drinking. The commentator also addresses a special scenario involving two vessels where taharrī was not performed: if one uses both waters for wudū', the validity of prayer depends on the order of wiping the head. This demonstrates the meticulous nature of Hanafi fiqh in balancing ritual purity and practical necessity.

Key Terms
تحري (taharrī): Legal effort to determine the pure water or clean garment by estimation when mixed with impure ones.
أوان (awān): Plural of inā', meaning vessels containing liquid.
نجس (najis): Ritually impure according to Hanafi definition: any substance that is essentially impure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person has two vessels, one pure and one impure, and he performs wudū' using both without taharrī, his prayer is valid only if:
A) He wipes one place on his head.
B) He wipes two places on his head.
C) He performed ghusl instead.
D) He recites the intention aloud.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on mixed vessels hinges on majority: when pure vessels are more, taharrī is wajib for purification; when impure are more, all are impure and tayammum is made, except for drinking.

Conflicting Reports and Istishab: The Hanafi Approach
Ruling-with-proof: conflicting reports and doubt categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of tahatur to conflicting evidence and distinguish the three types of doubt to determine the correct ruling.

Core Idea
When two credible reports cancel out, the original legal state prevails – istishab is the default.

In Islamic law, uncertainty often arises from conflicting pieces of evidence. The Hanafi school has a clear method: when two equally trustworthy reports contradict each other, they cancel out (tahatur), and the original ruling remains in force. This lesson unpacks that principle and also categorizes doubt into three types, each with its own legal consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario of conflicting reports
Start by recognizing when two trustworthy witnesses give opposite information about a legal object (e.g., meat, water).
Both reporters are assumed equally honest ('adl) – otherwise tarjih (preponderance) would apply.
2
Apply tahatur and revert to the original ruling
Since the reports are equal, they cancel out. Then apply istishab – the original state (e.g., prohibition of meat, purity of water) is presumed to continue.
This is the Hanafi position; other schools may use different methods.
3
Classify the type of doubt
The text teaches that doubt (shakk) is of three kinds: (1) doubt on an originally prohibited matter, (2) doubt on an originally permissible matter, (3) doubt with unknown origin. Identify which category a given case falls into.
Each type has a default ruling: prohibition, permissibility, or general permissibility with dislike.
4
Determine the outcome based on the original ruling
For each type, state the ruling: for type 1, the object remains prohibited unless the doubt is resolved by predominant opinion (ghalaba); for type 2, it remains permissible; for type 3, the transaction is permissible but makruh.
Exception: if the majority of the population is Muslim, meat is halal (ghalaba overrides the original prohibition).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالتحري، بدليل أنه لو صلى فيه بالتحري، ثم تبين أنه نجس، يعيد الصلاة، فمتى جعلناه طاهراً بالاجتهاد للضرورة، لا يجوز جعله نجساً باجتهاد مثله، فإن تيقن أن ثوب الظهر كان نجساً، أعاد الظهر وأجزأته العصر، كذا في « الوجيز » . وكذلك إن صلى بأحدهما الظهر وبالآخر العصر، ثم بالأول المغرب، وبالثاني العشاء، فالظهر والمغرب جائزان والعصر والعشاء فاسدان، وعلى هذا كل ما صلي في الثوب الأول جازت صلاته، وما صلي بالثاني لم تجز كذا في «مجمع الروايات»، وإذا تحرى في الأواني التي أكثرها طاهراً، والثياب مطلقاً، ثم ظهر أنه أخطأ، تجب الإعادة، كما في «البرهان»، ولو أخبره عدل، أن هذا اللحم ذبيحة مجوسي أو ميتة، وعدل آخر أنه ذبيحة مسلم، فإنه لا يحل له، لأنه لما تهاتر الخبران بقي على الحرمة الأصلية؛ لأنه لا يحل إلا بالذكاة الشرعية، ولو أخبرا عن ماء وتهاترا بقي على الطهارة الأصلية، كما تقدم.
(1) أي: تساقطهما لاستوائهما في الصدق. ط. وفي معجم لغة الفقهاء، التهاتر : السقط من الكلام والخطأ فيه، وتهاتر القوم: ادعى كل منهم على صاحبه باطلا.
[ تنبيه ]: مثل تعارض الخبرين الشك، وقالوا: إن الشك على ثلاثة أضرب: شك طرأ على أصل حرام. وشك طرأ على أصل مباح، وشك لا يعرف أصله. فالأول: مثل أن يجد شاة مذبوحة في بلد فيها مسلمون ومجوس، فلا تحل حتى يعلم أنها ذكاة مسلم، لأن الأصل فيها الحرمة، إذاً حل الأكل يتوقف على تحقق الذكاة الشرعية فصار حل الأكل مشكوكاً، فلو كان الغالب فيها المسلمين جاز الأكل عملاً بالغالب المفيد للحل.
والثاني: أن يجد ماء متغيراً واحتمل أن يكون تغيره بنجاسة أو طول مكث يجوز التطهير به عملاً بأصل الطهارة. والثالث: مثل معاملة من أكثر ماله حرام لا تحرم مبايعته، حيث لم يتحقق حرمة ما أخذه منه، ولكن يكره خوفاً من الوقوع في الحرام. ط.
(2) الذكاة: الذبح أو النحر بشروطه الشرعية. معجم لغة الفقهاء / ذكاة /.
By investigation (taharrī), evidenced by the fact that if one prays in it by investigation and then it becomes clear that it was impure, he must repeat the prayer. So when we consider it pure by ijtihad out of necessity, it is not permissible to consider it impure by a similar ijtihad. If he is certain that the garment of Zuhr was impure, he repeats Zuhr and his Asr is valid. Likewise, if he prays Zuhr in one of them and Asr in the other, then Maghrib in the first and Isha in the second, Zuhr and Maghrib are valid, while Asr and Isha are invalid. On this basis, every prayer performed in the first garment is valid, and what is performed in the second is not valid. This is in Majma' al-Riwayat. If he investigates regarding vessels, the majority of which are pure, and regarding garments absolutely, then it becomes apparent that he was mistaken, repetition is obligatory, as in al-Burhan. If a trustworthy person informs him that this meat is the slaughter of a Magian or carrion, and another trustworthy person informs him that it is the slaughter of a Muslim, then it is not permissible for him, because when the two reports cancel each other out, it remains upon the original prohibition, since it is not permissible except by legal slaughter. If the two report about water and cancel each other out, it remains upon the original purity, as previously.
(1) That is, their mutual cancellation due to equality in truthfulness. In the dictionary of jurists, al-tahātur means falling from speech and error therein.
[Note]: The analogy of conflicting reports is doubt. They said: Doubt is of three types: doubt that arises upon an originally prohibited matter, doubt that arises upon an originally permissible matter, and doubt whose origin is unknown. The first: like finding a slaughtered sheep in a land where there are both Muslims and Magians; it is not permissible until one knows that it is the slaughter of a Muslim, because the original ruling is prohibition. Thus, the permissibility of eating depends on the verification of legal slaughter, so permissibility becomes doubtful. If the majority of the people are Muslims, eating is permissible based on the predominant (ghalaba) that indicates permissibility.
The second: like finding water that has changed and it is possible that its change is due to impurity or prolonged standing; it is permissible to perform purification with it based on the original ruling of purity.
The third: like dealing with someone most of whose wealth is unlawful; he is not forbidden from selling to him, because the impermissibility of what he has taken is not verified, but it is disliked out of fear of falling into the unlawful.
(2) Al-Dhakāt: slaughter or nahr with its legal conditions.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the commentary on Nur al-Idah, explaining the legal effect of conflicting reports (ta'adul al-khabarayn) and the categories of doubt (shakk). The author begins by discussing the ruling on prayer performed with investigation (taharrī) into the state of a garment: if one prays after investigation and later discovers the garment was impure, the prayer must be repeated. This establishes that the investigation does not change the reality; it only allows a temporary dispensation. Then he gives an example with two garments and multiple prayers to illustrate which prayers are valid and which are invalid. The key principle is that when two reliable witnesses give contradictory reports, the original ruling (asl) prevails. If both report about meat, the original prohibition remains, so the meat is not permissible. If both report about water, the original purity remains, so the water is pure. In all cases, the original state is given precedence (istishab). This is followed by a useful note (tanbīh) that classifies doubt into three types: (1) doubt arising on an originally prohibited basis (e.g., finding meat in a mixed population), where the original prohibition prevents permissibility unless the doubt is resolved by predominant opinion; (2) doubt arising on an originally permissible basis (e.g., water that may have changed due to impurity or age), where the original purity allows use; (3) doubt with no known origin (e.g., dealing with someone of doubtful wealth), where the transaction is permissible but disliked. The Hanafi view relies on the principle of istishab (presumption of continuity) and the use of predominant opinion (ghalaba) when necessary. The concept of tahatur (mutual cancellation) is defined in a footnote: when two reports are equally credible, they cancel each other out, and the original ruling remains.

Key Terms
التهاتر (al-tahātur): Mutual cancellation of two reports when they are equal in credibility; neither takes precedence.
الذكاة (al-dhakāt): Legal slaughter or nahr with its conditions, making meat permissible.
التحري (al-taharrī): Making the best effort to determine the correct ruling or state when the truth is unknown, often due to conflicting evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in the passage, if two trustworthy witnesses give conflicting reports about water (one says pure, one says impure), what is the status of the water?
A) The water is considered impure because of doubt.
B) The water remains on its original ruling of purity.
C) One must investigate until the truth is known.
D) The water is pure only if the majority of people are Muslims.

Key Takeaway
When two equally credible reports cancel out (tahatur), the original legal state prevails (istishab) – this is the Hanafi default for resolving conflicting evidence.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Causes Requiring Draining a Small Well
Listing impurities and animals that require draining a small well

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five causes that obligate draining a small well in the Hanafi school and explain the consensus-based proof for the human death case.

Core Idea
A small well must be drained when any impurity (except small dung) falls in, or when certain animals die or bloat.

This passage from the Sharh of Nur al-Idah opens the chapter on wells by enumerating the specific events that make the water of a small well impure such that draining becomes obligatory. Understanding these causes is essential for maintaining taharah in daily water use, especially in rural or well-dependent settings. The author grounds the ruling in transmitted reports (athar) and cites the famous incident of the Zamzam well as evidence for the case of a human death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
The core ruling is that draining (nazh) is obligatory for a small well. First, note what a 'small well' is: one whose dimensions are less than 10 x 10 cubits (approx. 5m x 5m).
The definition is important because different rules may apply to larger wells.
2
List the five causes for draining
From the matn (the base text): (1) any impurity other than dung, even a tiny amount; (2) a pig falling in, even if it escapes alive without touching water; (3) death of a dog in the well; (4) death of a sheep or human; (5) bloating of any animal, even a small one.
Each cause has its own rationale; note that for dogs it is only death, not just falling in alive.
3
Distinguish the special case of dung
The passage explicitly excludes dung (arwath) from the 'any impurity' category. Dung only renders the water impure if it is a large amount. All other impurities, like blood or wine, cause impurity even in the smallest quantity.
This is a distinctive Hanafi position – other schools may treat dung as heavy impurity.
4
Analyze the dalil for human death
The proof is the hadith of al-Tahawi: a black man fell into the Zamzam well and died. Ibn Abbas and Ibn al-Zubayr ordered the well drained. Many Companions were present and no one objected, thus establishing consensus (ijma). This proof shows that the ruling is based on authoritative transmitted precedent, not mere opinion.
The hadith is cited as 'qati' in both transmission and meaning, making the ruling strong.
5
Understand the bloating case
Bloating of an animal causes the well to be drained because the moisture (bulla) spreads throughout the water, contaminating it. This applies even to tiny animals like chicks.
The commentary explains that the bloating itself causes physical contamination regardless of death.

Source Text
