فصل في مسائل الآبار
تُنْزَحُ البئرُ الصَّغيرَةُ بِوُقُوع نَجَاسَةِ - وَإِنْ قَلَتْ مِنْ غيرِ الأَرْوَاتِ: كَفَطْرَةِ دَمَ، أَوْ خَمْرٍ وَبِوُقُوعِ خِنْزِيرٍ، وَلَوْ خَرَجَ حَيًا، وَلَمْ يُصِبْ فَمُهُ المَاءَ، وَمَوْتِ كَلْبٍ، أَوْ شَاةٍ، أَوْ آدَمِي فِيهَا، وَبِالْتَفَاخِ حيوان، وَلَوْ صَغيرًا.

فصل في مسائل الآبار
ومسائلها مبنية على اتباع الآثار، وحاصل الأمر أن الواقع في البئر، إما أن يكون من غير نجاسة الأرواث، أو منها، أو حيواناً فغير الأرواث منجس وإن قل، والأرواث ينجس كثيرهـا فقـط، والحيوان منجس، لكنه يتفاوت مقدار ما ينزح به، وشرع في بيانه فقال: (تُنْزَحُ الْبِئْرُ الصَّغيرَةُ)، وهي التي لا تبلغ عشراً في عشر، (بِوُقُوعِ نَجَاسَةٍ وَإِنْ قَلَتْ مِنْ غَيْرِ الأَرْوَاثِ كَفَطْرَةِ دَمٍ، أو خَمْرٍ) لأن القليل من النجاسة ينجس القليل من الماء، وإن لم يظهر أثره فيه، (و) تنزح (بِوُقُوعِ خِنْزِيرٍ، وَلَوْ خَرَجَ حَيًا، وَلَمْ يُصِبْ فَمُهُ المَاءَ) لنجاسة عينه، (وَ) تنزح بِمَوْتِ كَلْبٍ قَيَّدَ بِمَوْتِهِ، لأنـه غَيْرُ نَجِسِ الْعَيْنِ، عَلَى الصَّحيحِ، فَإِذَا خَرَجَ حَيًا، وَلَمْ يُصِبْ فَمُهُ المَاءَ، لا يَنْجِسُ، (أَوْ) مَوْتِ (شَاةٍ، أَوْ) مَوْتِ (آدَمِي فِيهَا) لِمَا رَوَى الطَّحَاوِي «أَنَّ زِنْجِيًّا وَقَعَ فِي بِئْرِ زَمْزَمَ، فَمَاتَ، فَأَمَرَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ وَابْنُ الزُّبَيْرِ بِهِ فَأُخْرِجَ، وَأَمَرَا بِأَنْ تُنْزَحَ». قالَ: فَغَلَبَتْهُمْ عَيْنٌ جَاءَتْ مِنَ الرُّكْنِ، فَأَمَرَ بِهَا فَسُدَّتْ بِالقَبَاطِي وَالمَطارِفِ حَتَّى نَزَحُوهَا، فَلَمَّا نَزَحُوهَا، انْفَجَرَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ). والصحابة متوافرون من غير نكير، فكان إجماعاً. والشاة ونحوها كالآدمي. (و) تنزح (بِانْتِفَاخِ حيوان)، وَلَوْ صَغِيراً لانتشار البلة في أجزاء الماء.
(1) نزح البئر : فرغها من الماء ولا يضر بقاء شيء قليل منه فيها. معجم لغة الفقهاء / نزح /.
(2) قصداً للمبالغة في إخراج جميع الماء. ط.
(3) لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِنَّهُ رِجْسٌ﴾ [الأنعام: 145].
(4) القبطية: ثياب كتان بيض رقاق تعمل بمصر. اللسان / قبط /.
(5) المطرف: رداء أو ثوب من خَز مربع ذو أعلام، المعجم الوسيط / طرف /.
(6) أخرجه الدار قطني في سننه، (33/1)، والبيهقي في سننه (268/1).
(7) بعد إخراج الواقع إلا إذا تعذر كخشبة، أو خرقة متنجسة هذا التعذر يكون في صورة كون البئر ذا عين لا يمكن إخراج الماء إلا بالتقدير الشرعي، وإما إذا كان غير ذي عين فلا بد من إخراجه. حاشية ابن عابدين (142/1).
(8) أي: الدموي غير مائي وكذا لو تفسخ أو تمعط شعره أو ريشه. ط.
Chapter on Matters of Wells
[A small well is drained by the occurrence of impurity - even if little - from other than dung: like a drop of blood, or wine, and by the occurrence of a pig, even if it comes out alive and its mouth does not touch the water, and the death of a dog, or a sheep, or a human in it, and by the bloating of an animal, even if small.

Chapter on Matters of Wells
And its matters are based on following the transmitted reports (athar). The gist is that what falls into the well is either from other than impurity of dung, or from it, or an animal. So other than dung is impurity, even if little; dung renders impure only if it is much; an animal is impurity, but the amount to be drained varies. And he began explaining it: The small well is drained, which is one that does not reach ten cubits by ten cubits, by the occurrence of an impurity, even if little, from other than dung, like a drop of blood or wine, because a small amount of impurity contaminates a small amount of water, even if its effect is not visible in it. And it is drained by the occurrence of a pig, even if it comes out alive and its mouth does not touch the water, because its substance is impure. And it is drained by the death of a dog, conditioned by its death, because it is not impure in substance according to the correct view; if it comes out alive and its mouth does not touch the water, it does not render impure. Or the death of a sheep, or the death of a human in it, because al-Tahawi narrated that a black man fell into the well of Zamzam and died, so Ibn Abbas and Ibn al-Zubayr ordered his removal and ordered that the well be drained. The narrator said: A spring from the corner overcame them, so he ordered that it be blocked with Qibati garments and Mutarraf until they drained it. When they drained it, it gushed forth upon them. And the Companions were numerous without objection, so it was consensus. And a sheep and the like are like a human. And it is drained by the bloating of an animal, even if small, because of the spread of moisture in the parts of the water.
[Footnotes: definitions, Quran verse, hadith source, and additional details.]
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the commentary on Nur al-Idah, opening the chapter on wells (masā'il al-ābār). The author first gives a concise summary of when a small well must be drained (nazh): when any impurity other than dung falls in (even a small amount like a drop of blood or wine), when a pig falls in (even if alive and its mouth does not touch the water), when a dog, sheep, or human dies in it, and when an animal bloats in it (even if small). The commentary then expands, stating that the rulings are based on transmitted reports (athar). It distinguishes between three types of falling objects: (1) impurities other than dung—these always render the water impure even in small amounts; (2) dung of animals—only a large amount renders the water impure; (3) animals—they render impure by falling dead or alive (for pigs) or by death (for dogs, sheep, humans). The evidence for the human case is a hadith reported by al-Tahawi about a man falling into the well of Zamzam; the Companions ordered the well to be drained, and this was done in the presence of many Companions without objection, establishing consensus (ijma). The commentary also notes that a small well is defined as less than 10×10 cubits, and that the amount of water to be drained varies based on the case. The passage also explains that a dog is not impure in substance when alive, so its death is what triggers draining; for pigs, even living they are impure in substance (citing Quran 6:145). The bloating of an animal is mentioned because it causes physical contamination. The overall approach is to follow the transmitted precedent (athar) rather than mere opinion.

Key Terms
تنزح (tunzah): She is drained; the well's water is completely removed except for a very small residual amount that does not spoil purity.
الأرواث (al-arthā): Dung of animals; only a large amount of it nullifies the purity of well water.
البئر الصغيرة (al-bi'r al-saghirah): A small well: its dimensions are less than 10 cubits × 10 cubits (approx. 5m × 5m).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A small well has a drop of wine fall into it. According to the passage, what is the ruling?
A) The well is not affected because a drop is negligible.
B) The well must be drained because wine is an impurity and even a small amount contaminates.
C) The well must be drained only if the wine is more than a drop.
D) The well must be drained but only if the wine changes its colour or taste.

Key Takeaway
For a small well, draining is wajib upon any non-dung impurity, a pig (alive or dead), death of a dog/sheep/human, or bloating of any animal; dung only matters in large amounts.

Rulings for Draining a Small Well When Impurities Fall In
States rulings for draining a small well when impurities fall in

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for draining a small well based on the type of impurity (non-dung, dung, animal) and apply the Hanafi proofs to determine the required action.

Core Idea
The small well must be drained completely for any impurity except dung, which only requires drainage for large amounts.

This lesson covers the Hanafi rulings for purifying a small well when various impurities fall into it. The key is classifying the impurity: non-dung (like blood, wine) impurifies even in tiny amounts; dung only in large quantities; and animals when they die or bloat. Understanding these distinctions is essential for proper taharah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the impurity type
Determine whether the substance is non-dung (e.g., blood, wine), dung (animal droppings/urine), or an animal (pig, dog, sheep, human).
Non-dung includes any impurity that is not animal dung/urine.
2
Check if the well is small
A small well is defined as one whose dimensions are less than ten cubits by ten cubits. Only small wells require complete drainage.
If the well is large, different rules apply.
3
Apply the drainage rule for non-dung impurities
For any non-dung impurity, even a tiny amount (e.g., a drop of blood) makes the well impure and requires complete drainage.
This is because a little impurity makes little water impure even if the effect is not visible.
4
Apply the rule for dung
Dung (arwath) impurifies only in large quantities. If a small amount falls, no drainage is required.
The definition of 'large' is a matter of scholarly discussion but generally means a significant amount.
5
Apply the rule for animals
Pigs always require drainage (even if alive and mouth not touching water). Dogs require drainage only if they die. Sheep and humans require drainage upon death. Any bloat (swelling) of an animal also requires drainage.
The proof for humans/sheep is the incident of Zamzam well and the consensus of the Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في مسائل الآبار ومسائلها مبنية على اتباع الآثار، وحاصل الأمر أن الواقع في البئر، إما أن يكون من غير نجاسة الأرواث، أو منها، أو حيواناً فغير الأرواث منجس وإن قل، والأرواث ينجس كثيرهـا فقـط، والحيوان منجس، لكنه يتفاوت مقدار ما ينزح به، وشرع في بيانه فقال: (تُنْزَحُ البِئْرُ الصَّغيرَةُ)، وهي التي لا تبلغ عشراً في عشر، (بوُقُوعِ نَجَاسَةٍ وإِنْ قَلَتْ مِنْ غيرِ الأَرْوَاثِ كَفَطْرَةِ دَمٍ، أو خمر) لأن القليل من النجاسة ينجس القليل من الماء، وإن لم يظهر أثره فيه، (و) تنزح (بوقوعِ خِنْزِيرٍ، وَلَوْ خَرَجَ حِيا، ولم يُصِبْ فمُهُ المَاءَ) لنجاسة عينه، (وَ) تنزح بِمَوْتِ كَلْبِ قيَّد بموته، لأنـه غـيـر نجـس الـعـيـن، على الصحيح، فإذا خرج حياً، ولم يصب فمه الماء، لا ينجس، (أو) موت (شَاةٍ، أو) موت (آدمِي فِيهَا) لما روى الطحاوي أنَّ زنجياً وَقَعَ فِي بِئْرِ زمزم، فمات، فأمر ابن عباس وابن الزبير به فأخرج، وأمرا بها أنْ تنزح. قالَ: فغلبتْهُم عين جَاءتْ مِنَ الركن، فأمرَ بِهَا فسدت بالقباطي والمطارف حتى نزحوهَا، فلما نزحوهَا، انفجرت عليهم، والصحابة متوافرون من غير نكير، فكان إجماعاً. والشاة ونحوها كالآدمي. (و) تنزح (بانتفاخ حيوان)، ولَوْ صَغيراً لانتشار البلة في أجزاء الماء.
Chapter on matters of wells. Their matters are based on following traditions. The sum of the matter is that what falls into the well is either from other than the impurity of dung, or from dung, or an animal. So other than dung is impurifying even if little, and dung impurifies only its large amount, and an animal is impurifying, but the quantity to be drained varies. He began explaining it, saying: 'The small well is drained' - and it is that which does not reach ten by ten cubits - 'by the falling of impurity, even if little, from other than dung, like a drop of blood, or wine' because a little impurity makes little water impure even if its effect does not appear. 'And it is drained by the fall of a pig, even if it comes out alive and its mouth did not touch the water' due to the impurity of its substance. 'And it is drained by the death of a dog' - restricted to its death because it is not impure in substance according to the correct view; if it comes out alive and its mouth did not touch the water, it does not make impure. 'Or the death of a sheep, or the death of a human in it' due to what al-Tahawi narrated: that a Zanjī fell into the well of Zamzam and died, so Ibn Abbas and Ibn al-Zubayr ordered him to be taken out and ordered the well to be drained. He said: 'A water vein from the corner overcame them, so he ordered it to be dammed with qibati clothes and multifari until they drained it. When they drained it, it burst upon them.' And the Companions were many without any denial, so it was consensus. The sheep and the like are like the human. 'And it is drained by the bloating of an animal', even if small, due to the spread of moisture in the parts of the water.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof. The author begins by stating the foundational principle for well purification: the type of substance falling into the well determines whether and how much water must be drained. Non-dung impurities (like blood, wine) are impurifying even in small amounts. Dung (like urine and droppings) only impurifies in large quantities. Animals are impurifying when they die or become bloated, but the amount of water to be drained varies. The text then clarifies the ruling for the 'small well' (less than 10x10 cubits). It must be drained completely if any non-dung impurity falls in, even a drop. For a pig, even if it climbs out alive without its mouth touching the water, the well is impure because the pig's whole body is ritually impure (najis al-ayn). For a dog, only death necessitates drainage because a live dog is not impure in substance according to the correct Hanafi view. For a sheep or human, death in the well requires complete drainage, based on the incident of the Zamzam well reported by al-Tahawi. The actions of Ibn Abbas and Ibn al-Zubayr with no opposition from other Companions constitute consensus (ijma'). Finally, if any animal swells (bloats) in the well, drainage is required even if the animal is small, as swelling indicates decomposition spreading impurity throughout the water.

Key Terms
البئر الصغيرة (al-bi'r al-saghirah): A well that does not measure ten cubits by ten cubits.
نزح (nazh): Draining or removing water from a well.
أرواث (arwath): Dung or droppings of animals (e.g., cow, sheep) and also urine.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The well becomes impure but only ten buckets need to be drawn.

Key Takeaway
For a small well, any non-dung impurity, any pig (alive or dead), death of a dog/sheep/human, or bloated animal requires complete drainage; dung requires drainage only in large amounts.

The 200 Bucket Ruling and Purification Dispute
Specifies the quantity of 200 buckets when the well cannot be fully drained, with ikhtilaf on purification moment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on draining a well when total drainage is impossible, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on the moment of purification.

Core Idea
When a well cannot be fully drained, 200 buckets are wajib; purification occurs when the last bucket leaves the well.

This passage addresses the common scenario where a well's water source is too strong to allow complete drainage. It establishes the obligation to draw 200 buckets (with the middle bucket) and presents a key intra-Hanafi dispute: when exactly does the water become pure? You will learn the majority view and its practical implications for daily acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the legal act: draining a well when completely emptying it is impossible. The hukm is wajib to draw 200 buckets using the middle bucket (the most commonly used bucket in that well).
2
Understand the definition of the middle bucket
The text gives several interpretations: most used in that well (zahir al-riwayah), the bucket that is moderate, or by custom of the land. The key is that the bucket size should make the obligation manageable.
Also note that using one huge bucket equivalent to 200 medium buckets suffices.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on purification moment
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: the well becomes pure when the last bucket is completely separated from the well. Muhammad: pure when the last bucket separates from the water, even if it drips back. Understand each proof and the practical consequence.
Dripping after separation: Muhammad disregards; Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf require full separation.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf due to caution—complete detachment from the well is required. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
The author sides with them, implying this view is stronger.
5
Apply the principle of expert estimation
If the original quantity of water in the well is unknown, two experienced men (male Muslims, as per shahada requirements) should estimate it. This reflects the Sharia principle of relying on experts.
Quranic reference: 'So ask the people of the reminder if you do not know.' (16:43)

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) تنزح وجوباً (مائتا دلو). ويستحب الزيادة إلى ثلاثمائة، ولو بالدلو الوسط، وهو: ما أكثر استعماله في تلك البئر، وهو ظاهر الرواية، وقيل ما يستعمل في كل بلد لأنه ذو حظ من الجانبين، إذ هو أكبر من الصغير، كما أن الكبير أكبر منه، وهو أصغر من الكبير، كما أن الصغير أصغر منه فيكون عدلاً. وقيل: يعتبر بالصاع)، وهو رواية الحسن عن الإمام وقيل: يعتبر في كـل بـلـد دولـهـا لإطلاق السلف، فينصرف إلى المعتاد، ولأنه أيسر عليهم. ولو نزح بدلو عظيـم مــرة بقدر الواجب، كفي لحصول المقصود، وهو تمييز النجس عن الطاهر شرعاً، وكذا لو نزح الواجب في أيام، أو غسل الثوب النجس في أيام طهر، وإذا انفصل الدلو الأخير عن البئر، طهرت عند أبي جنيفة وأبـي يوسف رحمهما الله، وقال محمد رحمه الله: تطهر بانفصال الدلو الأخير عن الماء، ولو قطر في البئر، لأن التقاطر ضروري، فلا يعتبر. وقالا بعده، لأن دليل الاتصال باق من وجه، فيشترط كمال الانفصال، وقدر الواجب بمائتي دلو (لَوْ لَمْ يُمْكِنْ نَزْحُها) محمد رحمه الله أفتـى بـمـا شــاهد في بغداد، لأن آبارها كثيرة الماء لمجاورتها دجلة، وفي ( الجامع الصغير) عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله : ينزح حتى يغلبهم الماء، ولم يقدر الغلبة بشيء كما هو دأبه. وقال «قاضي خان»: الأصح في تفسير الغلبة العجز. وقال غيره: يعتبر غلبة الظن لا غير. وفي [ غير ] رواية الأصول، أنه ينزح مائة دلو. والأشبه بالفقيه أن يقدر ما كان في البئر وقت الوقوع، بقول رجلين لهمـا خـبـرة بـأمـر المـاء، وهـو الأصح، لكونهما نصاب الشهادة، والرجوع إلى أهل البصر أصل في كثير من الأحكام، كالحكمين في تقويم المتلف. وقال تعالى: ﴿فَتَلُوا أَهْلَ الذِكرِ إِن كُنتُمْ لَا تَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ [النحل: ٤٣]. وهو مروي عن أبي نصر «محمد بن سلام رحمه الله.
And it is drained obligatorily two hundred buckets. It is recommended to increase to three hundred, and that is with the middle bucket, which is what is most used in that well, and that is the apparent narration. And it was said: what is used in every land because it has portion from both sides, as it is larger than the small, just as the large is larger than it, and it is smaller than the large, just as the small is smaller than it, so it is moderate. And it was said: it is considered by the sa', and that is a narration of al-Hasan from the Imam. And it was said: in every land their own bucket because of the unrestricted application of the predecessors, so it refers to the customary, and because it is easier for them. And if he drains with a huge bucket once equivalent to the obligated amount, it suffices due to achieving the goal, which is distinguishing the impure from the pure legally. Similarly, if he drains the obligated amount over days, or washes an impure garment over days, it becomes pure. And when the last bucket separates from the well, it becomes pure according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on them. And Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, said: it becomes pure with the separation of the last bucket from the water, even if it drips into the well, because dripping is unavoidable, so it is not considered. And they (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) said after him: because the evidence of connection remains in some respect, so complete separation is required. And the obligated amount is two hundred buckets if it is not possible to drain it completely. Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, gave a fatwa based on what he witnessed in Baghdad, because its wells are abundant in water due to their proximity to the Tigris. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him: he drains until the water overcomes them, and he did not define 'overcome' with anything, as is his practice. And Qadi Khan said: the soundest in interpretation of 'overcome' is inability. And others said: only the prevailing of opinion is considered. And according to a non-essential narration, he drains one hundred buckets. And the most befitting for a jurist is to estimate what was in the well at the time of occurrence by the statement of two men who have experience with water matter, and that is the soundest, because they constitute the full number for testimony, and referring to experts is a principle in many rulings, like the two arbitrators in evaluating damaged property. And Allah Most High said: 'So ask the people of the reminder if you do not know.' And this is narrated from Abu Nasr Muhammad ibn Salam, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof and includes an intra-Hanafi dispute. The author specifies that if a well cannot be fully drained (e.g., due to a strong water source), the obligation is to draw 200 buckets using the 'middle bucket'—the one commonly used in that well. Various opinions exist on defining the bucket (e.g., by sa' measurement, by local custom). The key ruling: if one uses a very large bucket equal to 200 medium buckets, once suffices. The time of purification is a point of ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say the well becomes pure when the last bucket is separated from the well (i.e., fully extracted); Muhammad al-Shaybani says it becomes pure when the last bucket separates from the water (even if it drips back). The majority Hanafi view (mufta bihi) follows the two elders. For wells where total drainage is impossible, Muhammad gave a pragmatic ruling based on Baghdad's wells. Abu Hanifa's general principle is to drain until one is overpowered (ghalabah), which Qadi Khan interprets as inability. The preferred method for determining the quantity originally in the well is to rely on two experienced witnesses, analogous to the principle of referring to experts in Islamic law. The verse from Surah al-Nahl is cited in support.

Key Terms
الدلو الوسط (al-dalu al-wasat): The middle-sized bucket commonly used in a particular well.
الغلبة (al-ghalabah): Being overwhelmed by water such that one cannot continue draining.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, when does a well become pure after drawing the required number of buckets?
A) When the last bucket separates from the water, even if it drips back.
B) When the last bucket is completely separated from the well.
C) When 200 buckets have been drawn, regardless of separation.
D) Only when the well is completely dry.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a well cannot be fully drained, drawing 200 buckets (or equivalent) is wajib, and the water becomes pure only when the last bucket is completely separated from the well.

Forty Buckets for Small Animals in a Well
Specifies the requirement of 40 buckets for chicken, cat, and similar animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required number of buckets for a chicken, cat, or similarly sized animal dying in a well without bloating, and cite the proof from early authorities.

Core Idea
A chicken-sized animal requires exactly 40 buckets — no more, no less, unless bloated.

In the previous lesson, we learned the general rule for well purification. Now we encounter specific quantities for small animals. This passage establishes forty buckets as the wajib minimum, supported by multiple early narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act? A chicken, cat, or similar animal dies in a well without bloating. The ruling: wajib to draw 40 buckets after removing the dead animal.
Bloating changes the ruling to complete drainage.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof comes from narrations of companions and successors: Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, al-Sha'bi, al-Nakha'i, 'Ata, and Hammad all state 40 buckets for such animals.
These narrations are considered zanni al-thubut but collectively strong.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit statement of forty buckets from multiple early authorities establishes the required quantity. The text does not give a rationale, but it is taken as a fixed quantity.
Any animal with similar body mass shares the ruling.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may have different quantities (e.g., Shafi'is may require complete drainage for any carcass). However, Hanafis rely on these specific narrations.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different proofs.
5
Evaluate the practical scope
The ruling applies only to non-bloated, medium-sized animals (chicken, cat, bird, rat). Larger animals such as a dog or goat require complete drainage, even without bloating.
The key variable is body size relative to a chicken.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنْ مَاتَ فِيهَا دجاجة، أو هرةٌ، أَوْ نَحْوُهُما) في الجثة، ولم تنتفخ (لَزِمَ نَزْحُ أربَعينَ دَلْوَاً) بعد إخراج الواقع منها. روي التقدير بالأربعين عن أبي سعيد الخدري في الدجاجة، وما قاربها يأخذ حكمها. وروى الطحاوي عن الشعبي في الطير والسنور، ونحوهما يقع في البئر، قال: ينزح منها أربعون دلواً). وعن النخعي في السنور والجرذون مثله. وروى ابن أبي شيبة عن عطاء، كما روى الطحاوي عن حماد، وتستحب الزيادة على الأربعين
And if a chicken, or a cat, or the like of them dies in it (the well) in terms of body size, and did not bloat, then drawing forty buckets is incumbent after removing the fallen thing from it. The estimation of forty is narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri concerning a chicken, and what approximates it takes its ruling. And al-Tahawi narrated from al-Sha'bi concerning a bird and a cat, and the like of them falling into a well, he said: draw from it forty buckets. And from al-Nakha'i concerning a cat and a rat, similar. And Ibn Abi Shayba narrated from 'Ata, as al-Tahawi narrated from Hammad, and it is recommended to increase beyond forty.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof specifying the quantity of water to be drawn when a chicken, cat, or similarly sized animal dies in a well without bloating. The required amount is forty buckets after removing the dead animal. This is based on narrations from companions and successors: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri for a chicken, from al-Sha'bi for birds and cats, and from al-Nakha'i for cats and rats. The principle is that animals with similar body mass take the same ruling. It is recommended (mustahabb) to add extra buckets for thorough purification. This ruling applies specifically when the animal has not bloated; if bloated, the well would require complete drainage according to earlier rules. The evidence is from the practice of early Muslims, which is considered a form of ijma' or at least strong transmission.

Key Terms
دجاجة (dajajah): Chicken; used as a benchmark for similar-sized animals.
هرة (hirah): Cat; included as another example of a small animal.
أربعون دلواً (arba'una dalwan): Forty buckets; the minimum required quantity for such animals.
نحوهما (nahwuhuma): Similar to them (the chicken and cat) in body mass.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Complete drainage of the well
B) 200 buckets
C) 40 buckets
D) 20 buckets

Key Takeaway
For any animal similar in size to a chicken that dies in a well without bloating, forty buckets must be drawn after removing the carcass.

Taharah — Purification

Well Purification After Animal Death: Obligatory Bucketfuls and Disputes
Prescribes required bucketfuls for various animals and conditions for well purity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligatory bucketfuls for a chicken/cat, mouse, and large animal, and explain the Hanafi dispute on when the well becomes pure.

Core Idea
The amount of water to draw depends on the animal's size, with two hundred for large, forty for medium, twenty for small.

When an animal dies in a well, the water becomes impure and must be removed. The Hanafi school prescribes specific bucketfuls based on the animal's size, supported by ahadith. A key internal dispute exists between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the exact moment the well becomes pure. This lesson will guide you through these rulings and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is required when an animal dies in the well and its legal status (wajib).
The text states the drawing of water is wajib.
2
Note the amounts for different animals
List the required bucketfuls for large animals (200), chicken/cat (40), and mouse (20), using the medium bucket.
The medium bucket is the one most used in that well.
3
Understand the dispute on purity timing
Compare the views of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf (upon separation from the well) and Muhammad (upon separation from the water).
The text implies the first view is relied upon.
4
Apply the rule for dung impurities
Learn that dry animal droppings do not defile the well unless they are so abundant that an observer considers them much.
This criterion is subjective, based on custom.

وإن مات فيها فأرة، أو نحوها، لزمَ نَزْحُ عشرين دلواً. وكان ذلك طهارة للبئر، والدلو، والرشاء، ويدِ المَسْتَقِي ولا تنجس البئرُ بالبَعْرِ، وَالرُّوثِ، والخني إلا أنْ يَستكثرَهُ النَّاظِرُ .
إلى خمسين، لما روي عن عطاء وحماد، أو إلى ستين)، لما روي عن الشعبي والنخعي. (وإن مات فيها ) أي : البئر، (فَأَرَةٌ) بالهمز ، (أو نَحْوُهَا) كعصفور وسام أبرص، ولم تنتفخ الزمَ نَزْحُ عِشْرِينَ دَلْوَا) بعد إخراج الواقع. لقول أنس الله في فأرة ماتت في البئر وأخرجت من ساعته: « يـنـزح

(ولا تَنْجُسُ البئرُ بالبَعْرِ) وهو : للإبل والغنم، وبعر يبعر، من حد منع (والرَّوْثِ) من راث، من حد نصر، وهو : للفرس والبغل والحمار (والخثي) بكسر الخاء، واحد الأخثاء للبقر، من باب ضرب، ولا فرق بـيـن آبـار الأمصار والفلوات ) في الصحيح، ولا فرق في ظاهر الرواية بين الرطب واليابس، والصحيح والمنكسر، في عدم تنجيس البئر بالقليل منها؛ لشمول الضرورة الكل، فلا تنجس بالواقع فيها من ذلك، إلا أن) يكون كثيراً، واختلف في تقدير الكثير على أقوال، منها قولان مصححان، فلذا أقتصر على ذكرهما، صحح في كثير من الكتب المعتمدة، أن الكثير ما (يَستكثرَهُ النَّاظِرُ) والقليـل مـا يستقله، وعليـه الاعتماد، لأن أبا حنيفة، لا يقدر شيئاً بالرأي، في مثل هذه المسائل التي تحتاج إلى التقدير، فكـان
And two hundred bucketfuls. If it is not possible to empty it, and if a chicken or a cat or similar dies in it, it is necessary to draw forty bucketfuls. (And) it is obligatory to draw (two hundred bucketfuls). And it is recommended to increase to three hundred, using the medium bucket, which is the one most used in that well – that is the apparent narration. And it is said: what is used in each country because it partakes of both sides, as it is larger than the small just as the large is larger than it, and it is smaller than the large just as the small is smaller than it, so it is moderate. And it is said: consideration is by the sa' – this is the narration of al-Hasan from the Imam. And it is said: consideration is by the buckets of each land due to the unrestricted usage of the Salaf, so it refers to the customary, and because it is easier for them. If one draws with a huge bucket once the amount of the obligatory required, it suffices because the purpose is achieved, which is distinguishing the impure from the pure legally. Similarly, if one draws the obligatory over days, or washes a impure garment over days and it becomes pure. And when the last bucket separates from the well, it becomes pure according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf – Allah have mercy on them – and Muhammad – Allah have mercy on him – said: It becomes pure when the last bucket separates from the water, even if a drop falls into the well, because dripping is inevitable and so not considered. And the two said: after that, because the evidence of connection remains in some way, so complete separation is required. And the obligatory amount is two hundred bucketfuls. (If it is not possible to empty it): Muhammad – Allah have mercy on him – gave a fatwa based on what he saw in Baghdad, because its wells have much water due to proximity to the Tigris. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir from Abu Hanifa – Allah have mercy on him – he said: Draw until the water overwhelms them, and he did not specify 'overwhelming' with anything, as is his practice. Qadi Khan said: The soundest interpretation of 'overwhelming' is inability. And others said: Consider overwhelming of opinion only. And in a non-authentic narration of the principles, that one draws 100 bucketfuls. The most appropriate for the jurist is to estimate what was in the well at the time of occurrence by the statement of two men who have experience with water – and this is the soundest, because they constitute the quorum for testimony, and referring to experts is a principle in many rulings, like the two arbiters in evaluating damages. And Allah Almighty said: {So ask the people of the reminder if you do not know} [al-Nahl: 43]. And this is narrated from Abu Nasr Muhammad ibn Salam – Allah have mercy on him. (And if a chicken or a cat or something similar in body dies in it) and it has not swollen, (then drawing forty bucketfuls is obligatory) after removing the fallen object. The estimation of forty is related from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri regarding a chicken, and whatever is similar takes its ruling. Al-Tahawi related from al-Sha'bi regarding a bird and a cat and similar falling into a well, he said: Forty bucketfuls are drawn from it. And from al-Nakha'i regarding a cat and a mouse the same. Ibn Abi Shayba related from 'Ata, as al-Tahawi related from Hammad, and the increase beyond forty is recommended up to fifty, due to what is related from 'Ata and Hammad, or up to sixty due to what is related from al-Sha'bi and al-Nakha'i. (And if a mouse dies in it) i.e., the well, (or something like it) such as a sparrow or a gecko, and it has not swollen, (then drawing twenty bucketfuls is obligatory) after removing the fallen object. Because of the saying of Anas – Allah be pleased with him – regarding a mouse that died in a well and was removed immediately: 'Twenty bucketfuls are drawn.' And increase to thirty is recommended, due to the possibility that the bucket mentioned in the tradition is larger than the medium with which it is estimated. (And that drawn water) is a purification for the well, the bucket, the rope, the pulley, and the hand of the drawer – that is related from Abu Yusuf and al-Hasan, because the impurity of these things was due to the impurity of the water, so their purification comes through its purification, in order to avoid hardship, like the purification of a wine jar by its vinegar turning, and the purification of the handle of a jug by purifying the hand when it is taken each time the hand is washed. If two or more mice fall in, from Abu Yusuf: four are like one mouse, five to nine like a chicken, ten like a sheep. Muhammad said: three to five like a cat, six like a dog – and that is the apparent narration. From Muhammad: if two are like a chicken, forty bucketfuls; for two cats, all the water is drawn. Whatever is between a mouse and a cat, its ruling is the ruling of a mouse; whatever is between a cat and a dog, its ruling is the ruling of a cat. If mouse and cat come together, they are like a cat, and the lesser is included in the greater. (The well does not become impure by dung) which is from camels and sheep (and horse dung) from horse, mule, donkey (and cow dung) – singular of cow dung. There is no difference between wells of cities and deserts according to the sound opinion, and no difference in the apparent narration between wet and dry, and between sound and broken, in that the well is not made impure by a small amount of these; because necessity encompasses all. Thus it does not become impure by what falls into it of that, unless it is so much that it is considered much by the observer. And there is disagreement on the estimation of 'much' – among the opinions, two are sound, so we limit to them. It is considered sound in many reliable books that 'much' is what the observer considers much, and 'little' is what he considers little, and that is relied upon, because Abu Hanifa does not estimate anything by opinion in such matters that need estimation.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah, details rulings for purifying a well when an animal dies in it. The text begins by stating the obligatory amount of water to draw for a chicken or cat: 200 bucketfuls. However, an exception is made if the well cannot be emptied due to abundant water – then one estimates based on experts or, in a weaker narration, draws 100 bucketfuls. The medium bucket is defined as the most used bucket in that well. The obligation is fulfilled if the equivalent volume is drawn with a large bucket once or over several days. A key dispute is noted regarding when the well becomes pure: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, it is when the last bucket separates from the well; according to Muhammad, it is when the last bucket separates from the water (even if drips fall back). The text then covers smaller animals: a chicken or cat requires 40 bucketfuls (with recommended increase to 50 or 60), and a mouse or sparrow requires 20 bucketfuls (recommended increase to 30). These amounts are supported by hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri and Anas. The drawn water purifies not only the well but also the bucket, rope, pulley, and hand of the drawer, by extension from the impurity source. For multiple animals, the text provides variations from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: generally, the largest animal's ruling dominates. Finally, the passage explains that dry animal droppings (camel, horse, cow, etc.) do not defile the well unless they are so abundant that an observer considers them 'much.' The criterion of 'much' is subjective, based on the observer's judgment, as Abu Hanifa refrained from arbitrary quantification in such matters.

Key Terms
الرشاء (al-risha'): The rope used to draw water from the well; it becomes impure due to contact with impure water and is purified by the same process.
الوسط (al-wasat): The medium-sized bucket, taken as the standard for measuring the required number of bucketfuls; defined as the most commonly used bucket in that well.
يستكثر الناظر (yastakthiruhu al-nazir): What the observer considers a large amount; used as the criterion for when dung impurities defile the well.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, how many bucketfuls are obligatory when a mouse dies in a well (without swelling)?
A) Forty bucketfuls
B) Twenty bucketfuls
C) Two hundred bucketfuls
D) One hundred bucketfuls

Key Takeaway
The number of bucketfuls required to purify a well after an animal dies depends on the animal's size: 200 for large, 40 for chicken/cat, 20 for mouse, with a reliance on the medium bucket and subjective estimation for dung impurities.

Ruling on a Single Mouse Dying in a Well: 20 Buckets and Purification
States the obligation of drawing 20 buckets when a mouse dies in a well and that it purifies the well and tools.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purifying a well when a mouse dies in it, identify the hadith evidence, and explain the purification of the tools by taba'iyyah.

Core Idea
Twenty buckets purify a well when a mouse dies; obligation is wajib from an ahad hadith.

Imagine a well used for drinking water. A small mouse falls in and dies. How is the well purified? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on a hadith of Anas ibn Malik: drawing twenty buckets of water purifies the well and all utensils used. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the principle of removing hardship that allows purification of tools by taba'iyyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its conditions
The act is the death of a mouse (or similar small animal) in a well. Condition: the animal has not swollen and is removed immediately. Under these conditions, the ruling applies.
Swollen animals require a different ruling.
2
State the obligation: 20 buckets
It is necessary (wajib) to draw twenty buckets of water from the well. This is based on the hadith of Anas.
The number twenty is specific.
3
Identify the dalil and its weight
The proof is the hadith: 'Draw twenty buckets.' This is an ahad hadith, making the ruling wajib, not fard. The imperative indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
The recommendation to increase to thirty is mustahabb, not wajib.
4
Explain the purification of tools by taba'iyyah
The drawn water purifies not only the well but also the bucket, rope, pulley, and hand. Since their impurity was derived from the water, they become pure when the water is purified, to remove hardship. This is analogous to a wine jar becoming pure when the wine turns to vinegar.
This principle is called taharah taba'iyyah (purification by following).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن مات فيها فأرة أو نحوها لم تنتفخ، لزم نزح عشرين دلوا بعد إخراج الواقع. لقول أنس رضي الله عنه في فأرة ماتت في البئر وأخرجت من ساعته: ينزح عشرون دلوا. ويستحب الزيادة إلى ثلاثين دلوا، لاحتمال زيادة الدلو المذكور في الأثر على ما قدر به من الوسط. وكان ذلك طهارة للبئر والدلو والرشاء والبكرة ويد المستقي. روي ذلك عن أبي يوسف والحسن، إذ نجاسة هذه الأشياء كانت لنجاسة الماء، فيكون طهارتها بطهارته، نفيا للحرج، كطهارة دن الخمر بتخليلها وطهارة عروة الإبريق بطهارة اليد، إذا أخذها كلما غسل يده.
And if a mouse or similar dies in it and has not swollen, it is necessary to draw twenty buckets after removing the fallen. Due to the saying of Anas, may Allah be pleased with him, regarding a mouse that died in the well and was taken out immediately: 'Draw twenty buckets.' And it is recommended to increase to thirty buckets, because the bucket mentioned in the tradition may be larger than the medium-sized one estimated. And that (water drawn) is purification for the well, the bucket, the rope, the pulley, and the hand of the drawer. That is reported from Abu Yusuf and al-Hasan, because the impurity of these items was due to the impurity of the water, so their purification is through its purification, to remove hardship, like the purification of a wine jar by turning it into vinegar, and the purification of the handle of a jug by the purification of the hand when one grasps it every time he washes his hand.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the purification of a well when a small animal, like a mouse, dies in it. The obligation is to draw twenty buckets of water after removing the animal, based on a hadith from Anas ibn Malik. It is recommended to draw thirty buckets if the bucket used is of a standard size. The drawn water purifies not only the well but also the bucket, rope, pulley, and the hand of the person drawing water. This is because these items became impure due to contact with the impure water; once the water is purified, they are also purified. This ruling is based on the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj), analogous to the purification of a wine jar by turning wine into vinegar, or the purification of a jug handle by washing one's hand. Note that the ruling applies only if the animal has not swollen and is removed promptly.

Key Terms
نَزْح (nazḥ): Drawing water from a well, especially to remove impurity.
دَلْو (dalw): A bucket used to draw water from a well.
رِشَاء (rishā’): The rope attached to the bucket for drawing water.
طهارة تبعية (taharah taba'iyyah): Purification by following; when the source of impurity is removed, the items that became impure due to it are purified without separate action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The well becomes permanently impure and must be emptied completely.
B) It is obligatory to draw twenty buckets of water, and that purifies the well and tools.
C) It is recommended to draw forty buckets of water.
D) No purification is needed because mice are naturally pure.

Key Takeaway
A single mouse dying in a well without swelling requires wajib drawing of twenty buckets, which purifies the well and all associated tools by the principle of taba'iyyah.

Ruling on Multiple Animals Dying in a Well: Intra-Hanafi Differences
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the amount of water to draw for multiple animals in a well.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the opinions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the required amount of water to draw when multiple animals die in a well and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
The lesser impurity is absorbed into the greater, and the relied-upon opinion is that of Muhammad al-Shaybani (zahir al-riwayah).

When multiple animals die in a well, the required amount of water to draw depends not just on the number but also on the size of the animals. Within the Hanafi school, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani offered different categorizations. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains their differences and identifies which opinion is the authoritative one (zahir al-riwayah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage deals with two or more animals (e.g., mice, cats, chickens, dogs) dying in a well. The key is to determine how much water must be drawn for purification.
The baseline for a single mouse is 20 buckets; for a cat, it is emptying the entire well.
2
State Abu Yusuf's opinion
Abu Yusuf classifies by number: 4 mice = 1 mouse (20 buckets), 5-9 mice = chicken (40 buckets), 10 mice = sheep (full emptying?).
His opinion is based on qiyas but is not the relied-upon view.
3
State Muhammad al-Shaybani's opinion
Muhammad classifies by size: 3-5 mice = cat (empty well), 6 mice = dog (empty well plus special treatment). For mixed animals, the larger governs: a mouse with a cat is treated as a cat.
This is declared the 'zahir al-riwayah' (apparent transmission), thus mufta bihi.
4
Apply the principle of 'lesser included in greater'
When animals of different sizes are present, the ruling follows the larger animal. The smaller's contamination is absorbed.
Example: a cat and a mouse together require emptying the well as per cat.
5
Determine the operative ruling (mufta bihi)
The text explicitly states that Muhammad's opinion is the zahir al-riwayah, making it the authoritative position for fatwa.
Thus, in practice, one follows Muhammad al-Shaybani's classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن وقع فيها فأرتان أو أكثر، فعن أبي يوسف أن الأربع كفارة واحدة، والخمس كالدجاجة إلى التسع، والعشرة كالشاة. وقال محمد: الثلاث إلى الخمس كالهرة، والست كالكلب وهو ظاهر الرواية. وعن محمد، إذا كانتا كهيئة الدجاجة، ينزح أربعون وفي الهرتين ينزح ماؤها كله، وما كان بين الفأرة والهرة، فحكمه حكم الفأرة، وما كان بين الهرة والكلب، فحكمه حكم الهرة، وإن اجتمع الفأرة مع الهرة فهما كالهرة، ويدخل الأقل في الأكثر.
And if two mice or more fall into it, then according to Abu Yusuf: four are like one mouse, five to nine are like a chicken, and ten are like a sheep. And Muhammad said: three to five are like a cat, and six are like a dog, and this is the apparent narration. And from Muhammad: if they are like a chicken, forty buckets are drawn; for two cats, all the water is drawn; and what is between a mouse and a cat, its ruling is the ruling of a mouse; what is between a cat and a dog, its ruling is the ruling of a cat; and if a mouse and a cat come together, they are like a cat, and the lesser is included in the greater.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario when multiple animals, such as mice, cats, chickens, etc., die in a well. There is a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Abu Yusuf categorizes by number: for example, four mice require the same as one mouse (twenty buckets), five to nine like a chicken (forty buckets?), and ten like a sheep (may require full emptying). Muhammad's opinion, which is the 'zahir al-riwayah' (the apparent transmission), classifies by size and type: three to five mice are like a cat (all water drawn?), six are like a dog (all water drawn, and the well must be treated like a dog's contamination). Furthermore, for animals that resemble chickens but are not, or between mouse and cat, the ruling follows the smaller; if a mouse and a cat are together, they are treated as a cat. The principle is that the lesser impurity is absorbed into the greater. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the opinion of Muhammad al-Shaybani, as it is the apparent narration.

Key Terms
فأرة (fa'ra): A mouse or rat; here used as a benchmark for small animals.
هرة (hirra): A cat; used as an intermediate category between mouse and dog.
ظاهر الرواية (zāhir al-riwāya): The apparent or well-known transmission from the early Hanafi masters (the six books of Muhammad).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Two mice
B) Three to five mice
C) Six mice
D) Ten mice

Key Takeaway
When multiple animals die in a well, classify by the largest animal present, and the mufta bihi opinion follows Muhammad al-Shaybani's categorization based on size.

Ruling on Dung Falling into a Well: Small Amounts Do Not Impurify
States that small amounts of camel, horse, or cow dung do not make a well impure unless the amount is considered large

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on animal dung falling into a well, identify the criterion for impurity (kathir), and apply the mufta bihi definition (observer's judgment) to common scenarios.

Core Idea
Small amounts of animal dung do not spoil a well; only if the observer considers it much does the well become impure.

This lesson examines a specific ruling of taharah: how dung from camels, horses, and cows affects the purity of well water. The Hanafi school makes a practical distinction between small and large amounts, relying on the observer's reasonable judgment. Understanding this ruling prevents unnecessary hardship and wasteful water disposal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is dung falling into a well. The default ruling is that the well remains pure (tahir).
2
Define key terms
Know that ba'r (camel/sheep dung), rawth (horse/mule dung), and khathy (cow dung) are all treated similarly.
3
Understand the exception (kathir)
The well becomes impure only if the amount is considered 'much' by a reasonable observer.
This is based on istihsan due to necessity.
4
Explore intra-Hanafi definitions
Review the variant opinions: three pieces, covering a quarter of the surface, every bucket contains dung.
These are not the mufta bihi.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is the observer's judgment, as it avoids arbitrary quantification.
عليه الاعتماد

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تنجس البئر بالبعر والروث والخثي إلا أن يستكثره الناظر. أو أن لا يخلو دلو عن بعرة ونحوها. وهذا رواية عن محمد بن سلمة، وصححها في المبسوط. وعن بعضهم: أن الثلاث كثير. وعن محمد: أنه ما يغطي ربع وجه الماء.
And the well does not become impure by camel/goat dung, horse/mule dung, and cow dung unless the observer considers it much. Or that a bucket is never free of dung or similar. And this is a narration from Muhammad ibn Salama, and it was declared sound in al-Mabsut. And from some: that three (pieces) are much. And from Muhammad: that it covers a quarter of the surface of the water.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage deals with the purity of a well when animal dung (b'air for camels/sheep, rawth for horses/mules, khithy for cows) falls into it. The rule is that small quantities do not affect the purity of the well; it remains pure. Impurity only occurs if the amount is 'much' (kathir), which is defined by the observer's judgment (yastakthiruhu al-nazir). There are other opinions: a narration from Muhammad ibn Salama considers it much if every bucket drawn contains dung; some say three pieces; and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) says if it covers a quarter of the water's surface. The relied-upon definition is the observer's judgment, because Imam Abu Hanifa did not like to specify quantities by opinion in such matters. This reflects the principle of istihsan due to necessity, as wells are frequently exposed to dung.

Key Terms
بَعْر (ba‘r): Dung of camels and sheep/goats.
رَوْث (rawth): Dung of horses, mules, and donkeys.
خَثْي (khathy): Dung of cows.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Only dried dung makes the well impure.
C) Only if the observer considers it to be a large amount (kathir).
D) Only if the dung is from cows.

Key Takeaway
The well remains pure after small amounts of dung; only when an observer deems the amount much does it become impure.

Purity of Edible Bird Droppings: A Ruling by Istihsan
States that droppings of edible birds do not spoil water, with hadith proof and istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the purity of edible bird droppings and identify the evidence (hadith and istihsan) that supports it.

Core Idea
Edible bird droppings are pure by istihsan; the Companions' actions and Prophetic gratitude prove it.

In this lesson, we examine a unique Hanafi ruling: the droppings of edible birds like pigeons and sparrows do not spoil water. This ruling is based on istihsan (juridical preference) and supported by the actions of Companions and a hadith of the Prophet. Understanding this ruling highlights how Hanafi fiqh balances textual evidence with the principle of ease.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? It is the effect of droppings of edible birds (pigeon, sparrow) on water. The ruling: water is not spoiled, indicating the droppings are pure (tahir). Note the exception of chicken and goose.
The exception is notable: chicken and goose droppings are not covered by this ruling; they may be considered impure.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites three pieces of evidence: action of Ibn Mas'ud (wiped droppings with finger), action of Ibn 'Umar (wiped with pebble and prayed without washing), and the hadith of Abu Umama about the Prophet thanking a pigeon.
These are ahad hadith and Companion actions, so thubut and dalala are zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Companions did not wash the affected area, indicating they considered the droppings not impure. The Prophet's gratitude implies the pigeon is honored, and by extension, its droppings are not impure.
This is a qawl sahabi and action, used as evidence for purity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
For non-edible birds, there is difference of correction: some say pure, others say impure but with light impurity (najis mukhaffaf). The text does not firmly settle it.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi for edible birds is clear.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text states that many books have chosen purity (at our school), indicating the preferred view is purity for edible birds. For non-edible, the light impurity view is adopted to avoid hardship.
Tarjih is based on istihsan and ease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يفسد الماء بخرء حمام وعصفور ونحوهما مما يؤكل من الطيور غير الدجاج والإوز، والحكم بطهارته استحسان، لحديث ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه أنه خرئت عليه حمامة فمسحه بأصبعه، وابن عمر ذرق عليه طائر فمسحه بحصاة وصلى ولم يغسله. وأصله حديث أبي أمامة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم شكر الحمامة وقال: إنها أوكرت على باب الغار حتى سلمت فجازاها الله المسجد مأواها. فهو دليل على طهارة ما يكون منها. واختار في كثير من الكتب طهارته عندنا، واختلف التصحيح في طهارة خرء ما لا يؤكل من الطيور، ونجاسته مخففة.
And water is not spoiled by the droppings of a pigeon and sparrow and similar birds that are eaten, except chicken and goose. And the ruling of its purity is based on istihsan, due to the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him, that a pigeon defecated on him and he wiped it with his finger; and Ibn 'Umar, a bird dropped excrement on him and he wiped it with a pebble and prayed without washing it. And its origin is the hadith of Abu Umama that the Prophet, peace be upon him, thanked the pigeon and said: 'It built a nest at the mouth of the cave until I was saved, so Allah compensated it by making the mosque its dwelling.' This is evidence of the purity of what comes from it. And many books have chosen its purity in our school, and there is difference in the correction of the purity of the droppings of birds that are not eaten, and their impurity is considered light (mukhaffafa).
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage explains the Hanafi ruling on the purity of bird droppings. For birds whose meat is halal (eaten), such as pigeons and sparrows, their droppings are considered pure (tahir) and do not spoil water. This ruling is based on istihsan, drawing from the actions of the Companions: Ibn Mas'ud wiped off pigeon droppings with his finger without washing, and Ibn 'Umar did likewise with a pebble and prayed. The hadith of Abu Umama reinforces this, as the Prophet showed gratitude to a pigeon that helped him during the hijra. For non-edible birds, there is a difference: some hold that their droppings are pure, others say they are impure but lightly so (najis mukhaffaf). The relied-upon view in many Hanafi books is purity for edible birds.

Key Terms
خرء (khar’): Droppings, excrement of birds.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juridical preference; a method of reasoning that departs from strict qiyas due to necessity or ease.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the droppings of a pigeon (an edible bird) falling into water?
A) The water becomes impure and must be discarded.
B) The water remains pure and can be used.
C) The water becomes makruh (disliked) but usable.
D) It depends on the quantity of droppings.

Key Takeaway
The droppings of edible birds (except chicken and goose) are pure by istihsan, proven by Companion actions and the hadith of the pigeon.

Ruling on Animals Without Flowing Blood Dying in Water
States that the death of animals without flowing blood (fish, frogs, insects) does not make water impure, with evidence from the hadith of the fly

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on water when an animal without flowing blood dies in it, and explain the evidence from the hadith of the fly.

Core Idea
Animals without flowing blood do not spoil water or liquids; the fly hadith proves their purity.

This lesson clarifies a practical ruling of taharah: when an animal without flowing blood (like a fly or fish) dies in water, the water remains pure and usable. The proof comes from a well-known hadith where the Prophet instructed to fully dip a fly that falls into a drink, rather than discarding the liquid. Understanding this ruling helps distinguish between different categories of animals and their effect on water purity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is the death of an animal without flowing blood in water. The ruling is that the water remains pure (tahir) and does not become impure.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of the fly narrated by al-Bukhari, Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, and al-Nasa'i. The text quotes the command to dip the fly and then remove it, indicating the liquid remains pure.
The hadith is ahad, but it is relied upon for this ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command to dip the fly implies that the fly does not render the liquid impure; otherwise, the Prophet would have ordered discarding it. The presence of disease and cure in the wings further shows that the fly is not inherently impure.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an intra-Hanafi difference regarding liquids other than water. The text states that the more correct view (asahh) extends the ruling to all liquids, not just water.
The mufta bihi is that they do not spoil any liquid.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The tarjih authority is the text itself, which declares 'وكذا المائعات على الأصح' (and likewise liquids on the more correct view). Therefore, the relied-upon position includes all liquids.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بموت ما لا دم له فيه، كسمك وضفدع، وحياة الماء، وبق، وذباب، وزنبور، وعقرب. لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: إذا وقع الذباب في شراب أحدكم فليغمسه، ثم لينزعه، فإن في أحد جناحيه داء وفي الآخر شفاء. رواه البخاري. زاد أبو داود: وإنه يتقي بجناحه الذي فيه الداء. وفي ابن ماجه والنسائي: إذا وقع في الطعام فامقلوه فيه، فإنه يقدم السم ويؤخر الشفاء.
And (water does not become impure) by the death of what has no blood, such as fish, frog, water animals, bedbug, fly, wasp, and scorpion. Due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'If a fly falls into the drink of one of you, then let him dip it, then remove it, for in one of its wings is disease and in the other is cure.' Narrated by al-Bukhari. Abu Dawud added: 'And it protects itself with the wing that has disease.' And in Ibn Majah and al-Nasa'i: 'If it falls into food, then dip it in, for it presents the poison and delays the cure.'
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling that water does not become impure (and other liquids, on the more correct opinion) when an animal without flowing blood dies in it. This includes fish, frogs, water animals like crab, bedbugs, flies, wasps, and scorpions. The proof is the hadith about a fly falling into a drink; the Prophet instructed to dip the fly fully then remove it, indicating that the drink remains pure and can be consumed. The hadith also implies that the fly is not inherently impure despite carrying disease. Note that animals with flowing blood, if they die in water, do cause impurity. The list covers both terrestrial and aquatic creatures that lack the category of 'crawling and flowing blood' (damm sa'il). The ruling is based on istihsan, extending the principle of necessity and ease.

Key Terms
ذُبَاب (dhubāb): Fly; as an example of an animal without flowing blood.
ضَفْدَع (ḍafda‘): Frog; among animals without flowing blood.

Key Takeaway
The death of an animal without flowing blood in water does not render the water impure, as evidenced by the hadith of the fly.

Purity of Water from Bird Droppings and Bloodless Creatures
Ruling with proof on water purity from droppings and dead bloodless creatures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on water spoiled by bird droppings and dead bloodless creatures, and identify the proofs (istihsan and hadith) that support it.

Core Idea
Droppings of edible birds and dead bloodless creatures do not spoil water—ruling by istihsan and prophetic practice.

A common concern in daily life is whether water becomes impure if a bird drops waste into it or if a small insect dies in it. The Hanafi school provides clear guidance: water remains pure in these cases, based on the principle of istihsan (juridical preference) and authentic hadith of the Companions. This lesson examines the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The text states two separate rulings: (1) water is not spoiled by droppings of pigeons and sparrows (and similar edible birds), and (2) water is not spoiled by the death of creatures without blood, like fish and insects.
These rulings apply to both water and other liquids on the correct view.
2
Recognize the category of birds
The ruling on droppings applies specifically to birds whose meat is eaten, such as pigeons and sparrows, but excludes chicken and geese (and by extension similar birds). For non-edible birds, there is a difference of opinion; some Hanafi scholars consider their droppings lightly impure.
The basis for distinguishing is the permissibility of eating the bird.
3
Understand the basis of istihsan
The ruling on purity of droppings is not based on strict qiyas (analogy) but on istihsan, which gives preference to a weaker analogy due to stronger evidence. The stronger evidence here is the practice of the Companions.
Istihsan is a distinctive Hanafi methodology.
4
Examine the hadith evidence
The text cites hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (pigeon droppings wiped with finger) and Ibn 'Umar (bird droppings wiped with pebble, prayed without washing). These show that the Companions did not consider such droppings impure enough to require washing.
Also the hadith of the fly, which implies its body is not impure despite containing poison and cure.
5
Identify the scope of bloodless creatures
The second ruling covers all creatures without flowing blood: fish, frogs (land frogs only if no blood), water animals, insects, scorpions, etc. If an animal has flowing blood, its death would spoil the water.
The key indicator is the presence of flowing blood, not size or habitat.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the purity of water when bird droppings or dead animals without blood fall into it. The author clarifies that water does not become impure by the droppings of pigeons and sparrows, based on istihsan and hadith from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Umar. The ruling applies to birds whose meat is eaten, except chicken and geese. For birds not eaten, there is a difference in verification. Similarly, water is not spoiled by the death of animals without blood, such as fish, frogs (land frogs only if they have no blood), water animals, bugs, flies, wasps, scorpions, etc. This is supported by the hadith instructing to submerge a fly if it falls into a drink, indicating its impurity is not absolute.

Key Terms
خُرْء (khur'): Bird droppings, specifically of pigeon and sparrow.
ما لا دَمَ لَهُ (mā lā dama lahu): Creatures without flowing blood, such as fish, frogs, insects.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juridical preference; the ruling is based on istihsan rather than strict qiyas.

Water Purity When Humans and Animals Fall In
Ruling statement explaining water purity when humans and various animals fall in, with conditions and exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on water purity when a human or an animal falls into water and identify when the water takes the animal's ruling.

Core Idea
Water remains pure when a human or a pure animal falls in; only impurity on the body or saliva reaching water changes the ruling.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains a common scenario in daily life: what happens when a human or an animal falls into a well or water container. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the purity of the animal's body and the potential impurity of its saliva. Understanding this ruling helps maintain proper taharah in unexpected situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The text rules on water purity when a human or an animal falls into it. Determine the specific hukm: water remains pure unless a condition is met.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith: 'O Salman, any food or drink into which a creature without blood falls and dies is halal to eat, drink, and use for wudu.' This indicates the creature's body is pure.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly permits use of water, implying the creature's body does not spoil it. Combined with the principle that animals are originally pure (al-asl al-taharah), this proves the ruling.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars analogize the moisture on the animal's body to saliva and require bailing all water. The correct view rejects this, as moisture is from a pure body.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author declares the correct view (fi al-sahih) based on the hadith and original purity. Saliva only matters if it actually reaches the water.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بوقوع آدمي، وما يُؤكَلُ حَمُهُ، إِذَا خَرَجَ حَيَا، وَلَمْ يَكُنْ على بدَنِهِ نَجَاسَةٌ، ولا بوقوع بَعْـلِ وَحِمَارٍ، وسباعِ طَيْرِ، وَوَحْشِ، في الصحيحِ وَإِنْ وصلَ لُعَابُ الوَاقِعِ إلى المَاءِ، أَحَدَ حُكْمَهُ وَوَجُودُ حَمَوَانٍ مَيْت فيها يُنَجِّسُهَا مِنْ يَومٍ وَلَيْلَةٍ، ومُنْتَفِخِ مِنْ ثلاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ وَلَيَالِيهَا، إِنْ لَمْ يُعْلَمْ وَقتُ وُقُوعِهِ
(1)
وقوله : ( يا سلمان، كلُّ طَعَامٍ وشَرَابِ وقعت فِيهِ دَابَّةٌ لَيْسَ لَهَا دَمٌ، فَمَاتَتْ فِيهِ، فَهُوَ حَلالٌ أَكْلُهُ وشربُهُ ووضووه ). (وَلا) يفسد الماء، أي: لا ينجس (بوقوع آدمي، و) لا بوقوع (ما يُؤكل لحمه)، كالإبل والبقر والغنم (إِذَا خَرَجَ حَيّاً، ولَمْ يَكُنْ عَلَى بَدَنِهِ نَجَاسَةٌ) متيقنة، وإنما قلنا ذلك؛ لأنـهـم قـالوا في البقر ونحوه يخرج حياً لا يجب نزح شيء، وإن كان الظاهر اشتمال بولها على أفخاذها، لكن احتمل طهارتها، بأن سقطت عقب دخولها ماء كثيراً، هذا مع أن الأصل الطهارة. (ولا) يفسد الـمـاء (بوقوع بغل وحِمارٍ، وسباع طير) كصقـر وشاهين وحدأة. (و) لا يفسد بوقوع (وحش)، كسـبـع، وضبـع، ونمر، وقرد، ( في الصحيح)، لطهارة بدنها. وقيل: يجب نزح كل الماء، إلحاقـاً لرطوبة المذكورات بلعابها، إذا لم يصل لعابها الماء، (وَإِنْ وصلَ لُعَابُ الوَاقِعِ إلى المَاءِ أَخَذَ الماء (حُكْمَهُ)، طهارة ونجاسة وكراهة، وقد علم ذلك في الأسار)، فينزح بالنجس والمشكوك، وفي المكروه يستحب نزحها، ويستحب نزح دلاء ولو طاهراً، وقيل: عشرين (۳)، وإن كان خنزيراً نزح الجميع، وإن لم يصل فمه الماء لنجاسة عينه. وقيل: الكلب مثله، والأصح أن الكلب غير نجس العين كما قدمناه. وقيل: دبــره منقلب إلى خارج. فلهذا يفسد الماء، بخلاف غيره من الحيوانات.
And not by the fall of a human, and what is eaten of its meat, when it comes out alive and there is no impurity on its body, and not by the fall of a mule, donkey, birds of prey, and wild animals, in the correct view. And if the saliva of the falling one reaches the water, the water takes its ruling. And the presence of a dead animal in it (the well) makes it impure from a day and a night, and a swollen one from three days and their nights, if the time of its fall is not known. And his saying: 'O Salman, every food and drink into which falls a creature that has no blood and dies in it, its eating, drinking, and wudu are halal.' (And it does not spoil) the water, i.e., it does not make it impure (by the fall of a human, and) not by the fall of (what is eaten of its meat), like camels, cows, sheep (when it comes out alive, and there is no confirmed impurity on its body). We only say that because they said about cows and the like that if they come out alive, no bailing is required, even though it is apparent that their urine covers their thighs, but (we) consider the possibility of their purity, as they may have fallen after entering abundant water, and the original principle is purity. (And it does not spoil) the water (by the fall of a mule and donkey, and birds of prey) like a falcon, hawk, and kite. (And) it does not spoil by the fall of (wild animals), like a lion, hyena, tiger, monkey, (in the correct view), because of the purity of their bodies. And it is said: the whole water must be bailed, analogizing the moisture of the mentioned ones to their saliva, if their saliva did not reach the water. (And if the saliva of the falling one reaches the water, the water takes its ruling), purity, impurity, or disapproval, and that is known from the law. So if it is impure or doubtful, it is bailed; if it is disapproved, it is recommended to bail it, and it is recommended to bail buckets even if pure, and it is said: twenty (buckets) (3), and if it is a pig, all is bailed even if its mouth did not reach the water because of the impurity of its substance. And it is said: the dog is like it, but the correct view is that the dog is not impure in substance as we presented. And it is said: its anus is turned outward, so it spoils the water, unlike other animals.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement explaining that water does not become impure when a human or certain animals fall into it. The author states that the falling of a human, an edible animal (if it came out alive and without confirmed impurity), a mule, donkey, birds of prey, and wild animals does not spoil the water, based on the purity of their bodies. However, if the saliva of the falling animal reaches the water, the water takes the ruling of that saliva (pure, impure, or disapproved). For a pig, all water must be bailed because its body is impure. The correct view is that the dog is not impure in substance, so it does not spoil water unless its saliva reaches it.

Key Terms
لُعَاب (lu'āb): Saliva of an animal that falls into water.
نَجِسُ الْعَيْن (najis al-'ayn): Impur in substance (like pig, dog according to some).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The water becomes impure and must be bailed entirely
B) The water remains pure because the dog is not impure in substance
C) The water becomes impure only if the dog has visible impurities
D) The water becomes impure and twenty buckets must be bailed

Key Takeaway
Water remains pure when a human or a non-impure animal falls into it, provided no impurity is on the body and saliva does not reach the water.

Dead Animal in Well: Impurity and Prayer Repetition
Ruling on impurity of well due to dead animal with unknown time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on impurity of well water when a dead animal is found without known time and apply the consequences for prayer repetition.

Core Idea
A dead animal in a well renders water impure from one day/night; swollen from three days/nights, as precaution.

How do we determine if well water is impure when we find a dead animal but don't know when it fell? The Hanafi school, following Abu Hanifa's precaution, uses time estimates based on the animal's condition. This lesson explains the ruling and its practical consequences for prayer and purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Condition
The ruling applies when a dead animal is found in a well and the time of its fall is unknown.
2
Note the Ruling for Normal vs. Swollen
If the animal is not swollen, the water is considered impure from one day and one night. If it is swollen, the period is three days and three nights.
Swelling indicates longer decomposition.
3
Understand the Basis: Precaution (Ihtiyat)
Abu Hanifa ruled by precaution, using the animal's condition to estimate the minimum time of impurity.
4
Apply Consequences for Prayers
If someone used the water for wudu or ghusl while in a state of hadath or janabah, they must repeat prayers performed during that period. But if they were already pure, no repetition is needed.
This is due to the principle that prayer is not invalidated by doubt.
5
Recognize the Analogy to Impurity on Garment
The text draws an analogy: just as finding impurity on a garment without knowing when does not require repeating past prayers, the same applies here for washing clothes from impurity.

Source Text

وَوُجُودُ حَيَوانِ مِّيْتَ فِيهَا) أي: البئر (يُنَجِّسُهَا مِنْ يَومٍ وَلَيْلَةٍ) عند أبي حنيفـة احتياطاً، (ومنتفخ) ينجسها ( من ثلاثةِ أيامٍ، وَلَيَالِيها؛ إنْ لَمْ يُعْلَمُ وقت وُقُوعِه)، فينجس الـمــاء فـي حــق الـوضــوء، فيلزم إعادة صلوات تلك المدة، إذا توضؤوا منها وهم محدثون، أو اغتسلوا منها من جنابة. وأما إذا توضؤوا منها وهم متوضئون، أو غسلوا ثيابهم من غير نجاسة، فإنهم لا يعيدون إجماعاً، لأن الصلاة لا تبطل بالشك، وأما إذا كانوا قد غسلوا ثيابهم عن نجاسة، ولم يتوضؤوا منها، فلا يلزمهم إلا غسلها على الصحيح، ويحكم بنجاستها في الحال من غير إسناد؛ لأنه من باب وجود النجاسة في الثوب، كمن وجدها بثوبه أكثر من درهم، ولم يدر متى أصابته لا يعيد شيئاً من صلاته اتفاقاً، هو الصحيح.

(1) أخرجه البيهقي في سننه، كتاب الطهارة، باب ما لا نفس له سائلة إذا مات في الماء القليل (٢٥٣/١)، والدارقطني في كتاب الطهارة، باب: كل طعام وقعت فيه دابة ليس لها دم (۳۷/۱).
(۳) لأن كل موضع فيه نزح لا ينزح أقل من العشرين لأنه أقل ما جاء به الشرع من المقادير اهـ وهـذا الـنـزح لتسكين القلب لا للتطهير، حتى لو توضأ منها من غير نزح جاز. ط.

And the presence of a dead animal in it (i.e., the well) makes it impure from a day and a night according to Abu Hanifa as a precaution, and a swollen one makes it impure from three days and their nights, if the time of its fall is not known. So the water becomes impure for the purpose of ablution, and repetition of prayers of that period becomes necessary if they performed ablution from it while in a state of hadath, or performed ghusl from janabah. But if they performed ablution while already in a state of purity, or washed their clothes without impurity, they do not repeat by consensus, because prayer is not invalidated by doubt. And if they had washed their clothes from impurity and did not perform ablution from it, then nothing is required of them except washing them according to the correct view, and it is judged to be impure at the present moment without attribution, because it falls under the category of finding impurity on the garment, like one who finds on his garment an impurity larger than a dirham and does not know when it affected him; he does not repeat any of his prayers by agreement. That is the correct view.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding the impurity of a well when a dead animal is found inside without knowing the time of its fall. According to Abu Hanifa, as a precaution, if the animal has been dead for a day and a night, the well is considered impure. If the animal is swollen, it is considered dead for three days and nights. The water is impure for wudu and ghusl. Prayers performed with wudu or ghusl from this water during that period must be repeated if the person was in a state of impurity (hadath or janabah). However, if they were already pure or washed clothes that were not impure, no repetition is needed. If they washed impure clothes, only the clothes need rewashing, not the prayers, because doubt does not invalidate prayers.

Key Terms
يُنجّس (yunajjisu): Renders the water impure (najis).
مُنْتَفِخ (muntafikh): A dead animal that has swollen, indicating it has been dead for a longer period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Repeat wudu
B) Repeat prayers
C) Nothing
D) Repeat both wudu and prayers

Key Takeaway
Impurity of well water due to a dead animal with unknown time is determined by precaution: one day/night for normal, three for swollen; prayer repetition depends on the state at time of use.
