Animals That Do Not Spoil Water When They Fall In
States which animals do not render water impure when falling in

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which animals do not render water impure when falling in, and explain the condition regarding their saliva.

Core Idea
Water is not rendered impure by the fall of a pure-bodied animal unless its saliva mixes with the water.

This passage from the commentary on Nur al-Idah clarifies which animals may fall into water without defiling it. Understanding these rulings is essential for everyday taharah (purification). The passage lists various animals and the conditions under which their fall leaves water pure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
The passage states that water is not invalidated (i.e., remains pure) by the fall of certain animals. Determine the overall principle: pure-bodied animals do not spoil water unless their saliva mixes with it.
2
List the animals exempted
Identify the animals listed: humans, edible livestock (if they come out alive and clean), mules, donkeys, predatory birds, and wild beasts (lion, hyena, tiger, monkey). Understand that these are considered pure-bodied in the Hanafi school.
Predatory birds and wild beasts are pure despite their diet.
3
Note the condition of coming out alive and clean
For edible livestock, the ruling depends on the animal coming out alive and having no certain impurity on its body. If it dies or is visibly impure, the ruling may differ.
The author argues that even if urine is likely on the thighs, purity is assumed due to the original presumption.
4
Understand the effect of saliva
If the saliva of the falling animal reaches the water, the water takes the ruling of that animal: pure, impure, or disliked. For pure animals, water remains pure; for impure animals (like pig), water becomes impure.
Saliva includes moisture from the mouth.
5
Recognize special cases and hadith evidence
The passage mentions that pigs are inherently impure (water must be removed even if mouth not submerged), while dogs are not inherently impure in the relied-upon view. It also cites a hadith about creatures without blood (e.g., flies) not affecting water.
The hadith supports that bloodless creatures do not spoil water.

(وَلا) يفسد الماء، أي: لا ينجس (بوقوع آدمي، و) لا بوقوع (ما يُؤكل لحمه)، كالإبل والبقر والغنم (إِذَا خَرَجَ حَيّاً، ولَمْ يَكُنْ عَلَى بَدَنِهِ نَجَاسَةٌ) متيقنة، وإنما قلنا ذلك؛ لأنـهـم قـالوا في البقر ونحوه يخرج حياً لا يجب نزح شيء، وإن كان الظاهر اشتمال بولها على أفخاذها، لكن احتمل طهارتها، بأن سقطت عقب دخولها ماء كثيراً، هذا مع أن الأصل الطهارة. (ولا) يفسد الـمـاء (بوقوع بغل وحِمارٍ، وسباع طير) كصقـر وشاهين وحدأة. (و) لا يفسد بوقوع (وحش)، كسـبـع، وضـبـع، ونمر، وقرد، ( في الصحيح)، لطهارة بدنها. وقيل: يجب نزح كل الماء، إلحاقـاً لرطوبة المذكورات بلعابها، إذا لم يصل لعابها الماء، (وَإِنْ وصلَ لُعَابُ الوَاقِعِ إلى المَاءِ أَخَذَ الماء (حُكْمَهُ)، طهارة ونجاسة وكراهة، وقد علم ذلك في الأسار)، فينزح بالنجس والمشكوك، وفي المكروه يستحب نزحها، ويستحب نزح دلاء ولو طاهراً، وقيل: عشرين (۳)، وإن كان خنزيراً نزح الجميع، وإن لم يصل فمه الماء لنجاسة عينه. وقيل: الكلب مثله، والأصح أن الكلب غير نجس العين كما قدمناه. وقيل: دبــره منقلب إلى خارج. فلهذا يفسد الماء، بخلاف غيره من الحيوانات. (1) أخرجه البيهقي في سننه، كتاب الطهارة، باب ما لا نفس له سائلة إذا مات في الماء القليل (٢٥٣/١)، والدارقطني في كتاب الطهارة، باب: كل طعام وقعت فيه دابة ليس لها دم (۳۷/۱).
And [water] is not invalidated by the fall of a human, nor of what is eaten for its meat, when it comes out alive, and there is no impurity on its body, nor by the fall of a mule and donkey, and predatory birds, and wild beasts, in the correct opinion. And if the saliva of the falling [animal] reaches the water, the water takes its ruling. Proof: And his saying: 'O Salman, every food and drink into which a creature that has no blood falls and dies, its eating, drinking, and performance of wudu are lawful.' And [water] is not spoiled, i.e., not rendered impure, by the fall of a human, nor by the fall of what is eaten for its meat, like camels, cows, and sheep, when it comes out alive and there is no certain impurity on its body. We said that because they said regarding cows and the like that if it comes out alive, no [water] is required to be removed, although it is apparent that its urine is on its thighs, but its purity is possible because it fell immediately after entering much water, and the original presumption is purity. And water is not spoiled by the fall of a mule and donkey, and predatory birds like falcon, hawk, and kite. And it is not spoiled by the fall of a wild beast, like lion, hyena, tiger, and monkey, in the correct opinion, due to the purity of their bodies. And it was said: all water must be removed, analogizing the moisture of the mentioned animals to their saliva, if their saliva does not reach the water. And if the saliva of the falling animal reaches the water, the water takes its ruling—purity, impurity, or dislikeability—as understood from the [previous] chapters. So for impure and doubtful [cases], water is removed; in disliked cases, it is recommended to remove it, and it is recommended to remove buckets even if pure, and it was said: twenty [buckets]. And if it is a pig, all water is removed, even if its mouth does not reach the water—due to its inherent impurity. And it was said: the dog is like it, but the correct [view] is that the dog is not inherently impure as we have mentioned. And it was said: its anus is turned outward, so this spoils the water, unlike other animals. Reported by al-Bayhaqi and al-Daraqutni.

Commentary
This passage expands upon the matn of Nur al-Idah concerning the rulings of animals falling into water. It begins by listing animals whose fall does not render water impure: humans, edible livestock when they come out alive and are clean, mules, donkeys, predatory birds, and wild beasts. The key condition is that the animal's body is pure. If the saliva of such an animal reaches the water, the water takes the ruling of that animal in terms of purity, impurity, or dislike. The author then quotes a hadith indicating that creatures without blood (e.g., flies) do not affect water. The passage also discusses the case of pigs (inherently impure) and dogs (not inherently impure in the relied-upon view). The footnote cites the hadith from the Sunan of al-Bayhaqi and al-Daraqutni.

Key Terms
سباع طير (sibāʿ ṭayr): Predatory birds such as falcons, hawks, and kites.
لعاب (luʿāb): Saliva or moisture from the mouth of an animal.

B) The water remains pure and no act is required.
C) The water becomes disliked and it is recommended to remove some buckets.
D) The water becomes impure only if the hawk had eaten carrion recently.

Key Takeaway
Water remains pure when a pure-bodied animal falls into it, provided the animal comes out alive and clean and its saliva does not mix with the water.

Dead Animal in a Well: Retroactive Impurity and the Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on retroactive impurity timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on retroactive impurity of well water when a dead animal is found, and evaluate the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa estimates impurity retroactively by animal condition; the Sahibayn require exact knowledge—precaution versus principle.

This passage addresses a practical dilemma: a dead animal is discovered in a well, but the time it fell in is unknown. How far back does the water become impure? Which past prayers must be repeated? Abu Hanifa provides an estimation based on the animal's state (non-bloated vs. bloated), while his students Abu Yusuf and Muhammad reject retroactive rulings without certainty. This lesson unpacks their proofs and the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling: water is retroactively impure for one day/night (non‑bloated) or three days/nights (bloated). Note the conditions: the time of falling is unknown.
This is a precautionary estimation based on the apparent cause (the fall).
2
Identify the Sahibayn's objection
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the water is impure only from the moment of discovery; no past acts are affected unless the exact time is known.
Their reasoning: the animal might have died instantly or been thrown in already dead.
3
Trace the dalil of each side
Abu Hanifa relies on the apparent cause (fall into the well is the likely cause of death) and empirical knowledge (bloating indicates about three days). The Sahibayn give weight to the possibility of immediate death or external factors.
The Hanafi principle of istihsan (juridical preference) and the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' also play a role.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The text argues that the apparent cause outweighs a mere remote possibility; precaution (ihtiyat) requires estimating the duration.
The objection that doubt invalidates retroactivity is countered by noting that prayer is not invalidated by doubt (consensus).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Under Abu Hanifa's view, many prayers may need to be repeated; under the Sahibayn's view, only those after the discovery. The text presents Abu Hanifa's as the primary opinion, though later practice may favour the Sahibayn for ease.
The author indicates that Abu Hanifa's estimation is the relied‑upon view in this commentary, but later Hanafi scholars often adopt the Sahibayn's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَوُجُودُ حَيَوَانِ مِّيْتَ فِيهَا) أي: البئر (يُنَجِّسُهَا مِنْ يَومٍ وَلَيْلَةٍ) عند أبي حنيفـة احتياطاً، (ومنتفخ) ينجسها ( من ثلاثةِ أيامٍ، وَلَيَالِيها؛ إنْ لَمْ يُعْلَمُ وقت وُقُوعِه)، فينجس الـمــاء فـي حــق الـوضــوء، فيلزم إعادة صلوات تلك المدة، إذا توضؤوا منها وهم محدثون، أو اغتسلوا منها من جنابة. وأما إذا توضؤوا منها وهم متوضئون، أو غسلوا ثيابهم من غير نجاسة، فإنهم لا يعيدون إجماعاً، لأن الصلاة لا تبطل بالشك، وأما إذا كانوا قد غسلوا ثيابهم عن نجاسة، ولم يتوضؤوا منها، فلا يلزمهم إلا غسلها على الصحيح، ويحكم بنجاستها في الحال من غير إسناد؛ لأنه من باب وجود النجاسة في الثوب، كمن وجدها بثوبه أكثر من درهم، ولم يدر متى أصابته لا يعيد شيئاً من صلاته اتفاقاً، هو الصحيح. والتقدير بتلك المدة قول الإمام رحمه الله؛ لأن الوقوع في البئر، سبب لموته ظاهراً فيحال عليه. و احتمال الموت بغيره موهوم، لا يعتبر في مقابلة الظاهر، وقدر زمان بقائه فيها ميتــاً بـيــوم وليلة، في غير المنتفخ احتياطاً؛ لأن ما دونه ساعات لا تنضبط لتفاوتها، وقدر في المنتفخ بثلاثة أيام، لأن الانتفاخ دليل تقادم العهد، والحيوان لا ينتفخ غالباً إلا بعد ثلاثة أيام. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمـد: يحكم بنجاستها وقت العلم بها، ولا يلزمهم إعادة شيء من الصلوات، ولا غسل ما أصابه ماؤها في الزمان الماضي، حتى يتحققوا متى وقعت؛ لاحتمال أنها ماتت في الحال وهي غير منتفخة، أو ألقاها الريح أو غيره ميتة منتفخة.
And the presence of a dead animal in it, i.e., the well, makes it impure from a day and a night according to Abu Hanifa as a precaution, and [a dead animal that is] bloated makes it impure from three days and their nights, if the time of its falling is unknown. So the water is impure with respect to wudu, and it becomes necessary to repeat the prayers of that period if they performed wudu from it while they were in a state of minor impurity, or performed ghusl from it for major impurity. But if they performed wudu from it while already in a state of wudu, or washed their clothes without impurity, they do not repeat by consensus, because prayer is not invalidated by doubt. And if they washed their clothes from impurity but did not perform wudu from it, they need only wash them according to the correct [view], and they are judged to be impure at present without ascription [to the past], because it is from the chapter of finding impurity on a garment, like one who finds impurity larger than a dirham on his garment and does not know when it got there; he does not repeat any of his prayers by agreement; that is correct. And the estimation with that period is the saying of Imam [Abu Hanifa]—may Allah have mercy on him—because falling into the well is an apparent cause of its death, so it is attributed to that. And the possibility of death by other [causes] is fanciful and not considered against the apparent. He estimated the duration of its remaining dead in it as a day and a night for the non-bloated as a precaution because lesser durations are unregulated due to their variation, and he estimated for the bloated as three days because bloating indicates the lapse of time, and an animal generally does not bloat except after three days. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: It is judged to be impure at the time it is known, and they are not required to repeat any prayers nor to wash what its water touched in the past until they ascertain when it fell, because it is possible that it died instantly while not bloated, or that the wind or something else threw it in dead and bloated.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario where a dead animal is discovered in a well, and the time of its falling is unknown. Abu Hanifa (the Imam) rules that the water is considered impure retroactively for a specific duration: one day and night for a non-bloated animal, and three days and nights for a bloated one. This is a precautionary measure based on the apparent cause (the fall). Consequently, if prayers were performed with that water, they must be repeated, provided the person was in a state of impurity at that time. On the other hand, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Sahibayn) hold that the water is only impure from the moment of discovery, and no past acts need to be repeated unless the exact time of death is known. Their reasoning is that the animal might have died immediately or been thrown in already dead. The passage also clarifies that if doubts arise about past perf-ormance (e.g., wudu while already pure), no repetition is needed by consensus, as prayer is not invalidated by doubt.

Key Terms
منتفخ (muntafikh): A dead animal that has become bloated, indicating it has been dead for some time
إعادة (iʿādah): Repetition of prayers that were invalid due to impurity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the duration of retroactive impurity for a bloated dead animal found in a well?
A) One day and one night
B) Three days and three nights
C) From the time of discovery only
D) Exactly one week

Key Takeaway
When a dead animal is found in a well with unknown fall time, Abu Hanifa retroactively impurifies the water based on the animal's condition (1 day if non-bloated, 3 if bloated), while the Sahibayn require exact knowledge; the practical difference lies in how many past prayers must be repeated.

Rulings on Dough Made with Impure Well Water
Supplementary ruling on dough from impure well water.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi opinions on disposing of dough made with impure well water and identify the relied-upon position according to al-Bada'i.

Core Idea
Impure well water renders dough impure; it cannot be eaten but may be fed to animals or sold to Shafi'is.

This supplement addresses a practical scenario: if dough is kneaded with water from an impure well, what should be done with it? The Hanafi school offers multiple opinions, reflecting different considerations of necessity and inter-madhhab interaction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the dough is made with water from a well that is suspected or known to be impure. The ruling is that the dough itself becomes impure (najis).
2
List the three opinions
The passage presents three opinions: (1) throw it to dogs, (2) feed it to livestock, (3) sell it to a follower of the Shafi'i school.
3
Identify the preferred Hanafi position
According to al-Bada'i, the first opinion (feed to dogs) is narrated as 'Our mashayikh said' and is thus the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view.
4
Understand the cross-madhhab element
Selling to a Shafi'i is allowed because the Shafi'i school considers the water pure unless a visible impurity appears, so the dough is considered pure for them.
This shows practical accommodation between madhhabs.
5
Note the underlying water purity principle
The footnote clarifies that if the well water reaches two qullahs (approx. 500 liters), it does not become impure by mere contact without a visible effect. This influences the initial ruling on the water.
Two qullahs is a key Hanafi threshold for water purity.

Source Text

تتمة: لو عُجِن بمائها عجين، قال بعضهم: يلقى للكلاب، وقال بعضهم: يعلـف بـه المواشي، وقال بعضهم: يباع من شافعي المذهب ) . وفي البدائع » : ذكر القول الأول بصيغـة قـال مشايخنا: يطعم للكلاب. انتهى. وذكر ابن رستم في فوائده ) عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله: من وجد في ثوبه منيــاً أعاد من آخر نومة نامها، لأنه سبب الاحتلام، وفي الدم لا يعيد شيئاً لأنه يصيبه من الخارج، بخلاف المني، حتى لو كان الثوب يلبسه هو وغيره، يستوي فيه حكم الدم والمني. وفي البول من آخر ما بال. (۱) لأن الماء إذا بلغ قلتين لا ينجس عنده بدون ظهور أثر. ط.
Supplement: If dough is kneaded with its water, some said: it is thrown to dogs; some said: it is fed to livestock; some said: it is sold to a follower of the Shafi'i school. And in al-Bada'i': the first opinion is mentioned with the wording: 'Our mashayikh said: it is fed to dogs.' End. And Ibn Rustam mentioned in his Fawa'id from Abu Hanifa—may Allah have mercy on him: Whoever finds semen on his garment repeats from the last sleep he slept, because it is the cause of the wet dream; and for blood he does not repeat anything, because it gets on him from outside, unlike semen. Even if the garment is worn by him and others, the ruling of blood and semen is the same. And for urine [he repeats] from the last time he urinated. (1) Because if the water reaches two qullahs, it does not become impure according to him without the appearance of an effect.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This supplement (tatemma) provides additional rulings related to water impurity. The first part discusses what to do with dough made with water from a well that is suspected to be impure. There are three opinions: give it to dogs, feed it to livestock, or sell it to a Shafi'i (since the Shafi'i school has different purity rules). The second part, quoting Ibn Rustam from Abu Hanifa, addresses the ruling on finding semen or blood on one's garment. If semen is found, one must repeat prayers from the last sleep, as it likely came from a wet dream. For blood, no repetition is needed because it can come from external sources. However, if the garment is shared, the same rule applies for both. The footnote adds that if the well water reaches two qullahs (a specific large quantity), it does not become impure unless an effect is visible, according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
عجين (ʿajīn): Dough made with water from a well that may be impure
قلتين (qullatayn): A large volume of water (approximately 500 liters) that prevents impurity from affecting it unless an impurity is visible

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which opinion is explicitly attributed to 'Our mashayikh' (our scholars) in al-Bada'i?
A) Throw the dough to dogs
B) Feed the dough to livestock
C) Sell the dough to a Shafi'i

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi view is to feed impure dough to dogs, though other valid opinions exist for different circumstances.

Rulings on Finding Semen or Blood on Garments
Supplementary ruling on impurities on garments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on finding semen or blood on one's garment and determine when prayers must be repeated.

Core Idea
Semen from a wet dream requires repeating prayers from the last sleep; blood from external sources does not, unless the garment is shared.

This passage from Ibn Rustam quotes Abu Hanifa on a common issue: discovering an impurity on one's garment after some time has passed. The ruling distinguishes between semen (presumed from a wet dream) and blood (presumed from external contact), with additional consideration for shared garments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases: semen and blood
The passage addresses two types of impurities found on a garment: semen (مني) and blood (دم). For each, there is a ruling on whether to repeat past prayers.
2
State the ruling for semen
If a person finds semen on his garment and believes it is from a wet dream, he must repeat all prayers from the last sleep he slept.
The sleep is considered the cause (sabab) of the wet dream.
3
State the ruling for blood
For blood, he does not repeat any prayers because blood can come from external sources (e.g., a cut) and may not have occurred during prayer.
4
Understand the exception for shared garments
If the garment is worn by the person and others (e.g., shared clothing), the same ruling applies for both semen and blood—meaning one must consider the possibility that the impurity came from someone else.
5
Note the parallel rule for urine
The passage also mentions urine: if found, one repeats from the last time he urinated, because urination is a known act that can cause impurity.

(۱) لأن الماء إذا بلغ قلتين لا ينجس عنده بدون ظهور أثر. ط.

Key Terms
مني (manī): Semen; a seminal fluid that is impure (najis) in the Hanafi school.
دم (dam): Blood; flowing blood from wounds or other sources is impure in quantities that smear.
احتلام (iḥtilām): Wet dream; involuntary ejaculation during sleep.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) From the last sleep he slept
C) From the last time he had a wet dream

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school presumes semen from a wet dream occurs during sleep, necessitating repetition of prayers from that sleep, while blood is presumed external and does not trigger repetition.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Well Impurity After a Dead Animal
Intra-Hanafi dispute on well impuritiy with retrospective ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on retrospective impurity of well water and explain the legal principle behind each view.

Core Idea
When an animal is found dead in a well, Abu Hanifa attributes impurity from the apparent cause; the Sahibayn require certainty.

This passage addresses a classic intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the time from which well water becomes impure when a dead animal is discovered. The ruling has practical consequences for whether past prayers must be repeated. To navigate this, we must understand how each side reasons from the apparent cause versus the need for certainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause of death
Recognise that Imam Abu Hanifa treats falling into the well as the apparent cause (sabab zahir) of the animal's death, so the impurity is attributed to that moment.
Also note the Sahibayn's objection: the animal might have died later or been thrown in already dead.
2
Understand the estimation of time
Abu Hanifa estimates one day/night for a non-swollen carcass and three days for a swollen one. Grasp why swelling indicates earlier death: animals generally swell after three days.
The estimation is precautionary because shorter periods are difficult to quantify precisely.
3
Contrast the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule that impurity begins only from the time of discovery. They do not require repeating prayers or washing items touched earlier because of uncertainty about the exact moment of death.
Their principle: impurity cannot be imposed retroactively without definite knowledge.
4
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Abu Hanifa mandates repeating prayers performed with the water from the estimated time of death; the Sahibayn do not.
This affects a Muslim's daily worship and highlights the importance of the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتقدير بتلك المدة قول الإمام رحمه الله؛ لأن الوقوع في البئر، سبب لموته ظاهراً فيحال عليه. و احتمال الموت بغيره موهوم، لا يعتبر في مقابلة الظاهر، وقدر زمان بقائه فيها ميتــاً بـيـوم وليلة، في غير المنتفخ احتياطاً؛ لأن ما دونه ساعات لا تنضبط لتفاوتها، وقدر في المنتفخ بثلاثة أيام، لأن الانتفاخ دليل تقادم العهد، والحيوان لا ينتفخ غالباً إلا بعد ثلاثة أيام. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمـد: يحكم بنجاستها وقت العلم بها، ولا يلزمهم إعادة شيء من الصلوات، ولا غسل ما أصابه ماؤها في الزمان الماضي، حتى يتحققوا متى وقعت؛ لاحتمال أنها ماتت في الحال وهي غير منتفخة، أو ألقاها الريح أو غيره ميتة منتفخة. تتمة: لو عُجِن بمائها عجين، قال بعضهم: يلقى للكلاب، وقال بعضهم: يعلـف بـه المواشي، وقال بعضهم: يباع من شافعي المذهب. وفي البدائع: ذكر القول الأول بصيغة قال مشايخنا: يطعم للكلاب. انتهى. وذكر ابن رستم في فوائده عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله: من وجد في ثوبه منيــاً أعاد من آخر نومة نامها، لأنه سبب الاحتلام، وفي الدم لا يعيد شيئاً لأنه يصيبه من الخارج، بخلاف المني، حتى لو كان الثوب يلبسه هو وغيره، يستوي فيه حكم الدم والمني. وفي البول من آخر ما بال.
The estimation with that period is the statement of Imam (Abu Hanifa), because falling into the well is an apparent cause of its death, so it is attributed to it. And the possibility of death by other causes is imaginary, not considered in the face of the apparent. He estimated the time of its remaining dead in it as one day and night for the non-swollen, as a precaution, because less than that is hours that cannot be controlled due to their variation. For the swollen, he estimated three days, because swelling indicates lapse of time, and animals generally do not swell except after three days. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The impurity is ruled from the time they know of it, and they are not required to repeat any prayers nor to wash anything that its water touched in the past, until they ascertain when it fell, due to the possibility that it died immediately while non-swollen, or the wind or something else threw a dead swollen animal. Supplement: If dough is kneaded with its water, some said: it is fed to dogs, some said: it is fed to livestock, some said: it is sold to a follower of the Shafi'i school. In al-Bada'i': the first opinion is mentioned in the phrasing 'our shaykhs said: it is fed to the dogs.' End. Ibn Rustom mentioned in his Fawa'id from Abu Hanifa: Whoever finds semen on his garment repeats the prayer from the last sleep he slept, because it is the cause of the wet dream. For blood, he does not repeat anything because it comes from external, unlike semen, to the extent that if the garment is worn by him and others, the ruling for blood and semen becomes equal. For urine, from the last time he urinated.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the impurity of well water when an animal is found dead in it. It begins by stating Imam Abu Hanifa's position: since falling into the well is an apparent cause of death, the animal is presumed to have died upon falling. He therefore estimates the time of death for the purpose of retrospective impurity: one day and night for a non-swollen carcass (since swelling takes time), and three days for a swollen one (as swelling typically occurs after three days). This is precautionary. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree: they rule that the well is only considered impure from the moment the carcass is discovered. They do not require repeating past prayers or washing items touched by the water before discovery, because the animal may have died immediately without swelling, or the carcass may have been thrown in by wind later. This difference stems from their view that the cause of death is not certain enough to retrospectively impose impurity. The passage then adds a supplement (tatimmah) regarding dough made with such water: three opinions are given—feeding it to dogs, livestock, or selling it to Shafi'is (who consider water less than two qullas impure anyway). The text references al-Bada'i' and Ibn Rustom's Fawa'id, the latter citing Abu Hanifa's ruling on finding semen or blood on a garment: for semen, one repeats prayer from the last sleep (since it likely came from a wet dream), for blood no repetition is needed (as it may come from external sources), but if the garment is shared, both are treated equally. For urine, one repeats from the last urination. This supplement illustrates the principle of attributing impurity to the most likely cause.

Key Terms
المنتفخ (al-muntafikh): The carcass that has become swollen/bloated, indicating some time has passed since death
تقادم العهد (taqaddum al-'ahd): The passage of time; specifically that swelling indicates the death occurred longer ago

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a non-swollen dead animal is found in a well, how long is the water considered impure from the time of discovery?
A) One day and night
B) Three days
C) From the time of knowledge
D) Not impure at all

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa attributes impurity to the apparent cause (falling) with estimated timing; the Sahibayn require certainty and only rule from the time of discovery.

Supplement: Dough from Impure Well Water and Garment Impurities
Supplement on practical applications of impurity rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi opinions on dough made with impure well water and explain the rulings on finding semen, blood, or urine on a garment.

Core Idea
Impure water used in dough is disposed of per three opinions; personal impurities on garments are attributed to the most likely cause.

This supplement expands on practical applications of impurity rulings. After discussing the well water dispute, the text addresses dough made with such water and then turns to rulings on finding semen, blood, or urine on a garment. These cases illustrate how Hanafi jurists apply the principle of attributing impurity to the most probable cause.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dough scenario
The supplement begins: 'If dough is kneaded with its water...' meaning the impure well water. Three opinions are given for what to do with the dough.
These are not necessarily a dispute but different views within the school.
2
Identify the three opinions
First: feed to dogs. Second: feed to livestock. Third: sell to Shafi'is (who consider water less than two qullas impure but their ruling allows them to use it).
The text references al-Bada'i' stating 'our shaykhs said feed to dogs' as the first opinion.
3
Analyse the garment impurity ruling
Ibn Rustom from Abu Hanifa: if a man finds semen on his garment, he repeats prayers from the last sleep (most likely cause: wet dream). For blood, no repetition because it may come from external sources. If the garment is shared, both semen and blood are treated equally (uncertainty).
For urine, repeat from the last urination.
4
Extract the principle
The ruling uses the concept of attributing impurity to the most likely cause (sabab ghalib). Semen is attributed to the last sleep; blood cannot be attributed to any specific time; urine is attributed to the last urination.
This is consistent with the earlier well dispute: Abu Hanifa attributes death to falling because it is the apparent cause.

نومة (nawma): A single sleep; the period between sleeping and waking.

Istinja and Istibra: Definitions and Legal Status
Definition and ruling on istinja and istibra

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal status of istinja (sunnah muakkadah) and istibra (lazim for men), and define each term with its linguistic derivation.

Core Idea
Istinja is a sunnah, not wajib — the Prophet's practice and hadith prove it; istibra is necessary for men.

This passage opens the chapter on istinja with a detailed linguistic analysis and then clarifies the ruling. You will learn why istinja is not obligatory despite being a regular practice of the Prophet, and why istibra is specially required for men. The hadith 'fala haraj' (no harm) is the key proof.

Guided Path
1
Parse linguistic derivation
Identify the root meanings of istinja (from 'najw' = cut off, or 'najwa' = elevated land). Note that the 'sin' indicates seeking. Distinguish terms: istinja, istitaba (general), istijmar (specific to stones).
Linguistic parsing helps understand the legal scope of the term.
2
Understand istibra and its necessity
Istibra is seeking to ensure no urine remains. The text says it is 'lazim' (necessary) for men, stronger than wajib. Women simply wait a little after urination. The means vary by habit (walking, coughing, etc.).
Istibra is a precondition for valid wudu.
3
Derive the ruling for istinja
Istinja is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) for both genders. The proof is the hadith: 'Whoever uses stones should do so an odd number; whoever does this has done well, and whoever does not, there is no harm.' The phrase 'fala haraj' shows it is not obligatory.
The Hanafi position relies on the absence of harm (haraj) in omission.
4
Apply the ruling to practice
A person who omits istinja does not sin, but loses a great reward and the prophetic practice. However, wudu is valid without istinja. For istibra, wudu cannot be started until one is sure seepage has stopped.
Distinguish between validity (sihha) and reward (thawab).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الاستنجاء
هو مأخوذ من نجوت الشجرة وأنجيتها، إذا قطعتها، كأنه يقطع الأذى عنه، وقيل: من النجوة، وهي ما ارتفع من الأرض، لأنه يستتر بها عن الناس والسين فيه يجوز أن تكون للطلب، أي: طلب النجو ليزيله، فالسين فيه كما في استخرج والاستنجاء، والاستطابة، والاستجمار، بمعنى: إزالة الخارج من السبيلين عنهما. لكن الثالث مختص بالحجر، مأخوذ من الجمار، وهي صغار الحصى، والأولان يعمان الحجر والماء. وقال في « الفائق » : الاستنجاء قطع النجاسة. انتهى. وهو ظاهر فيما إذا كان بالماء لا الحجر. فالتفسير الأول أليق، وهو المنقول عن المطرزي وغيره. ( يَلْزَمُ الرَّجُلَ الاستبراء) عبر باللزوم، لكونه أقوى من التعبير بالواجب، فإن هذا أمر يفوت الجواز بفوته، وهو : طلب البراءة مطلقاً، ويراد به في باب الطهارة، طلب براءة المخرج عن أثر البول (حتى يزول أثر البول) أراد بالأثر البلل الذي يظهر على الحجر ، ويَطْمَئِنَّ قَلْبُهُ) أي: الرجل، وإنما قيد بالرجل لأن المرأة لا تحتاج إلى ما يحتاج إليه الرجل، من نحو التنحنح، بل كلما فرغت من البول تصبر قليلاً ثـم تستنجي، ولما كان الذي يحصل به الاستبراء مختلفاً باختلاف عادات الناس، لـم يـقـيـد بشـيء، فيـكـون على حَسَبِ عادتِهِ إِمّا بالمشي، أوِ التَّنَحْنُحِ ، أو الاضْطِجَاعِ على جانبه الأيسر، (أو غَيْرِهِ)؛ من نقــل الأقدام والركض بها، وعصر الذكر برفق، (وَلا يَجُوزُ ) أي : لا يصح (له الشروع في الوضوء، حتى يطمئن بزوالِ رَشحِ البَوْلِ)؛ لأن ظهور الرشح على رأس السبيل مثل تقاطره، فيمنع صحة الوضوء. ثـم شرع في صفة الاستنجاء فقال: ( والاسْتِنْجَاءُ) ليس إلا قسماً واحداً وهو: (سنة) مؤكدة للرجال والنساء، لأنه واظب عليه، ولم يكن واجباً لتركه عليه الصلاة والسلام، ذلك في بعض الأوقات. وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: ( مَنْ اسْتَجْمَرَ فَلْيُوتِرُ، وَمَنْ فَعَلَ هَذَا فَقَدْ أَحْسَنَ، وَمَنْ لَا فَلَا حَرَجَ)
Chapter on Istinja. It is derived from 'najawtu al-shajara' (I cut the tree) and 'anjaytuha', meaning you cut it, as if he cuts off the harm. It is said it is from 'al-najwa' which is elevated land, because he screens himself with it from people. The 'sin' in it may be for seeking, i.e., seeking the elevated place to remove it. So the 'sin' is as in 'istakhraja'. Istinja, istitaba, and istijmar all mean removing the exit from the two passages. But the third is specific to stones, derived from 'al-jimar' which are small pebbles, while the first two are general for stones and water. It is said in al-Fa'iq: Istinja is cutting off the impurity. End. That is apparent when it is with water, not stones. So the first interpretation is more fitting, and it is transmitted from al-Mutarrizi and others. (The man is obligated to perform istibra) He used 'luzum' (necessity) because it is stronger than expressing 'wajib' (obligatory), for this is a matter whose loss forfeits permissibility. It is seeking absolute freedom (from impurity). In the chapter on purification, it means seeking the release of the exit from the trace of urine. (Until the trace of urine disappears) He meant by 'trace' the moisture that appears on the stone. (And his heart is at ease) i.e., the man. He restricted it to men because women do not need what men need, like clearing the throat. Rather, when she finishes urination, she waits a little then performs istinja. Since the means of istibra differ according to people's habits, it is not restricted to something specific; it is according to his habit, either by walking, clearing the throat, lying on his left side, or other means such as shifting feet, running, or gently squeezing the penis. (And it is not permissible for him to begin wudu until he is assured of the disappearance of the seepage of urine) because the appearance of seepage at the tip of the passage is like dripping, preventing the validity of wudu. Then he began describing the manner of istinja, saying: (Istinja) is only one category, and it is a confirmed sunnah for men and women, because he (the Prophet) continuously performed it and it was not obligatory as he left it sometimes. The Prophet said: 'Whoever uses stones (istijmar) should do so an odd number of times; whoever does this has done well, and whoever does not, there is no harm.'
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter (fasl) on istinja (cleansing after relieving oneself). It first gives the linguistic derivation: istinja comes from 'najw' meaning to cut, as if cutting off impurity, or from 'najwa' meaning elevated land, since one uses it for concealment. The 'sin' indicates seeking. Then it distinguishes between istinja (general), istitaba (same), and istijmar (specific to using stones). The preferred definition is 'cutting off impurity'. The text then addresses istibra (ensuring no urine remains): it is 'lazim' (necessary) for men, stronger than 'wajib', because without it the prayer is not valid. Istibra is seeking to be free from urine by ensuring no drops remain. For women, they simply wait a short while after urination. The means of istibra vary by habit: walking, coughing, lying on left side, etc. It is not valid to begin wudu until one is certain the seepage has stopped. Finally, the text states that istinja itself is a sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah), not wajib, because the Prophet sometimes omitted it. The proof is the hadith that whoever uses stones should use an odd number, and there is no harm in not doing it.

Key Terms
الاستنجاء (al-istinja): Cleansing the private parts from impurity after relieving oneself, generally using water or stones
الاستبراء (al-istibra'): Ensuring that no urine remains in the urethra after urination; it is necessary (lazim) for men
الاستجمار (al-istijmar): Cleansing with stones or similar dry materials

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of istinja according to the Hanafi school?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah muakkadah
C) Mubah
D) Fard

Key Takeaway
Istinja is a confirmed sunnah (not wajib) and istibra is necessary (lazim) for men to ensure wudu's validity.

The Necessity of Istibra' for Men
Ruling on necessity of istibra' for men

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on istibra' for men and state the consequences of omitting it before wudu.

Core Idea
Istibra' is necessary for men; without it, any wudu is invalid due to residual urine.

In this passage, the author explains that after urination, a man must perform istibra' — ensuring no moisture remains — before starting wudu. The term 'lazim' is used to emphasize its importance. We will explore the methods and the legal consequence of neglecting it.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the ruling
Identify that istibra' is termed 'lazim' (necessary) for men, which is stronger than 'wajib'.
The author explicitly says 'يلزم الرجل الاستبراء'.
2
Understand the method
List the recommended methods: walking, clearing throat, lying on left side, etc. Note that the method varies by custom.
The text mentions these as examples (إما بالمشي، أو التنحنح، أو الاصطجاع).
3
Distinguish between men and women
Note that women only need to wait a short time after urination before istinja'. They do not need extra actions.
The text says المرأة لا تحتاج إلى ما يحتاج إليه الرجل.
4
Link to wudu validity
Understand that if seepage (رَشح) occurs after wudu begins, the wudu is invalid. Certainty of dryness is required before starting wudu.
The text: 'ولا يجوز له الشروع في الوضوء حتى يطمئن بزوال رشح البول'.
5
Apply to scenario
Consider a man who skips istibra' and begins wudu directly. His wudu is invalid because urine may still be present.
This is the direct consequence.

فصل في الاستنجاء يَلْزَمُ الرَّجُلَ الاستبراء حتى يزُولَ أثرُ البَوْلِ، وَيَطْمَئِنَّ قَلْبُهُ على حَسَبِ عادتِهِ، إما بالمشي، أو التنحْنُحِ، أو الاصْطِجَاعِ، أَوْ غَيْرِهِ، ولا يجوز له الشروع في الوضوء حتى يطمئِن بزوالِ رَشحِ البَوْلِ. والاستنجاء سنة . فصل في الاستنجاء هو مأخوذ من نجوت الشجرة وأنجيتها، إذا قطعتها، كأنه يقطع الأذى عنه، وقيل: من النجوة، وهي ما ارتفع من الأرض، لأنه يستتر بها عن الناس والسين فيه يجوز أن تكون للطلب، أي: طلب النجو ليزيله، فالسين فيه كما في استخرج والاستنجاء، والاستطابة، والاستجمار، بمعنى: إزالة الخارج من السبيلين عنهما. لكن الثالث مختص بالحجر، مأخوذ من الجمار، وهي صغار الحصى، والأولان يعمان الحجر والماء. وقال في « الفائق » : الاستنجاء قطع النجاسة. انتهى. وهو ظاهر فيما إذا كان بالماء لا الحجر. فالتفسير الأول أليق، وهو المنقول عن المطرزي وغيره. ( يَلْزَمُ الرَّجُلَ الاستبراء) عبر باللزوم، لكونه أقوى من التعبير بالواجب، فإن هذا أمر يفوت الجواز بفوته، وهو : طلب البراءة مطلقاً، ويراد به في باب الطهارة، طلب براءة المخرج عن أثر البول (حتى يزول أثر البول) أراد بالأثر البلل الذي يظهر على الحجر ، ويَطْمَئِنَّ قَلْبُهُ) أي: الرجل، وإنما قيد بالرجل لأن المرأة لا تحتاج إلى ما يحتاج إليه الرجل، من نحو التنحنح، بل كلما فرغت من البول تصبر قليلاً ثـم تستنجي، ولما كان الذي يحصل به الاستبراء مختلفاً باختلاف عادات الناس، لـم يـقـيـد بشـيء، فيـكـون على حَسَبِ عادتِهِ إِمّا بالمشي، أوِ التَّنَحْنُحِ ، أو الاضْطِجَاعِ على جانبه الأيسر، (أو غَيْرِهِ)؛ من نقــل الأقدام والركض بها، وعصر الذكر برفق، (وَلا يَجُوزُ ) أي : لا يصح (له الشروع في الوضوء، حتى يطمئن بزوالِ رَشحِ البَوْلِ)؛ لأن ظهور الرشح على رأس السبيل مثل تقاطره، فيمنع صحة الوضوء. ثـم شرع في صفة الاستنجاء فقال: ( والاسْتِنْجَاءُ) ليس إلا قسماً واحداً وهو: (سنة) مؤكدة للرجال والنساء، لأنه واظب عليه، ولم يكن واجباً لتركه عليه الصلاة والسلام، ذلك في بعض الأوقات. وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: ( مَنْ اسْتَجْمَرَ فَلْيُوتِرُ، وَمَنْ فَعَلَ هَذَا فَقَدْ أَحْسَنَ، وَمَنْ لَا فَلَا حَرَجَ ) رواه أبو حاتم في صحيحه وغيره، وما ذكره بعضهم من تقسيمه إلى فرض وغيره، ففيه تسامح، سنذكر على ما يظهر به وجه ذلك، إن شاء الله تعالى،
Chapter on Istinja'. It is necessary for a man to perform istibra' until the trace of urine is removed and his heart is at ease according to his habit, either by walking, clearing the throat, lying on his side, or other means. He may not begin wudu until he is certain that the seepage of urine has ceased. Istinja' is sunnah. Chapter on Istinja': It is derived from 'najawtu al-shajara' meaning I cut the tree, as if he cuts off harm. It is said from 'najwa', a raised piece of land, because he hides behind it from people. The 'sin' may be for seeking, i.e., seeking the 'najw' to remove it, like in 'istakhraja'. Istinja', istitaba, and istijmar all mean removing the excretion from the two passages. The third is specific to stones, from 'jimar' (small pebbles), while the first two include stones and water. In 'al-Fa'iq', istinja' means cutting off impurity. This is apparent when using water, not stones. The first interpretation is more appropriate, transmitted from al-Mutarrizi and others. 'It is necessary for a man to perform istibra'' – he used 'lazim' because it is stronger than 'wajib', as it is something whose loss invalidates permission. It means seeking absolute freedom, and in purification, it means seeking the exit's freedom from urine traces. 'Until the trace of urine is removed' – he meant by 'trace' the moisture that appears on the stone. 'And his heart is at ease' – i.e., the man. He specified the man because women do not need what men need, like clearing the throat. Rather, whenever she finishes urinating, she waits a little then performs istinja'. Since the method of istibra' differs according to people's habits, it is not specified, so it is according to his habit: by walking, clearing the throat, lying on his left side, or other means such as moving his feet, kicking them, or gently squeezing the penis. 'And it is not permissible for him to begin wudu until he is certain of the cessation of urine seepage' – because the appearance of seepage at the head of the passage is like dripping, preventing the validity of wudu. Then he began describing istinja': 'And istinja' is only one type, and it is a confirmed sunnah for men and women, because he (peace be upon him) consistently performed it and it was not obligatory, as he abandoned it on some occasions. He said: 'Whoever uses stones for cleaning, let him do it an odd number of times; whoever does this has done well, and whoever does not, there is no harm.' Narrated by Abu Hatim in his Sahih and others. What some have mentioned about dividing it into obligatory and other categories is lenient; we will mention that which clarifies the matter, if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on istibra' and istinja'. The author first states that istibra' (ensuring the urethra is free of residual urine) is necessary (lazim) for men, using a term stronger than wajib to emphasize its importance. The method varies by custom but must achieve certainty that no moisture remains. Women have a different, simpler process. The author then defines istinja' linguistically and legally, clarifying that it is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), not wajib, because the Prophet occasionally omitted it and the hadith indicates no sin for leaving it. The hadith narrated by Abu Hatim supports this: one who cleanses with stones should do it an odd number of times, but there is no harm in not doing so. Thus, istinja' is recommended but not obligatory.

Key Terms
استبراء (istibra'): Seeking to ensure the urethra is free of any residual urine after urination, by methods such as walking, clearing throat, or lying down.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a man who begins wudu without performing istibra'?
A) His wudu is valid.
B) His wudu is invalid.
C) His wudu is valid but makruh.
D) He must repeat the prayer only.

Key Takeaway
Istibra' is a necessary act (lazim) for men after urination to ensure wudu's validity; skipping it renders wudu invalid.

6 min
Istinja' is a Confirmed Sunnah, Not Wajib
Establishing istinja' as sunnah with linguistic and hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to prove that istinja' is sunnah mu'akkadah in the Hanafi school, using the hadith and the Prophet's practice, and identify the difference from those who consider it wajib.

Core Idea
Istinja' is sunnah mu'akkadah, proven by the Prophet's occasional omission and the hadith 'whoever does not, there is no harm'.

The author now defines istinja' linguistically and states clearly that it is a confirmed sunnah for both men and women. This is supported by a hadith that indicates no sin in leaving it, distinguishing the Hanafi position from those who consider it wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Note that the author explicitly states 'والاستنجاء سنة' (istinja' is sunnah).
The text calls it sunnah mu'akkadah for both genders.
2
Understand the linguistic derivation
The term istinja' means cutting off impurity (from 'najw' or 'najawa'). It is synonymous with istitaba and istijmar but istijmar is specific to stones.
This clarifies that istinja' can be done with water or stones.
3
Analyze the hadith proof
The author cites: 'Whoever uses stones, let him do it odd. Whoever does this has done well; whoever does not, there is no harm.' The phrase 'la haraj' (no harm) indicates neither sin nor obligation.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Hatim and is ahad, meaning zanni thubut and zanni dalala.
4
Refute the wajib claim
Some scholars consider istinja' obligatory, but the author dismisses this as lenience (tasamuh). The Hanafi position relies on the Prophet's occasional omission and the hadith.
The text says: 'وما ذكره بعضهم من تقسيمه إلى فرض وغيره ففيه تسامح'.
5
Apply to practice
A person who does not perform istinja' but uses only dry tissue or nothing is not sinful, but it is recommended to perform it. The wudu remains valid, though the act is incomplete in perfection.
This is the practical consequence: sunnah does not invalidate wudu if omitted.

Chapter on Istinja'. It is necessary for a man to perform istibra' until the trace of urine is removed and his heart is at ease according to his habit, either by walking, clearing the throat, lying on his side, or other means. He may not begin wudu until he is certain that the seepage of urine has ceased. Istinja' is sunnah. Chapter on Istinja': It is derived from 'najawtu al-shajara' meaning I cut the tree, as if he cuts off harm. It is said from 'najwa', a raised piece of land, because he hides behind it from people. The 'sin' may be for seeking, i.e., seeking the 'najw' to remove it, like in 'istakhraja'. Istinja', istitaba, and istijmar all mean removing the excretion from the two passages. The third is specific to stones, from 'jimar' (small pebbles), while the first two include stones and water. In 'al-Fa'iq', istinja' means cutting off impurity. This is apparent when using water, not stones. The first interpretation is more appropriate, transmitted from al-Mutarrizi and others. 'It is necessary for a man to perform istibra'' – he used 'lazim' because it is stronger than 'wajib', as it is something whose loss invalidates permission. It means seeking absolute freedom, and in purification, it means seeking the exit's freedom from urine traces. 'Until the trace of urine is removed' – he meant by 'trace' the moisture that appears on the stone. 'And his heart is at ease' – i.e., the man. He specified the man because women do not need what men need, like clearing the throat. Rather, whenever she finishes urinating, she waits a little then performs istinja'. Since the method of istibra' differs according to people's habits, it is not specified, so it is according to his habit: by walking, clearing the throat, lying on his left side, or other means such as moving his feet, kicking them, or gently squeezing the penis. 'And it is not permissible for him to begin wudu until he is certain of the cessation of urine seepage' – because the appearance of seepage at the head of the passage is like dripping, preventing the validity of wudu. Then he began describing istinja': 'And istinja' is only one type, and it is a confirmed sunnah for men and women, because he (peace be upon him) consistently performed it and it was not obligatory, as he abandoned it on some occasions. He said: 'Whoever uses stones for cleaning, let him do it an odd number of times; whoever does this has done well, and whoever does not, there is no harm.' Narrated by Abu Hatim in his Sahih and others. What some have mentioned about dividing it into obligatory and other categories is lenient; we will mention that which clarifies the matter, if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on istibra' and istinja'. The author first states that istibra' (ensuring the urethra is free of residual urine) is necessary (lazim) for men, using a term stronger than wajib to emphasize its importance. The method varies by custom but must achieve certainty that no moisture remains. Women have a different, simpler process. The author then defines istinja' linguistically and legally, clarifying that it is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), not wajib, because the Prophet occasionally omitted it and the hadith indicates no sin for leaving it. The hadith narrated by Abu Hatim supports this: one who cleanses with stones should do it an odd number of times, but there is no harm in not doing so. Thus, istinja' is recommended but not obligatory.

Key Terms
استنجاء (istinja'): Cleansing the private parts after relieving oneself, using water or stones, to remove impurity.
استجمار (istijmar): Cleaning with stones or similar dry materials, specifically done an odd number of times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What hadith does the author use to prove that istinja' is sunnah and not wajib?
A) 'Cleanliness is half of faith'
B) 'Whoever uses stones, let him do it an odd number...'
C) 'When you relieve yourself, wash thoroughly'
D) 'The key to prayer is purification'

Key Takeaway
Istinja' is a confirmed sunnah, not wajib, as proven by the hadith's 'no harm' phrase and the Prophet's occasional omission.

Thresholds of Impurity Removal in the Hanafi School
Fiqh ruling on impurity removal thresholds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for removing impurity from the private parts by distinguishing between sunnah, wajib, and fard based on quantity and location, and explain the exception for sweat and the ruling during ghusl.

Core Idea
Impurity inside the exit is sunnah to remove; if it exceeds and equals a dirham, wajib; if more than a dirham, fard — water is required for amounts exceeding the exit.

This lesson from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies the graduated obligations for removing impurity (najas) from the private parts. While many assume any impurity must be washed, the Hanafi school establishes clear thresholds using the dirham measure. Understanding these thresholds ensures correct purification before prayer and during ghusl.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the three quantity zones
Identify the categories: impurity that does not exceed the exit (sunnah), equals a dirham (wajib), and exceeds a dirham (fard).
2
Define the dirham measure
Understand that a dirham is 20 qirats (approx 2.8 g) for solids or equivalent area for liquids.
3
Apply the ruling to ghusl
During ghusl for janabah, hayd, or nifas, washing the exit is fard even if the impurity is little, because ghusl requires purity from both hadath and najas.
4
Recognize exceptions
Wind is not najis, and sweat from the private parts does not prevent prayer even if it exceeds a dirham, due to consensus of later scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من نجس يَخْرُجُ من السَّبِيلَيْنِ، مَا لَم يَتَجاوز المخرج، وإن تجاوز، وكان قَدْرَ الدرهم، وجب إزالته بالماء، وإن زادَ على الدرهم افْتَرِضَ غسلهُ ويُفْتَرَضَ عَسَلُ ما في المخرج عند الاغتسال من الجنابة، والحيض، والنفاس، وإن كان ما في المخرج قليلاً. رواه أبو حاتم في صحيحه وغيره، وما ذكره بعضهم من تقسيمه إلى فرض وغيره، ففيه تسامح، سنذكر على ما يظهر به وجه ذلك، إن شاء الله تعالى. وقوله : ( منْ نَجَس) احترز به عن الريح، فإنه ليس بنجس الصحيح، ولا يكون على السبيل، والاستنجاء منه بدعة، وقوله: (يَخْرُجُ من السَّبِيلَيْنِ) جري على الغالب، إذ لو أصاب المخرج نجاسة من غيره، يطهر بالاستنجاء بالحجر ونحوه كالخارج، ولا فــرق بـيـن كون الخارج معتاداً، أو غير معتاد في الصحيح، حتى لو خرج من السبيلين دم، أو قيــح يطهر بالحجارة في حق العرق، وجواز الصلاة معه لإجماع المتأخرين على أنه لو سـال الـعـرقُ منه وأصاب الثوب والبدن أكثر من قدر الدرهم ، لا يمنع جواز الصلاة معه، وأما إذ جلس في ماء قليل، فإنه ينجس. وقوله: ما لم يتجاوز المَخْرَجَ)، قيد لتسميته استنجاء؛ ولكونه مسنوناً، وإِنْ تَجَاوَزَ) المخرج، (وَكَانَ) المتجاوز (قَدْرَ الدّرهم) لا ـ إزالة المتجاوز استنجاء، فلهذا (وَجَبَ إِزَالَتُهُ بِالمَاءِ) أو المائع، ولا يطهر بالحجر، لأنه من باب إزالة النجاسة الحقيقية عن البدن، (وَإِنْ زَادَ) المتجاوز (عَلَى) قـدر (الدرهم) المثقالي، وهو: عشرون قيراطاً في المتجسد، أو زاد على قدره مساحة في المائع (افْتُرِضَ غسله بالماء أو المائع، ويُفْتَرَضَ غَسْلُ مَا فِي المَخْرَجَ عِنْدَ الاغْتِسَالِ مِنَ الجَنابِة، والحَيْض، والنِّفاسِ) بالماء المطلق، وإنْ كَانَ مَا فِي المَخْرَجِ قَلِيلاً)؛ ليسقط فرضية غسله للحدث.
From impurity that exits from the two passages: as long as it does not exceed the exit; if it does exceed and is the size of a dirham, its removal with water is obligatory; if it exceeds a dirham, washing it becomes obligatory (fard). And it is obligatory to wash what is in the exit during ghusl for janabah, hayd, and nifas, even if what is in the exit is little. Abu Hatim narrated it in his Sahih and others; what some have mentioned about dividing it into fard and other categories is lenient; we will mention that which clarifies the matter, if Allah wills. His saying: 'from impurity' excludes wind, for it is not impure according to the correct view, and it is not on the passage, and istinja' from it is an innovation. His saying: 'that exits from the two passages' follows the common case, for if impurity from elsewhere hits the exit, it is purified by istinja' with stones and the like, like the exiting impurity. There is no difference, in the correct view, between the exiting substance being normal or abnormal, even if blood or pus exits from the two passages, it is purified by stones regarding the excuse and the permissibility of prayer with it, due to the consensus of later scholars that if sweat flows from it and touches the garment and body more than the size of a dirham, it does not prevent the permissibility of prayer. But if he sits in a small amount of water, it becomes impure. His saying: 'as long as it does not exceed the exit' is a condition for it to be called istinja' and for it to be sunnah. If it exceeds the exit and is the size of a dirham, the removal of the exceeded part is not istinja'; therefore its removal with water or liquid is obligatory, and it is not purified by stone, because it is a case of removing actual impurity from the body. If the exceeded part is more than a dirham (the weight of a dirham, which is twenty qirats in solid form, or exceeding its area in liquid form), its washing with water or liquid becomes fard. And it is fard to wash what is in the exit during ghusl for janabah, hayd, and nifas with pure water, even if what is in the exit is little, in order to lift the fardiyyah of washing for hadath.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the obligation to remove impurity (najas) from the private parts. It clarifies three scenarios: (1) If the impurity does not exceed the exit (makhraj), istinja' with stones or water is sunnah. (2) If it exceeds and is equal to a dirham in weight or area, removal with water is obligatory (wajib); stones are insufficient because it is actual impurity on the body. (3) If it exceeds more than a dirham, washing becomes fard (obligatory). The dirham is defined as 20 qirats (approximately 2.812 grams) for solid, or equivalent area for liquids. The passage also discusses the ruling during ghusl: it is fard to wash the exit (even if the impurity is little) when performing ghusl for janabah, hayd, or nifas, because the ghusl requires purity from both hadath and najas. Additionally, wind is not considered impure, and istinja' from it is an innovation (bid'ah). The author cites the consensus of later scholars that sweat from the private parts does not invalidate prayer even if it exceeds a dirham, but if one sits in a small amount of water, it becomes impure.

Key Terms
درهم (dirham): A silver coin used as a unit of weight; here defined as 20 qirats = approximately 2.812 grams, or equivalent area for liquid impurities.
نجس (najas): Impurity; specifically here, what exits from the two passages (urine, feces, blood, pus, etc.), excluding wind.
مخرج (makhraj): The exit; the external opening of the private parts (anus or urethra).
قيراط (qirat): A unit of weight; 20 qirats = 1 dirham (approx. 2.812 g).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Only when the impurity is more than a dirham and exceeds the exit
C) When the impurity is any amount that exits
D) When the impurity is from a dog or pig

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies removal of impurity from the private parts into three categories based on quantity and location: sunnah (inside exit), wajib (equals dirham and exceeds), fard (exceeds dirham).

Method of Istinja': Combining Water and Stone, and the Ruling on the Number of Stones
Ruling on istinja' methods and number of stones

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred methods of istinja' in the Hanafi school and explain why using three stones is mandub rather than sunnah mu'akkadah.

Core Idea
The best istinja' combines water and stone; using three stones is recommended, not obligatory.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the Hanafi rulings on the method of istinja'. It clarifies the gradation of preference: water alone is more beloved than stone alone, but combining both is the best and is considered a sunnah mu'akkadah. The passage also addresses the common misconception that the number three stones is a confirmed sunnah, showing instead that it is only recommended (mandub) because the goal is cleanliness. We will walk through the proofs and the tarjih that establishes the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three methods and their rulings
From the passage, list the three main methods of istinja': (1) combining water and stone, (2) water alone, (3) stone alone. Note the relative virtue and the legal ruling (sunnah mu'akkadah, more beloved, permissible) for each.
The passage grades them: combining is 'afdal', water alone is 'ahabb' (next in virtue), stone alone is permissible but lower.
2
Examine the proof for combining water and stone
The passage cites the verse 'In it are men who love to purify themselves' (9:108) and the hadith of the people of Quba' who used both stone and water. Understand how this story demonstrates the virtue of combining, and note that the text declares this combination a 'sunnah on an absolute basis' (sunnah mu'akkadah).
The phrase 'wa huwa al-sahih wa 'alayhi al-fatwa' indicates this is the relied-upon position.
3
Analyze the ruling on the number of stones
The passage states that the number three is mandub, not sunnah mu'akkadah. Extract the proof from the hadith 'man istajmara falyutir' and its additional wording 'man fa'ala faqad ahsana, wa man la fala haraj' (whoever does so has done well, and whoever does not, there is no sin). Interpret this as indicating permissibility, not obligation.
The footnote (6) clarifies that the hadith is 'muhkam fi al-takhyir' (clearly permissive).
4
Identify the conditions for the stone
The stone must be 'munq' (clean), meaning not rough like brick and not smooth, and must be a pure substance that removes impurity without harming, and it must not be valuable or respected (e.g., food or paper with writing). List these conditions from the first part of the passage.
The condition 'ghayr mutaqawwim wa la muhtaram' (not valuable or respected) prevents using objects like food or paper with Quranic verses.
5
Understand the overall sunnah and goal
The passage emphasizes that the true sunnah is 'inqa' al-mahall' (cleaning the place), not the specific means or number. Recognize that both stone and water achieve this, but combining is best because it ensures the highest level of purity.
This explains why the number three is not emphasized: even if cleaning is achieved with fewer stones, the sunnah (cleaning) is still fulfilled.

Commentary
This passage continues the expansion of Nur al-Idah, focusing on the method and rulings of istinja' (cleaning after relieving oneself). It begins by recommending that one use a 'clean stone' (munq) – one that is not rough or smooth – to effectively remove impurity. The author then grades the methods: washing with water is more beloved (ahabb) than stone alone because water achieves unanimous purification. The best (afdal) method is to combine water and stone, wiping first with a stone then washing with water, citing the famous hadith of the people of Quba'. Combining is considered a sunnah in every era, and this is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi). However, it is permissible to use only water or only stone; using water is more virtuous than stone. The true sunnah is to achieve cleanliness (inqa'), not the specific number of stones. Therefore, using three stones is commendable (mandub), not a confirmed sunnah, because the hadith 'perform istijmar in odd numbers' is interpreted as permissive, as clarified by the additional phrase 'whoever does so has done well, and whoever does not, there is no sin.' The passage also mentions the method: wipe from the side (front to back, as per other sources). The footnotes provide references and definitions, including that 'munq' means clean.

Key Terms
منق (munq): Clean, from tanqiya or inqa', meaning free from impurity
استنجاء (istinjā'): Cleaning the exit after relieving oneself, typically with stone, water, or both
مندوب (mandūb): Recommended; an action that brings reward but no sin for leaving
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed sunnah; regularly performed by the Prophet and emphasized

The best istinja' combines water and stone (sunnah mu'akkadah); using three stones is only recommended (mandub) because the goal is cleanliness, not a specific number.

Ruling on Istinja: Methods and Proofs
Ruling on istinja methods with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istinja methods, explain the preference hierarchy, and cite the Quranic and hadith proofs.

Core Idea
The best istinja is to combine stones and water; the sunnah is achieved by cleansing, not by a specific method.

Istinja (cleansing after relieving oneself) is a sunnah act in the Hanafi school. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the recommended methods and their virtues, along with the evidence from the Quran and the practice of the people of Quba. Understanding these rulings helps you practice taharah in a complete and meritorious way.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Istinja is a sunnah, not obligatory. The passage states 'والسنة إنقاء المحل' meaning the sunnah is to cleanse the place. The act itself is recommended.
Some other schools consider washing obligatory; Hanafi holds it as sunnah.
2
Understand the preferred methods
The passage outlines three methods in order of virtue: (1) combining stone and water (best), (2) using water only (next best), (3) using stone only (least but still valid). The combination is 'الأفضل' (the best).
Water alone is 'أحب' (more beloved) than stone alone.
3
Note the conditions for using stones
The stone must be 'munq' – neither rough nor smooth – and generally any pure substance that removes impurity without causing harm, except valuable or respected items. The goal is 'inqa'' (thorough cleansing).
Baked clay is given as an example of a suitable stone.
4
Examine the Quranic proof
The verse from Surah al-Tawbah (9:108) praises those who love to purify themselves. The hadith explains that the people of Quba used stones then water. This establishes the combination as a continuous sunnah.
The dalil is a Quranic verse (qati al-thubut) with zanni al-dalala regarding the specific method.
5
Understand the permissibility of limitation
It is permissible (يجوز) to use only water or only stone. The sunnah is fulfilled by achieving inqa'. The virtue varies, but all methods are valid.
The passage explicitly says 'ويجوز أن يقتصر على الماء أو الحجر'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأن يستنجي بحجر منق ونحوه، والغسل بالماء أحب، والأفضل الجمع بين الماء والحجر، فيمسح ثم يغسل. ويجوز أن يقتصر على الماء أو الحجر والسنة إنقاء المحل. (و) يسن (أن يستنجي بحجر منق) وهو الذي لا يكون خشناً، كالآجر ولا أملس، لأن الإنقاء هو المقصود بالاستنجاء ولا يكون بدونه، (ونحوه) أي: الحجر من كل طاهر مزيل بلا ضر غير متقوم ولا محترم. (والغسل بالماء) المطلق (أحب) لحصول الطهارة المتفق عليها، وإقامة السنة على الوجه الأكمل، لأن الحجر مقلل، والمائع غير الماء مختلف في تطهيره. (والأفضل) في كل زمان (الجمع بين) استعمال (الماء والحجر) مرتباً، (فيمسح) الخارج، ثم يغسل المخرج لقوله تعالى: {أَن تَقُومَ فِيهِ رِجَالٌ يُحِبُّونَ أَن يَنطَهَرُوا} [التوبة: 108]. قيل: لما نزلت هذه الآية، قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: (يا أهل قباء، إن الله أثنى عليكم فماذا تصنعون عند الغائط؟ قالوا: نتبع الغائط الأحجار، ثم نتبع الأحجار الماء). فكان الجمع سنة على الإطلاق في كل زمان، وهو الصحيح وعليه الفتوى، وقيل: ذلك في زماننا لأنهم كانوا يبعرون. (ويجوز) أي: يصح (أن يقتصر على الماء) فقط، وهو يلي الجمع بين الماء والحجر في الفضل (أو) على (الحجر) وهو دون ما قبله في الفضل، وتحصل السنة، وإن تفاوت الفضل، (والسنة إنقاء المحل) لأنه المقصود.
And that he performs istinja with a pure stone and the like. Washing with water is more beloved. The best is to combine water and stone: he wipes then washes. It is permissible to limit oneself to water or stone, and the sunnah is cleansing the place. And it is sunnah to perform istinja with a pure stone—meaning one that is not rough, like baked clay, nor smooth—because cleansing is the purpose of istinja and cannot be achieved without it. 'And the like' means every pure substance that removes without harm, not a valuable object nor one that is respected. Washing with pure water is more beloved because it achieves agreed-upon purity and establishes the sunnah in the most complete manner, since the stone is a reducer, and liquids other than water are disagreed upon regarding purification. And the best in every time is the combination of using water and stone in order: he wipes the excrement, then washes the exit. This is based on His statement: 'In it are men who love to purify themselves' [Surah al-Tawbah: 108]. It is said that when this verse was revealed, the Messenger of Allah said: 'O people of Quba', Allah has praised you. What do you do when you relieve yourselves?' They said: 'We follow the excrement with stones, then follow the stones with water.' Thus the combination is a sunnah absolutely in every time—this is the correct view and the fatwa is upon it. It is also said that this applies in our time because they used to [only] use dry droppings. And it is permissible to limit oneself to water only—this follows the combination in virtue—or to stone only, which is inferior to the previous. The sunnah is attained, although the virtue varies. And the sunnah is to cleanse the place, because that is the purpose.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah comments on the matn of Nur al-Idah regarding istinja (cleansing after relieving oneself). The commentator first explains that the recommended method is to use a pure stone—neither rough nor smooth—because the goal is to remove the impurity. Any clean substance that removes without harm is permissible, except valuable or respected items. Washing with pure water is more beloved because it is universally agreed to purify, whereas the stone only reduces impurity. The best practice is to combine both: first wipe with stones, then wash with water. The proof is the verse of Surah al-Tawbah and the hadith of the people of Quba', which establishes this combination as a continuous sunnah. It is also permissible to use only water or only stone, but water is superior to stone in virtue. The sunnah is fulfilled by cleansing the area, regardless of the method used.

Key Terms
مَنْق (munq): A pure stone that is neither rough nor smooth, suitable for cleaning.
اسْتِنْجَاء (istinja): The act of cleaning the private parts after relieving oneself.
إِنْقَاء (inqa'): Complete cleansing and removal of impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the most virtuous method of istinja?
A) Using only water
B) Using only stones
C) Combining water and stones
D) Using any liquid

Key Takeaway
The sunnah of istinja is fulfilled by cleansing the place (inqa'), and the most virtuous method is to combine a dry substance (like a pure stone) and water, in that order.
